وجوب الإفتاء بظاهر الرواية
وقولي: "أو كان ظاهر الرواية إلخ " معناه أن ما كان من المسائل في الكتب التي رويت عن محمد بن الحسن رواية ظاهرة، يفتى به وإن لم يصرحوا بتصحيحه، نعم ! لو صححوا رواية أخرى من غير كتب ظاهر الرواية يتبع ما صححوه.
قال العلامة الطرسوسي في "أنفع الوسائل" في مسألة الكفالة إلى شهر: "إن القاضي المقلد لا يجوز له أن يحكم إلا بما هو ظاهر الرواية، لا بالرواية الشاذة، إلا أن ينصوا على أن الفتوى عليها".
وكتب ظاهر الروايات أتت ستا وبالأصول أيضا سمّيت
الشيباني حرّر فيها المذهب النعماني الكبير
الصغير والكبير والسير صنفها محمد الجامع
ثم الزيادات مع كذا والصغير المبسوط تواترت بالسند المضبوط
له مسائل النوادر إسنادها في الكتب غير ظاهر
وبعدها مسائل النوازل خرجها الأشياخ بالدلائل
The obligation to issue fatwa based on Zahir al-Riwayah.
My statement: 'or it was Zahir al-Riwayah, etc.' means that whatever matters are in the books that were narrated from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan through clear/well-known transmission, fatwa is given according to them, even if the scholars did not explicitly state their correctness. However, if they corrected another narration from outside the books of Zahir al-Riwayah, then what they corrected is followed.
Al-Tarsusi said in 'Anfa' al-Wasa'il' regarding the issue of surety until a month: 'A muqallid judge is not permitted to judge except by what is Zahir al-Riwayah, not by a weak/shaz narration, unless they explicitly state that the fatwa is upon it.'
The books of Zahir al-Riwayah are six, and they are also called by the fundamentals.
Al-Shaybani recorded in them the great Nu'mani madhhab.
Al-Saghir, al-Kabir, and al-Siyar were authored by Muhammad; al-Jami'.
Then al-Ziyadat, along with such-and-such, and al-Saghir, and al-Mabsut have been transmitted through an authenticated chain.
He has the Nawadir issues whose chains are in non-Zahir books.
After them are the Nawazil issues that the elders extracted with evidence.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage establishes a core rasm rule: a mufti (or judge) must issue fatwa based on Zahir al-Riwayah—the well-known books transmitted from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. The author explains that if a ruling is found in these books, it is followed even if not explicitly declared correct. However, if later scholars correct a different narration from outside these books, the corrected version takes precedence. The quote from al-Tarsusi reinforces this: a muqallid judge cannot rule by a shaz (weak, rare) narration unless specifically instructed. The poem then enumerates the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah: al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat, and al-Mabsut. These are the foundations of the Hanafi fatwa. In contrast, al-Nawadir (rare transmissions) are not in these books, and al-Nawazil (new issues) are derived by later scholars using evidence.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The well-known and widely transmitted books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani that form the authoritative basis of the Hanafi school.
الرواية الشاذة (al-riwayah al-shadhdhah): A rare or weak narration that is not part of Zahir al-Riwayah and is generally not followed unless specifically adopted by later scholars.
مسائل النوادر (masa'il al-nawadir): Rare or exceptional issues narrated from the founders but not in the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah.
مسائل النوازل (masa'il al-nawazil): Newly arising issues that later scholars derived using evidence from the principles of the school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Tarsusi, what is a muqallid judge permitted to base his judgment on?
A) Any reliable book he chooses.
B) Only what is in Zahir al-Riwayah.
C) The most common practice in his city.
D) The opinion of the most learned scholar of his time.

Key Takeaway
Fatwa and judicial rulings in the Hanafi school must be based on the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah to ensure reliability; rare narrations are not authoritative unless later scholars have explicitly adopted them.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

The Three Categories of Hanafi Rulings
Classifying Hanafi transmitted rulings into three hierarchical categories.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and distinguish the three hierarchical categories of Hanafi rulings (usul, nawadir, fatawa) and apply the correct hierarchy when issuing a fatwa.

Core Idea
Hanafi fatwa authority depends on a three-tier hierarchy: usul (core), nawadir (rare), fatawa (later ijtihad).

This lesson introduces the foundational hierarchy of rulings in the Hanafi school. Understanding these categories is essential for a mufti to know which ruling carries more weight. The passage from Ibn Abi al-Izz's commentary on 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti explains three layers and how later compilations mixed them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
Read the passage and list the three categories of masail mentioned: usul, nawadir, and fatawa/waqi'at. Note the Arabic terms and their definitions.
Usul are the foundational transmitted rulings; nawadir are rare individual narrations; fatawa are later derived rulings.
2
Understand the sources for each
For each category, identify the types of sources or scholars mentioned. Usul come from early mujtahids and the six authoritative works; nawadir from specific narrators like Ibn Sama'a; fatawa from later jurists like Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi.
3
Note the historical development
Trace how later compilations (e.g., Fatawa Qadi Khan) mixed categories, while some (al-Muhit by al-Sarakhsi) kept them separate. Understand why this distinction matters for the mufti.
4
Recognize the authority weight
Classify the authority level: usul (highest), nawadir (medium), fatawa (lowest). Understand that in the absence of a ruling in usul, the mufti moves to nawadir, then to fatawa.
This hierarchy is unique to Hanafi usul al-iftaa.
5
Apply the hierarchy
Given a hypothetical fatwa question, determine which source category to consult first, second, and third. Explain your reasoning.

لرضي الدين السرخسي، فإنه ذكر أولا مسائل الأصول، ثم النوادر، ثم الفتاوى، ونعم ما فعل.
Layers of Masail. The predecessors among jurists, hadith scholars, and Arabic linguists and others used to author books in their sciences, but they became extinct with the loss of knowledge and scholars - and to Allah is the destination. The Shafi'i scholars call something similar 'Ta'liqa'. And sometimes [transmission is] through individual narrations like the narration of Ibn Sama'a, and Mu'alla ibn Mansur and others concerning particular issues. The third category: al-Fatawa and al-Waqi'at, which are issues derived by later mujtahids when they were asked about them and did not find a narration from the early scholars of the madhhab. They are the companions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad and the companions of their companions, and so on. They are many; the place to know them is the books of Tabaqat of our scholars and books of history. From the companions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, [such as] Hamlah? like 'Isam ibn Yusuf, Ibn Rustam, Muhammad ibn Sama'a, Abu Sulayman al-Juzjani, Abu Hafs al-Bukhari, and after them like Muhammad ibn Salama, Muhammad ibn Muqatil, Nasir ibn Yahya, and Abu al-Nasr al-Qasim ibn Sallam. It may happen that they oppose the scholars of the madhhab due to proofs and reasons that appeared to them. The first book compiled on their fatwas, as far as we know, is the book 'al-Nawazil' by the jurist Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi. Then later scholars compiled other books, like 'Majmu' al-Nawazil wa al-Waqi'at' by al-Natafi, and 'al-Waqi'at' by al-Sadr al-Shahid. Then later scholars mentioned these issues mixed together without distinction, as in 'Fatawa Qadi Khan' and 'al-Khulasa' and others. Some distinguished them, as in 'Kitab al-Muhit' by Radi al-Din al-Sarakhsi, for he first mentioned the issues of Usul, then Nawadir, then Fatawa - and excellent is what he did.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage is a classification of the layers of legal rulings in the Hanafi madhhab. The author, Ibn Abi al-Izz, explains that the early scholars from various disciplines used to write books, but these works disappeared. The Shafi'is call a similar compilation 'Ta'liqa'. He then describes three categories of transmitted rulings: first, the usul (foundational texts) from the early mujtahids; second, the nawadir (rare or individual transmissions) like the narrations of Ibn Sama'a and Mu'alla ibn Mansur on specific issues; and third, the fatawa and waqi'at (later fatwas and case rulings) derived by later jurists when they did not find an existing transmission. These later jurists include the direct students of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, such as 'Isam ibn Yusuf, Ibn Rustam, Muhammad ibn Sama'a, Abu Sulayman al-Juzjani, and Abu Hafs al-Bukhari, as well as later figures like Muhammad ibn Salama, Muhammad ibn Muqatil, Nasir ibn Yahya, and Abu al-Nasr al-Qasim ibn Sallam. The author notes that these later jurists might occasionally depart from the established madhhab positions based on evidence and reasoning. The first compilation of such fatwas was 'al-Nawazil' by Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi, followed by works like al-Natafi's collection and 'al-Waqi'at' by al-Sadr al-Shahid. Later compilations, such as 'Fatawa Qadi Khan' and 'al-Khulasa', mixed all categories without distinction, but Radi al-Din al-Sarakhsi in 'al-Muhit' commendably separated them into usul, nawadir, and fatawa.

Key Terms
طبقات المسائل (tabaqat al-masail): The hierarchical classification of legal rulings in the Hanafi madhhab: usul (core transmitted rulings), nawadir (rare or individual transmissions), and fatawa/waqi'at (later fatwas derived by post-classical jurists).
النوادر (al-nawadir): Rare or individual narrations from the early mujtahids (like Abu Hanifa) that are not part of the widely transmitted usul, often transmitted through a single chain like Ibn Sama'a or Mu'alla ibn Mansur.
الفتاوى والواقعات (al-fatawa wa al-waqi'at): Later rulings and case decisions derived by post-classical Hanafi jurists (like Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi) when they found no explicit transmission from the early madhhab, based on their own ijtihad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which work is praised for distinguishing between usul, nawadir, and fatawa?
A) Fatawa Qadi Khan
B) al-Khulasa
C) Kitab al-Muhit by Radi al-Din al-Sarakhsi
D) al-Nawazil by Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufti must apply a strict hierarchy: first usul (core texts), then nawadir (rare transmissions), and finally fatawa (later ijtihad).

Zahir al-Riwayah vs Riwayat al-Usul: A Distinction for the Mufti
Clarifying the difference between Zahir al-Riwayah and Riwayat al-Usul through a Hajj case study

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between Zahir al-Riwayah and Riwayat al-Usul, and apply this distinction to evaluate the authority of a Hanafi transmission in fatwa practice.

Core Idea
Zahir al-Riwayah is broader than Riwayat al-Usul; a Nawadir narration can be considered Zahir al-Riwayah if reliable.

This passage addresses a critical nuance in Hanafi usul al-ifta: the difference between 'Zahir al-Riwayah' (the apparent/relied-upon transmission) and 'Riwayat al-Usul' (the six core books of Imam Muhammad). Many later commentators treat them as identical, but Ibn Kamal Pasha, citing al-Sarakhsi's usage in a Hajj case, shows that Zahir al-Riwayah can include certain Nawadir narrations when they are well-known and conflict-free. Understanding this distinction is essential for a mufti to correctly weigh transmissions in fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Fiqh Trigger
The distinction is prompted by a specific fiqh issue: whether a woman who can afford her own Hajj expenses but not her mahram's is obligated. Al-Sarakhsi states that Zahir al-Riwayah requires the mahram's expenses; al-Muhit and al-Dhakhira report a narration from al-Hasan ibn Ziyad that only her own expenses suffice.
This conflict in narrations from Imam Muhammad (al-Shaybani) leads al-Sarakhsi to adopt al-Hasan's narration as Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Define the Technical Terms
Riwayat al-Usul are the six books of Imam Muhammad: al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat, al-Siyar al-Kabir, and al-Siyar al-Saghir. Zahir al-Riwayah is a broader category that includes the most apparent and reliable transmissions, which may come from other sources, such as the Nawadir of al-Hasan ibn Ziyad.
Ibn Kamal Pasha emphasizes that Zahir al-Riwayah is not coextensive with Riwayat al-Usul.
3
Analyze al-Sarakhsi's Usage
In al-Mabsut, al-Sarakhsi calls al-Hasan's narrative 'Zahir al-Riwayah'. Since al-Hasan's narration is not in the Usul books, this proves that 'Zahir al-Riwayah' can refer to a Nawadir transmission when it is well-known and deemed reliable.
The author of this passage (the sharih of Rasm al-Mufti) supports Ibn Kamal Pasha's view.
4
Recognize the Opposing View
Some later Hanafi commentators claim that Zahir al-Riwayah is exactly Riwayat al-Usul and that Nawadir can never be Zahir al-Riwayah. Their error stems from conflating the two terms.
This view is criticized as neglectful of al-Sarakhsi's practice.
5
Apply the Distinction to Fatwa Hierarchy
For a mufti, the operative rule (mufta bihi) is determined by the strongest transmission. If a Nawadir narration like al-Hasan's is considered Zahir al-Riwayah, it can outweigh conflicting Usul narrations when the Usul are contradictory. In the Hajj case, the mufti would follow al-Hasan's narration (no need for mahram's expenses).
This distinction directly impacts the mufti's tarjih (preference) process.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هذا وقد فرق العلامة ابن كمال باشا بين رواية الأصول وظاهر الرواية، حيث قال في شرحه على "الهداية" في مسألة المرأة: ما حج حاصله "إنه ذكر في مبسوط السرخسي : أن ظاهر الرواية أنه يشترط أن تملك قدر نفقة محرمها. وإنه ذكر في "المحيط" و"الذخيرة": أنه روى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة أنها إذا قدرت على نفقة نفسها ونفقة محرمها، لزمها الحج. واضطربت الروايات عن محمد ثم قال: ومن هنا ظهر أن مراد الإمام السرخسي من ظاهر الرواية رواية الحسن عن أبي حنيفة، واتضح الفرق بين ظاهر الرواية ورواية الأصول؛ إذ المراد من الأصول: "المبسوط"، و"الجامع الصغير"، و"الجامع الكبير"، و"الزيادات"، والسير الكبير ، وليس فيها رواية الحسن بل كلها رواية محمد. وعلم أن رواية النوادر قد تكون ظاهر الرواية، والمراد من رواية النوادر رواية غير الأصول المذكورة. فاحفظ هذا فإن شراح هذا الكتاب قد غفلوا عنه، وقد صرح بعضهم بعدم الفرق بين ظاهر الرواية ورواية الأصول، وزعم أن رواية النوادر لا تكون ظاهر الرواية". أقول: لا يخفى عليك أن قول "المحيط" و"الذخيرة": "إن هذه رواية الحسن عن أبي حنيفة ، لا يلزم منه أن تكون مخالفة لرواية الأصول، فقد يكون رواها الحسن في كتب النوادر ، أو رواها محمد في كتب الأصول، وإنما ذكر رواية الحسن؛ لعدم الاضطراب عنه، بدليل قوله: واضطربت الروايات عن محمد"، وحينئذ فقول السرخسي: "إنها ظاهر الرواية"
And indeed, Allama Ibn Kamal Pasha distinguished between Riwayat al-Usul and Zahir al-Riwayah. He said in his commentary on al-Hidayah concerning the issue of a woman performing Hajj: The summary of what he said is: 'It is mentioned in Mabsut al-Sarakhsi that the apparent transmission (Zahir al-Riwayah) requires that she possess enough for the expenses of her mahram. And it is mentioned in al-Muhit and al-Dhakhira that al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa that if she can afford expenses for herself and her mahram, then Hajj is obligatory on her. The narrations from Muhammad are conflicting. Then he said: From here it becomes clear that the intention of Imam al-Sarakhsi in using Zahir al-Riwayah is the narration of al-Hasan from Abu Hanifa, and the difference between Zahir al-Riwayah and Riwayat al-Usul is evident. For the meaning of al-Usul is: al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat, and al-Siyar al-Kabir. In these, there is no narration of al-Hasan; rather all are narrations of Muhammad. And it is known that the narration of Nawadir may be considered Zahir al-Riwayah, and the meaning of Riwayat al-Nawadir is the narration other than the aforementioned Usul. So remember this, for the commentators of this book have neglected it, and some of them have stated that there is no difference between Zahir al-Riwayah and Riwayat al-Usul, and they assume that the narration of Nawadir is not considered Zahir al-Riwayah.' I say: It is not hidden from you that the statement of al-Muhit and al-Dhakhira: 'This is a narration of al-Hasan from Abu Hanifa' does not necessarily imply that it contradicts the Riwayat al-Usul. It may be that al-Hasan narrated it in the books of Nawadir, or Muhammad narrated it in the books of Usul. The narration of al-Hasan is mentioned only because there is no conflict in his narration, as evidenced by his statement: 'the narrations from Muhammad are conflicting.' In that case, the statement of al-Sarakhsi that 'it is Zahir al-Riwayah' is justified.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage is a methodological analysis of two technical terms in Hanafi usul al-iftā': 'Zāhir al-Riwāyah' and 'Riwāyat al-Uṣūl'. The author presents the view of Ibn Kamāl Pāshā from his commentary on al-Hidāyah concerning a specific fiqh issue: whether a woman who can afford her own Hajj expenses but not those of her mahram (male guardian) is obligated to perform Hajj. The Mabsūt of al-Sarakhsī states that according to Zāhir al-Riwāyah, she must possess sufficient funds for her mahram's expenses. However, al-Muḥīṭ and al-Dhakhīra report a narration from al-Ḥasan ibn Ziyād from Abū Ḥanīfa that if she can afford both her own and her mahram's expenses, Hajj becomes obligatory. The narrations from Imam Muhammad are conflicting. Ibn Kamāl Pāshā concludes that when al-Sarakhsī says 'Zāhir al-Riwāyah', he is referring to al-Ḥasan's narration, not the six core books (Uṣūl) which contain only Muhammad's narrations. This establishes that Zāhir al-Riwāyah can include certain Nawādir transmissions. The author then critiques this, arguing that the narration of al-Ḥasan does not necessarily contradict the Uṣūl, as it might also be found in Muhammad's books. The key point is that the term Zāhir al-Riwāyah is broader than Riwāyat al-Uṣūl, and in some contexts, a Nawādir narration that is well-known and relied upon is considered Zāhir al-Riwāyah. This distinction is crucial for understanding the weight of different transmissions in Hanafi fatwa.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The most apparent and relied-upon transmissions in the Hanafi school, which may include narrations from both Imam Muhammad and other transmitters like al-Hasan ibn Ziyad, as long as they are well-known and free from conflict.
رواية الأصول (Riwayat al-Usul): The transmissions in the six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani: al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat, al-Siyar al-Kabir, and al-Siyar al-Saghir.
رواية النوادر (Riwayat al-Nawadir): Transmissions outside the six books, including narrations from other students of Abu Hanifa like al-Hasan ibn Ziyad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Zahir al-Riwayah is not confined to the six Usul books; a reliable Nawadir narration can be considered Zahir al-Riwayah, which directly impacts the mufti's tarjih in fatwa.

Defining Kutub al-Usul and the Term al-Asl
Defining the canonical books and the meaning of 'al-Asl'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the canonical Hanafi texts classified as Kutub al-Usul and distinguish the specific reference of the term 'al-Asl'.

Core Idea
The term 'al-Usul' collectively refers to the six core books of Zahir al-Riwayah; 'al-Asl' specifically means al-Mabsut.

In every madhhab, the mufti must know which books are authoritative. The Hanafi tradition has a precise hierarchy. This passage defines two crucial terms: al-Usul (the collective sources) and al-Asl (the singular foundational text). Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly navigating Hanafi fatwa references.

Guided Path
1
Identify the collective term
Recognize that 'al-Usul' refers to the books of Zahir al-Riwayah, the six core texts authored by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.
The passage explicitly states: 'the books of Zahir al-Riwayah are called al-Usul.'
2
Understand the example from al-Hidayah
The Hidayah mentions 'riwayat al-usul' and 'ghair riwayat al-usul'. The commentators clarify which books belong to each category.
Riwayat al-usul includes al-Jami'ain, al-Ziyadat, al-Mabsut.
3
Recognize the singular 'al-Asl'
When the text says 'dhakarahū fī al-asl', it refers specifically to al-Mabsut, not any other book of al-Usul.
The passage cites the commentators' standard interpretation.
4
Note the chronological order and reliance
Al-Mabsut was authored first, then al-Jami' al-Saghir, then al-Kabir, then al-Ziyadat. However, al-Jami' al-Saghir is the relied-upon source because it represents Imam Muhammad's later refined compilation.
This hierarchy is crucial: when a ruling appears in both, al-Jami' al-Saghir takes precedence.
5
Apply the rule
When reading Hanafi texts, a mufti must check the context: 'al-Asl' always means al-Mabsut, and the preferred source for fatwa is al-Jami' al-Saghir when consistent.
This prevents misattributing rulings to weaker narrations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قدمنا أن كتب ظاهر الرواية تسمى بالأصول، ومنه قول "الهداية" في باب التيمم "وعن أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف في غير رواية الأصول". قال الشراح: هناك رواية الأصول: رواية الجامعين، والزيادات، والمبسوط. ورواية غير الأصول: رواية النوادر والأمالي والرقيات، والكيسانيات، والهارونيات. وكثيرا ما يقولون: "ذكره محمد في الأصل"، ويفسره الشراح بـ "المبسوط"، فعلم أن الأصل مفردًا هو المبسوط، اشتهر به من بين باقي كتب الأصول. وقال في "البحر" في باب صلاة العيد عن "غاية البيان": الأصل أصلا؛ لأنه صنف أولا، ثم الجامع الصغير، ثم الكبير، ثم الزيادات. وقال: إن الجامع الصغير صنفه محمد بعد الأصل، فما فيه هو المعول عليه.
We have already stated that the books of Zahir al-Riwayah are called al-Usul (the sources). From this is the statement of al-Hidayah in the chapter of Tayammum: 'And from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf in other than the narration of al-Usul.' The commentators said: The narration of al-Usul: the narration of the two Jami's (al-Jami' al-Saghir and al-Jami' al-Kabir), al-Ziyadat, and al-Mabsut. And the narration of other than al-Usul: the narration of al-Nawadir, al-Amali, al-Ruqyat, al-Kaysaniyat, and al-Haruniyat. And they frequently say: 'Muhammad mentioned it in al-Asl,' and the commentators interpret it as al-Mabsut. Thus it is known that al-Asl in the singular is al-Mabsut, which became famous among the remaining books of al-Usul. And it is said in al-Bahr in the chapter of Salat al-Id from Ghayat al-Bayan: Al-Asl is the original because it was authored first, then al-Jami' al-Saghir, then al-Kabir, then al-Ziyadat. And he said: Indeed al-Jami' al-Saghir was authored by Muhammad after al-Asl, so what is in it is the relied-upon.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage establishes a fundamental rule of Hanafi fatwa hierarchy: the books of Zahir al-Riwayah (the six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani) are termed 'al-Usul' (the sources). The Hidayah references this distinction in the chapter of Tayammum, noting transmissions from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf that are not from the authoritative sources. The commentators clarify that 'riwayat al-usul' includes al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat, and al-Mabsut. The term 'al-Asl' in the singular, when Muhammad says 'dhakarahū fī al-asl', specifically refers to al-Mabsut. Al-Bahr, citing Ghayat al-Bayan, confirms that al-Asl (al-Mabsut) was authored first, followed by the other books. Importantly, although al-Jami' al-Saghir was compiled after al-Mabsut, it is considered the relied-upon source. This hierarchy is crucial for a mufti: when a ruling appears in both, the Jami' al-Saghir takes precedence because it represents the later and more refined compilation.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The six books authored by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani that contain the relied-upon transmissions from Abu Hanifa and his disciples.
الأصول (al-Usul): A collective term for the Zahir al-Riwayah books.
الأصل (al-Asl): In the singular, it specifically refers to Imam Muhammad's al-Mabsut.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi sources are hierarchically ordered; knowing the terminological distinction between al-Usul and al-Asl is essential for accurate fatwa.

Distinguishing Saghir and Kabir Books in Hanafi Transmission
Clarifying which books were ratified by Abu Yusuf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between Saghir and Kabir books in the Hanafi transmission hierarchy and apply the rule of preference when issuing fatwa.

Core Idea
Saghir books carry joint authority; Kabir books are Muhammad's own — know the distinction for correct tarjih.

A mufti must know not only the rulings but also the chain of transmission behind them. This lesson clarifies a critical distinction: which of Imam Muhammad's works were double-checked by Abu Yusuf and which were not. Understanding this hierarchy ensures that fatwas are based on the most authoritative sources within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Categories
Recognize that books described as 'al-Saghir' (e.g., al-Jami' al-Saghir) are those presented to and approved by both Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. Books described as 'al-Kabir' (e.g., al-Jami' al-Kabir) were compiled solely by Muhammad without review by Abu Yusuf.
The terms 'Saghir' and 'Kabir' do not refer to physical size but to the approval chain.
2
Understand the Approval Chain
Grasp the historical context: after Abu Yusuf became chief judge, Muhammad would present his works to him for review. Works that were reviewed and agreed upon are called 'Saghir'. Works he authored later without such review are 'Kabir'.
This is based on statements from al-Bahr and Ibn Amir Haj al-Halabi.
3
Memorize the Examples
Learn the specific Kabir books mentioned: al-Mudaraba al-Kabir, al-Muzara'a al-Kabir, al-Ma'dhun al-Kabir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Kabir. These are all Muhammad's own compilations.
The corresponding Saghir versions also exist for some.
4
Apply Ibn al-Humam's Rule
Note the rule: if Muhammad narrates a ruling without noting any disagreement, it is considered the unanimous position of the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad). This rule is used in tarjih when resolving apparent conflicts.
This is a separate but related principle from the same passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال في "البحر" في بحث التشهد: كل تأليف لمحمد بن الحسن موصوف بـ"الصغير"، فهو باتفاق الشيخين: أبي يوسف ومحمد، بخلاف "الكبير"، فإنه لم يعرض على أبي يوسف. وقال المحقق ابن أمير حاج الحلبي في شرحه على "المنية" في بحث التسميع: "إن محمدا قرأ أكثر الكتب على أبي يوسف، إلا ما كان فيه اسم الكبير، فإنه من تصنيف محمد كـ "المضاربة الكبير"، و"المزارعة الكبير"، و"المأذون الكبير"، و"الجامع الكبير"، و"السير الكبير". وذكر المحقق ابن الهمام كما في فتاوى تلميذه العلامة قاسم: "أن ما لم يحكِ محمد فيه خلافا، فهو قولهم جميعا".
And he said in al-Bahr in the discussion of Tashahhud: Every work of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan described as 'al-Saghir' is by agreement of the two Shaykhs: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. Contrary to 'al-Kabir', for it was not presented to Abu Yusuf. And the investigator Ibn Amir Haj al-Halabi said in his commentary on al-Munya in the discussion of Tasmi': 'Indeed Muhammad read most of the books to Abu Yusuf, except those in which the name 'al-Kabir' appears, for they are Muhammad's own works, such as al-Mudaraba al-Kabir, al-Muzara'a al-Kabir, al-Ma'dhun al-Kabir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, and al-Siyar al-Kabir.' And the investigator Ibn al-Humam mentioned, as in the fatawa of his student Allamah Qasim: 'That which Muhammad did not relate a difference in, it is the statement of all of them.'
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage establishes a crucial distinction for muftis: books with 'Saghir' (Small) in their title were presented to and approved by both Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, thus reflecting their joint agreement. Books with 'Kabir' (Large) were authored solely by Muhammad without review by Abu Yusuf. This does not diminish their authority but indicates a different transmission path. The examples given include al-Mudaraba al-Kabir, al-Muzara'a al-Kabir, etc. Furthermore, a rule from Ibn al-Humam: if Muhammad narrates a ruling without noting any disagreement, it is considered the unanimous position of the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad). This rule is used in tarjih (preference) when resolving apparent conflicts.

Key Terms
الصغير (al-Saghir): A descriptor for works presented to and agreed upon by both Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.
الكبير (al-Kabir): A descriptor for works authored solely by Muhammad without presentation to Abu Yusuf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does 'al-Saghir' indicate about a book by Imam Muhammad?
A) It is smaller in size
B) It was presented to and approved by Abu Yusuf
C) It contains only prayers
D) It was written later

Key Takeaway
When issuing fatwa, prefer rulings from Saghir books over Kabir books, as they carry joint approval of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Method of Tarjih and Authoritative Hanafi Texts
Explaining the rule for preferring opinions and listing authoritative books

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule for tarjih when there is ikhtilaf, distinguishing the duties of a mujtahid from those of a muqallid, and identify the most authoritative Hanafi texts for fatwa.

Core Idea
The muqallid follows the latest classification unless later scholars choose otherwise — their chosen opinion becomes obligatory.

This passage from Rasm al-Mufti sources lays down a critical procedural rule for Hanafi fatwa. It distinguishes the method of the mujtahid, who weighs evidences, from the muqallid, who relies on authoritative compilations. Understanding this rule ensures that you correctly navigate cases of ikhtilaf within the school, and know which texts to prioritize.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two roles
The passage distinguishes between the mujtahid and the muqallid. The mujtahid looks at evidences and chooses the preponderant opinion. The muqallid follows authoritative compilations.
This is a fundamental distinction in Hanafi fatwa methodology.
2
Extract the default rule for the muqallid
The default rule for the muqallid is to take the last classification (al-tasnif al-akhir), which is identified as al-Siyar.
Al-Siyar refers to Imam Muhammad's al-Siyar al-Kabir.
3
Identify the exception
If later mashayikh (later scholars) choose a different opinion, that chosen opinion becomes obligatory (wajib al-‘amal), even if it is the opinion of Zufar.
This overrides the default rule, showing that later scholarly consensus can shift the relied-upon position.
4
Locate the authoritative books
The passage identifies Kitab al-Kafi as the collection of the six books of Zahir al-Riwaya. Its strongest commentary is Mabsut al-Sarakhsi, which is so authoritative that nothing contradictory is acted upon.
Mabsut al-Sarakhsi is considered the ultimate source for fatwa in the Hanafi school.
5
Assess the authority of Mabsut al-Sarakhsi
Multiple sources confirm that fatwa is not given except from Mabsut al-Sarakhsi, and it is relied upon exclusively.
This establishes a clear hierarchy: al-Kafi > Mabsut al-Sarakhsi > other commentaries.

وجه ترجيح الراجح عند الاختلاف
دون العراق؛ فإنها محدثة فتحا فبلغ ذلك محمدا، فغاظه ذلك، وفرّغ نفسه حتى صنّف هذا الكتاب فحكي أنه لما نظر فيه الأوزاعي قال: لا ما ضمنه من الأحاديث لقلت: إنه يضع العلم، وإن الله تعالى عيّن جهة إصابة الجواب في رأيه، صدق الله العظيم: ﴿وَفَوْقَ كُلِّ ذِي عِلْمٍ عَلِيم﴾ (يوسف: ٧٦). ثم أمر محمد أن يكتب هذا في ستين دفترا، وأن يحمل على عجلة إلى باب الخليفة، فأعجبه ذلك، وعده من مفاخر زمانه.

"كتاب الكافي" للحاكم
قال في "فتح القدير" وغيره: "إن "كتاب الكافي" هو جمع كلام محمد كتبه الست التي هي كتب ظاهر الرواية".
وفي شرح الأشباه للعلامة إبراهيم البيري: "اعلم أن من كتب مسائل الأصول كتاب الكافي للحاكم الشهيد، وهو كتاب معتمد في نقل المذهب، شرحه جماعة من المشايخ منهم شمس الأئمة السرخسي، وهو المشهور بـ" مبسوط السرخسي".
قال الشيخ إسماعيل النابلسي: قال العلامة الطرسوسي: مبسوط السرخسي لا يعمل بما يخالفه ولا يركن إلا إليه، ولا يفتى ولا يعول إلا عليه".
وذكر التميمي في طبقاته أشعارا كثيرة في مدحه، منها ما أنشده لبعضهم:
عليك بمبسوط السرخسي إنه هو البحر والدر الفريد مسائله ولا تعتمد إلا عليه فإنه يجاب بإعطاء الرغائب سائله
قال العلامة الشيخ هبة الله البعلي في شرحه على "الأشباه": "المبسوط" للإمام الكبير محمد بن محمد بن أبي سهل السرخسي، أحد الأئمة الكبار المتكلم الفقيه الأصولي، لزم شمس الأئمة عبد العزيز الحلواني وتخرج به حتى صار أنظر أهل زمانه، وأخذ بالتصنيف وأملى "المبسوط" نحو خمسة عشر مجلدا، وهو في السجن بأوزجند، بكلمة كان فيها من الناصحين توفي سنة أربع مائة وتسعين".
The manner of preferring the preponderant opinion when there is disagreement
... other than Iraq; for it is an innovation [فتحا?] conquest, and that reached Muhammad, and it angered him, and he devoted himself until he compiled this book. It is narrated that when al-Awza'i looked at it, he said: 'Were it not for what it contains of hadiths, I would have said that he is placing knowledge [deceptively]. And Allah Almighty appointed the direction of correctness in his opinion. Allah the Almighty spoke the truth: And above every possessor of knowledge is the All-Knowing (Yusuf 12:76). Then he commanded Muhammad to write this in sixty notebooks and to carry it on a cart to the caliph's gate. That pleased him, and he counted it among the glories of his time.'
[The manner of preferring the preponderant opinion when there is disagreement]
And in Sharh al-Ashbah by al-Biri: 'Our scholars said: When an incident is disputed, the best and chosen course for the mujtahid is to look at the evidences and look at what is preponderant in his view. The muqallid takes the last classification, which is al-Siyar, unless the later scholars choose otherwise, then acting on it is obligatory, even if it is the opinion of Zufar. And the six books are gathered in Kitab al-Kafi of al-Hakim al-Shahid, for it is sufficient. Its strongest commentary, which is like the sun, is the Mabsut of Shams al-Umma al-Sarakhsi, relied upon in transmission. Nothing is acted upon that contradicts it, and nothing is turned away from it. Among them: Mabsut Shams al-Umma: a change necessitated by meter; for he is nicknamed 'Shams al-A'imma', plural of imam. Benefit: The title 'Shams al-A'imma' is given to many of our imams: Shams al-A'imma al-Halawani, his student Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi, Shams al-A'imma Muhammad Abd al-Sattar al-Kardari, Shams al-A'imma Bakr ibn Muhammad al-Zaranjari, his son Shams al-A'imma Imad al-Din Umar ibn Bakr ibn Muhammad al-Zaranjari, Shams al-A'imma al-Bayhaqi, Shams al-A'imma al-Uzjandi, and his name is Mahmud, and often he is called 'Shams al-Islam'. This is found in Hashiyat Nuh Afandi on al-Durar wa al-Ghurar in the chapter of mahr.'
'Kitab al-Kafi' of al-Hakim
He said in Fath al-Qadir and others: 'Indeed Kitab al-Kafi is the collection of the statements of Muhammad, his six books which are the books of Zahir al-Riwaya.'
And in Sharh al-Ashbah of the scholar Ibrahim al-Biri: 'Know that among the books of the foundational issues is Kitab al-Kafi of al-Hakim al-Shahid, and it is a reliable book in transmitting the madhhab. A group of scholars commented on it, among them Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi, and it is famous as Mabsut al-Sarakhsi.'
Sheikh Ismail al-Nabulsi said: Allama al-Tarsusi said: 'Mabsut al-Sarakhsi: nothing is acted upon that contradicts it, and nothing is relied upon except it; fatwa is not given except from it, and nothing is depended upon except it.'
And al-Tamimi in his Tabaqat mentioned many poems in its praise, among them what someone recited:
'You must use Mabsut al-Sarakhsi, for it is the sea and the unique pearl of its issues. Rely only on it, for it gives the seeker what he desires.'
The scholar Sheikh Hibat Allah al-Ba'li said in his commentary on al-Ashbah: 'Al-Mabsut is by the great Imam Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Abi Sahl al-Sarakhsi, one of the great imams, theologian, jurist, and usuli. He was a companion of Shams al-A'imma Abd al-Aziz al-Halawani and graduated from him until he became the most insightful of his time. He took to writing and dictated al-Mabsut in about fifteen volumes while he was in prison in Uzjand, because of a word he uttered among the advisors. He died in the year 490 AH.'
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage is a rasm rule discussion on the methodology of tarjih (preferring one opinion over another) in the Hanafi school. It opens with a historical anecdote: Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani compiled a book that angered some, but when al-Awza'i saw it, he praised its hadith content and recognized its authority. The story illustrates how early Hanafi works were received.

Then the passage quotes al-Biri's Sharh al-Ashbah, which lays down the rule: when a case is subject to ikhtilaf, a mujtahid should weigh evidences and choose the preponderant opinion. A muqallid (non-mujtahid) should follow the latest compilation of the madhhab (al-tasnif al-akhir), which is al-Siyar (likely referring to Imam Muhammad's al-Siyar al-Kabir), unless later mashayikh have chosen a different opinion—then that chosen opinion must be acted upon, even if it is from a less authoritative source like Zufar. This establishes that the latest authoritative compilation is default, but later scholarly consensus can override it.

Next, the passage identifies the most relied-upon books: Kitab al-Kafi by al-Hakim al-Shahid, which collects the six books of Zahir al-Riwaya. Its strongest commentary is Mabsut al-Sarakhsi, which is so authoritative that nothing contradictory is acted upon, and it is the exclusive source for fatwa. The text then provides a list of scholars nicknamed 'Shams al-A'imma', indicating the high rank of these scholars.

Finally, the passage gives a biography of Imam al-Sarakhsi, noting that he dictated the Mabsut while in prison. This underscores the extraordinary effort behind the work and its unmatched authority in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
مبسوط السرخسي (Mabsut al-Sarakhsi): The authoritative commentary by Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi on Kitab al-Kafi, considered the most relied-upon text in the Hanafi school.
كتاب الكافي (Kitab al-Kafi): A collection by al-Hakim al-Shahid that compiles the six books of Zahir al-Riwaya of Imam Muhammad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Follow the opinion of Zufar.
D) Follow the opinion of the mujtahid.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fatwa, the muqallid's default is the latest classification, but later scholars' explicit choice overrides it; Mabsut al-Sarakhsi is the ultimate authority.

Resolving Contradictory Statements and Transmissions
Rasm al-mufti rule for handling contradictory statements and transmissions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule for resolving contradictory statements (qawl) from a mujtahid, distinguish qawl from riwaya, and determine the appropriate procedure for a mufti, advanced student, or layperson.

Core Idea
A mujtahid cannot have two contradictory statements; the later abrogates; if unknown, use heart (shahadat al-qalb).

This passage addresses a fundamental challenge for the mufti: how to handle apparent contradictions in the statements of Imam Abu Hanifa. It provides a clear hierarchy, from knowing the later statement to relying on inner conviction. Additionally, it distinguishes between a direct statement (qawl) and a transmission (riwaya), shifting the responsibility from the originator to the transmitter.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of inconsistency
Determine whether the issue involves two statements (qawl) from the mujtahid or two transmissions (riwaya) of his statement. This distinction is crucial because the source of the contradiction differs.
Qawl: contradiction originates with the mujtahid. Riwaya: contradiction originates with the transmitter.
2
If qawl, check for known later statement
If the later statement is known in time, it is considered a retraction (ruju') of the earlier statement. The later one is followed.
This resolves the contradiction definitively.
3
If no date known, apply hierarchy
First, prefer the statement with stronger supporting evidence. If not available, a mujtahid within the madhhab (muttabi') uses preponderators (murajjihaat). If none, he chooses with his heart (shahadat al-qalb).
A layman follows the most pious mufti; a mutafaqqih follows later scholars.
4
Consider the role of the questioner
The mufti must adapt his answer based on who is asking: for a layman, give the fatwa of the most pious and knowledgeable; for an advanced student, guide to the more correct and precautionary position.
This ensures the answer is appropriate to the level of the questioner.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اختلاف القول والرواية واعلم بأن عن أبي حنيفه جاءت روايات غدت منيفه اختار منها بعضها والباقي يختار منه سائر الرفاق فلم يكن لغيره جواب كما عليه أقسم الأصحاب [القولان لمجتهد] اعلم بأن المنقول عن عامة العلماء في كتب الأصول : أنه لا يصح في مسألة لمجتهد قولان للتناقض، فإن عرف المتأخر منهما تعين كون ذلك رجوعا، وإلا وجب ترجيح المجتهد بعده بشهادة قلبه، كما في بعض كتب الحنفية المشهورة. وفي بعضها أنه إن لم يعرف تاريخ، فإن نقل في أحد القولين عنه ما يقويه، فهو الصحيح عنده، وإلا فإن وجد متبع بلغ الاجتهاد في المذهب، رجح بما مر من المرجحات إن وجد، وإلا يعمل بأيهما شاء بشهادة قلبه. وإن كان عاميا اتبع فتوى المفتي فيه الأتقى الأعلم. وإن كان متفقهاً تبع المتأخرين، وعمل بما هو أصوب وأحوط عنده. كذا في "التحرير" للمحقق ابن الهمام. اختلاف القول والرواية ] واعلم أن اختلاف الروايتين ليس من باب اختلاف القولين؛ لأن القولين نص المجتهد عليهما بخلاف الروايتين، فالاختلاف في القولين من جهة المنقول عنه لا الناقل والاختلاف في الروايتين بالعكس، كما ذكره المحقق ابن أمير حاج في "شرح التحرير". لكن ذكر بعده عن الإمام أبي بكر البليغي في "الدرر" : أن الاختلاف في الرواية عن أبي حنيفة من وجوه:
Difference of Statement and Transmission. Know that from Abu Hanifa came transmissions that became elevated. He selected some of them, and the remaining choose from them the rest of the companions. So no one else has an answer, as the companions have sworn upon it. [Two statements for a mujtahid] Know that what is transmitted from the general body of scholars in the books of Usul: that it is not valid for a mujtahid to have two statements on one issue due to contradiction. If the later of the two is known, it is necessarily a retraction. Otherwise, it is obligatory for the mujtahid after him to weigh with the testimony of his heart, as in some famous Hanafi books. In some of them: if the date is not known, and in one of the statements there is something that strengthens it, then that is the correct one according to him. Otherwise, if there is a follower who has reached the level of ijtihad in the madhhab, he weighs with the previously mentioned preponderators if found. Otherwise, he acts on whichever he wishes with the testimony of his heart. If he is a layman, he follows the fatwa of the mufti who is more pious and knowledgeable. If he is a jurist-in-training (mutafaqqih), he follows the later scholars and acts on what is more correct and more precautionary according to him. This is in al-Tahrir by the investigator Ibn al-Humam. [Difference of statement and transmission] And know that difference in transmissions is not from the category of difference in statements, because the statements are the texts of the mujtahid on them, unlike the transmissions. So the difference in statements is from the aspect of the one from whom it is transmitted, not the transmitter, and the difference in transmissions is the opposite, as mentioned by the investigator Ibn Amir Haj in Sharh al-Tahrir. But he mentioned after him from Imam Abu Bakr al-Bulayghi in al-Durar: that the difference in transmission from Abu Hanifa is of several types:
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage discusses a critical rasm al-mufti rule: how to handle contradictory statements from a single mujtahid (Imam Abu Hanifa). It begins by noting that from Abu Hanifa multiple transmissions exist, some of which he chose and others were chosen by his companions. The core rule: a mujtahid cannot have two contradictory statements on the same issue because that is contradictory. If the later statement is known, it is a retraction (ruju'). If not, later jurists must weigh with their hearts (istishhad al-qalb). The text provides a hierarchy: if one statement has supporting evidence, it is preferred; if no evidence, a mujtahid muttabi' (within the madhhab) uses preponderators; otherwise he chooses with his heart. For a layperson, follow the most pious mufti. For a mutafaqqih (advanced student), follow later scholars. Then the passage distinguishes between 'qawl' (direct statement of the mujtahid) and 'riwaya' (transmission of his statement). In qawl, the inconsistency lies with the originator; in riwaya, it lies with the transmitter. The passage ends by mentioning al-Bulayghi's list of types of ikhtilaf in riwaya, but the list is cut off. This is foundational for a mufti's methodology when faced with apparent contradictions in the madhhab.

Key Terms
القولان لمجتهد (al-Qawlani li-Mujtahid): Two contradictory statements attributed to the same mujtahid regarding a single issue. In Hanafi usul, such contradiction is impermissible; the later statement is deemed a retraction.
اختلاف الروايتين (Ikhtilaf al-Riwayatayn): Discrepancy between two transmissions of a statement from the mujtahid, possibly due to errors in transmission. This is distinguished from ikhtilaf al-qawlayn; the issue lies with the transmitter, not the originator.
شهادة القلب (Shahadat al-Qalb): The procedure of a mufti using his inner conviction (based on evidence) to choose between conflicting rulings. Used when textual preponderators are absent; it is a legitimate method for tarjih.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How does a layman (ammi) choose between two conflicting rulings from Imam Abu Hanifa?
A) He follows the ruling that has more evidence.
B) He follows the fatwa of the more pious and knowledgeable mufti.
C) He chooses with his own heart.
D) He follows the later scholars.

Key Takeaway
When faced with contradictory statements from Imam Abu Hanifa, the mufti must first distinguish qawl from riwaya, then apply the hierarchy: known later statement → evidence → preponderators → shahadat al-qalb, and tailor the answer to the questioner's level.

Resolving Conflicting Statements from Imam Abu Hanifa (Ikhtilaf al-Qawl)
Defines the rule on conflicting statements from a mujtahid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule that a mujtahid cannot have two contradictory statements, and apply the methods of retraction or tarjih to resolve conflicting reports attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa.

Core Idea
A mujtahid's two contradictory statements on the same issue are invalid; resolve by retraction or tarjih.

This passage from Sharh al-'Uqud explains a foundational principle for muftis: when Imam Abu Hanifa appears to have said two opposing things on the same issue, this cannot be a genuine ikhtilaf al-qawl unless one was his later view. The passage guides the mufti on how to determine the correct position through tarjih, and also addresses the roles of laymen and legal scholars in following fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core prohibition
The text states it is not valid for a mujtahid to have two contradictory statements on one issue due to contradiction.
2
Determine chronological order
If the later statement is known, it is a retraction (ruju').
This is the default resolution.
3
Apply tarjih when chronology unknown
If date unknown, look for one statement with stronger support; if none, the mujtahid uses his heart's testimony.
Tarjih factors include strength of evidence.
4
Differentiate levels of followers
Laymen follow the most pious mufti; mutafaqqihs follow later scholars.
This ensures practical fatwa application.

اختلاف القول والرواية
واعلم بأن عن أبي حنيفه جاءت روايات غدت منيفه

فلم يكن لغيره جواب كما عليه أقسم الأصحاب
[القولان لمجتهد]
اعلم بأن المنقول عن عامة العلماء في كتب الأصول : أنه لا يصح في مسألة لمجتهد قولان للتناقض، فإن عرف المتأخر منهما تعين كون ذلك رجوعا، وإلا وجب ترجيح المجتهد بعده بشهادة قلبه، كما في بعض كتب الحنفية المشهورة. وفي بعضها أنه إن لم يعرف تاريخ، فإن نقل في أحد القولين عنه ما يقويه، فهو الصحيح عنده، وإلا فإن وجد متبع بلغ الاجتهاد في المذهب، رجح بما مر من المرجحات إن وجد، وإلا يعمل بأيهما شاء بشهادة قلبه. وإن كان عاميا اتبع فتوى المفتي فيه الأتقى الأعلم. وإن كان متفقهاً تبع المتأخرين، وعمل بما هو أصوب وأحوط عنده. كذا في "التحرير" للمحقق ابن الهمام.
اختلاف القول والرواية 
واعلم أن اختلاف الروايتين ليس من باب اختلاف القولين؛ لأن القولين نص المجتهد عليهما بخلاف الروايتين، فالاختلاف في القولين من جهة المنقول عنه لا الناقل والاختلاف في الروايتين بالعكس، كما ذكره المحقق ابن أمير حاج في "شرح التحرير".
لكن ذكر بعده عن الإمام أبي بكر البليغي في "الدرر" : أن الاختلاف في الرواية عن أبي حنيفة من وجوه:

شرح عقود رسم المفتي
٣٠
اختلاف القول والرواية
منها: الغلط في السماع، كأن يجيب بحرف النفي إذا سئل عن حادثة،
ويقول : لا يجوز ، فيشتبه على الراوي فينقل ما سمع. ومنها: أن يكون له قول قد رجع عنه ويعلم بعض من يختلف إليه رجوعه فيروي الثاني والآخر لم يعلمه فيروي الأول.
ومنها: أن يكون قال أحدهما على وجه القياس، والآخر على
وجه
الاستحسان، فيسمع كل واحد أحدهما، فينقل كما سمع". ومنها: أن يكون الجواب في مسألة من وجهين: من جهة الحكم، ومن جهة الاحتياط، فينقل كل كما سمع. قلت: فعلى ما عدا الوجه الأول يكون الاختلاف في الروايتين من جهة المنقول عنه أيضا لابتناء الاختلاف فيهما على اختلاف القولين المرويين، فيكونان من باب واحد ويؤيده أن ناقل الروايتين قد يكون ،واحدا، فإن إحدى الروايتين قد تكون في كتاب من كتب الأصول، والأخرى في كتب النوادر ، بل قد يكون كل منهما في كتب الأصول، والكل من جَمْع واحد وهو الإمام محمد حله، وهذا ينافي الوجه الأول، ويبعد الوجه الثاني، فالأظهر الاقتصار على الوجهين الأخيرين، لكن لا في كل فرع اختلفت فيه الرواية، بل بعض ذلك قد يكون لأحدهما، والبعض الآخر للآخر. لكن هذا إنما يتأتى فيما يصلح أن يكون فيه قياس واستحسان أو احتياط وغيره، نعم! يتأتى الوجهان الأولان فيما إذا اختلف الراوي.
وقد يقال: إن من وجوه الاختلاف أيضا، تردد المجتهد في الحكم لتعارض الأدلة عنده بلا ،مرجح أو لاختلاف رأيه في مدلول الدليل
Explanation of the Contract of the Mufti's Rule
29
Difference of Statement and Transmission
Know that from Abu Hanifa there have come lofty transmissions; some of them he chose, and the rest are chosen from him by all the followers. So no one else had an answer, as the companions swore.
[Two Statements for a Mujtahid]
Know that what is transmitted from the generality of scholars in the books of Usul is that it is not valid for a mujtahid to have two statements in one issue due to contradiction. If the later of the two is known, it is necessarily a retraction; otherwise, the mujtahid thereafter must give preference by the testimony of his heart, as in some well-known Hanafi books. And in some of them, if the date is not known, and one of the two statements is transmitted with something that strengthens it, that is the correct one according to him; otherwise, if there is a follower who has reached the level of ijtihad in the madhhab, he gives preference by the preponderances mentioned, if found; otherwise, he acts with whichever he wishes by the testimony of his heart. If the questioner is a layman, he follows the fatwa of the mufti who is more pious and more knowledgeable. If he is a legal scholar (mutafaqqih), he follows the later scholars and acts with what is more correct and more cautious according to him. This is in 'al-Tahrir' by the muhaqqiq Ibn al-Humam.
Difference of Statement and Transmission
Know that the difference of the two transmissions is not from the category of difference of the two statements, because the two statements are texts from the mujtahid, unlike the two transmissions. So the difference in the two statements is from the side of the one from whom it is transmitted, not the transmitter, and the difference in the two transmissions is the opposite, as mentioned by the muhaqqiq Ibn Amir Haj in 'Sharh al-Tahrir'.
But later he mentioned from Imam Abu Bakr al-Balighi in 'al-Durar' that the difference in transmission from Abu Hanifa is from aspects:
From them: error in hearing, as when he answers with the negative particle if asked about an incident, and says: it is not permissible, and the transmitter confuses and transmits what he heard. And from them: that he has a statement from which he has retracted, and some of those who visit him know of his retraction, so he transmits the second, while the other does not know it, so he transmits the first.
And from them: that he said one of them on the basis of qiyas, and the other on the basis of istihsan, and each one hears one of them and transmits as he heard. And from them: that the answer in an issue is from two aspects: from the aspect of the ruling and from the aspect of precaution, so each transmits as he heard.
I say: Apart from the first aspect, the difference in the two transmissions is from the side of the one from whom it is transmitted as well, because the difference in them is based on the difference of the two transmitted statements, so they become from one category. And this is supported by the fact that the transmitter of the two transmissions may be one: for one of the two transmissions may be in a book of the principal books (usul), and the other in the books of nawadir; rather, each of them may be in the books of usul, and all from a single collection, which is Imam Muhammad's compilation. This contradicts the first aspect and makes the second aspect unlikely. So the apparent view is to restrict to the last two aspects, but not in every branch where the report differs. Rather, some of that may be for one, and some for the other. But this only applies where qiyas and istihsan or precaution etc. are possible. Yes! The first two aspects apply when the transmitter differs.
It may be said: Among the aspects of difference also is the mujtahid's hesitation in the ruling due to conflicting evidences without a preponderant, or due to a difference of his opinion on the meaning of the evidence.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage is a methodological discussion on how a Hanafi mufti should handle conflicting reports attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa. It distinguishes between two types of disagreement: ikhtilaf al-qawl (conflicting statements directly from the Imam) and ikhtilaf al-riwaya (conflicting transmissions attributed to him). The author first establishes the rule that a mujtahid cannot have two contradictory statements on the same issue; if two statements are reported, one must determine which is later (indicating retraction) or use tarjih (preference). He then clarifies that ikhtilaf al-riwaya is different: it arises from the transmitter's error or differing contexts, not from the Imam himself holding two opinions. The author lists four causes of transmission differences: (1) error in hearing, (2) ignorance of the Imam's retraction, (3) one transmission based on qiyas and another on istihsan, and (4) one from the perspective of the legal ruling and another from precaution. He critiques the first two causes, arguing that they actually stem from the Imam's differing statements, not pure transmission error. He concludes that only the last two causes are distinct, and only in issues where qiyas/istihsan or precaution are applicable. The passage guides the mufti in how to weigh and resolve conflicting transmissions to issue sound fatwas.

Key Terms
اختلاف القول (ikhtilaf al-qawl): Two contradictory statements directly from a mujtahid on the same issue
ترجيح (tarjih): Method of preferring one transmission over another based on preponderating factors
شهادة القلب (shahadat al-qalb): The mujtahid's inner conviction as a means of preferring one view when clear evidence is lacking

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what should a mufti do if two contradictory statements from Abu Hanifa are reported without known chronology?
A) Follow the majority opinion.
B) Use tarjih or heart's testimony.
C) Combine both rulings.
D) Ask another scholar.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi method requires resolving apparent contradictions in Imam Abu Hanifa's statements by seeking the later retraction or applying tarjih, ensuring fatwa consistency.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
10 min
Distinguishing Ikhtilaf al-Qawl from Ikhtilaf al-Riwaya
Distinguishes types of scholarly disagreement in Hanafi law

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between ikhtilaf al-qawl and ikhtilaf al-riwaya, and identify the four causes of transmission differences attributed to Abu Hanifa.

Core Idea
Ikhtilaf al-riwaya stems from transmitters, not from Imam Abu Hanifa; resolve by identifying the cause.

This passage clarifies a common confusion: not all differences in Hanafi rulings reflect a genuine disagreement of Imam Abu Hanifa. Many are due to errors or differing contexts in transmission. The author lists four causes and critiques two, guiding the mufti to distinguish true ikhtilaf al-qawl from transmission variants.

Guided Path
1
Define the two types
Ikhtilaf al-qawl is from the mujtahid directly; ikhtilaf al-riwaya is from the transmitter.
2
List the four causes
1) Error in hearing, 2) Ignorance of retraction, 3) One based on qiyas, other on istihsan, 4) One based on ruling, other on precaution.
3
Analyze the author's critique
The author refutes the first two causes, arguing they revert back to ikhtilaf al-qawl.
4
Apply the distinction
When encountering conflicting transmissions, first determine if the cause is transmitter error or actual qawl difference.

intermediate

Causes of Difference in Rulings and Narrations
List and analysis of causes for conflicting narrations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four main causes of conflicting narrations from a single Hanafi imam and apply the commentator's method for weighing them.

Core Idea
Conflicting narrations from one imam arise from hearing errors, retractions, methodological differences (qiyas vs istihsan), and dual-aspect answers.

This passage from a work on the rules of ifta (rasm al-mufti) addresses a critical issue: how can a single great Imam like Abu Hanifa have multiple, seemingly contradictory narrations on the same issue? The author lists four causes and then adds his own analysis, helping the mufti understand why these differences occur and how to prioritize. Understanding these causes is essential for any scholar who must navigate the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four causes
Read the first part of the Arabic passage and list the four causes mentioned: error in hearing, retraction, qiyas vs istihsan, and ruling vs precaution.
Each cause represents a distinct scenario leading to conflicting reports.
2
Distinguish transmitter error from imam's variation
The commentator notes that apart from the first cause (hearing error), the other causes originate from the imam himself. Separate causes that involve the reporter's mistake from those involving the imam's own multiple statements.
This distinction affects how the mufti evaluates the reliability of each narration.
3
Analyze the commentator's critique
The commentator argues that the first two causes are less plausible when both narrations come from the same reliable transmitter like Imam Muhammad. Understand why he restricts them to cases where different reporters are involved.
This refinement is a practical tool for prioritizing narrations.
4
Recognize the additional cause
At the end, the author mentions a fifth cause: the mujtahid's own hesitation due to conflicting evidences or differing interpretations of a proof. Add this to your mental list.
This shows that even the imam himself may not have a settled view.

Difference of statement and narration. Among them: error in hearing, as when [the imam] answers with a negative particle when asked about an incident and says 'it is not permissible,' and the reporter is confused and transmits what he heard. And among them: that he has a statement from which he has retracted, and some of those who attend him know of his retraction, so he reports the second, while the other did not know it, so he reports the first. And among them: that one of them spoke on the basis of analogy (qiyas) and the other on the basis of juristic preference (istihsan), so each hears one and transmits as he heard. And among them: that the answer in a matter is from two aspects: from the aspect of the ruling and from the aspect of precaution (ihtiyat), so each transmits as he heard. I say: Apart from the first aspect, the difference in the two narrations is also from the side of the one reported from, because the difference in them is based on the difference of the two reported statements, so they are of one category. This is supported by the fact that the transmitter of the two narrations may be one, for one of the two narrations may be in a book of the principal works (usul) and the other in the books of rare transmissions (nawadir), or both may be in the principal works, and all from one compiler, Imam Muhammad—may Allah have mercy on him—and this contradicts the first aspect and distances the second. So the apparent view is to limit to the last two aspects, but not in every branch where narration differs, rather some of that may be for one and some for the other. But this only applies where qiyas and istihsan or ihtiyat and other things are suitable. Yes, the first two aspects apply when the reporter differs. And it may be said: Among the causes of difference also is the mujtahid's hesitation in the ruling due to conflicting evidences with no preponderance, or due to difference of his opinion regarding the purport of the evidence.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is a methodological explanation of the causes of difference in narrations (ikhtilaf al-riwaya) from a single imam, which is a crucial topic in the rules of ifta (rasm al-mufti). The author lists four main causes: (1) error in hearing—the mufti may give a brief answer that the reporter mishears; (2) the imam's retraction—some students know of the retraction and report the later view, others do not and report the earlier; (3) difference between qiyas and istihsan—the imam may give one answer based on analogy and another based on juristic preference, and each reporter hears only one; (4) the answer is given from the angle of the ruling (hukm) and from the angle of precaution (ihtiyat), and reporters transmit differently. The commentator then analyzes these causes, noting that apart from the first, the difference originates from the imam himself. He observes that both narrations may come from a single transmitter like Imam Muhammad, appearing in different books (usul vs. nawadir), which rules out the first two causes. Thus, the most appropriate view is to restrict the first two causes to cases where the reporter differs. He adds a fifth cause: the mujtahid's own hesitation due to conflicting evidences with no clear preponderance or his varying interpretation of the evidence.

Key Terms
اختلاف القول والرواية (ikhtilaf al-qawl wa al-riwaya): Differences in the transmitted statements and narrations from a single mujtahid imam.
الغلط في السماع (al-ghalat fi al-sama'): An error in hearing the imam's answer, leading to a misreport.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning used by the mujtahid to derive a ruling.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that often overrides qiyas based on considerations of equity or public interest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT listed as a cause of ikhtilaf al-qawl wa al-riwaya?
A) Error in hearing the imam's answer.
B) The imam retracting a previous statement.
C) The imam changing his ijtihad due to new evidence.
D) The answer being given from two aspects: hukm and ihtiyat.

Key Takeaway
A mufti must identify the cause of conflicting narrations to properly weigh them, recognizing that many differences reflect the imam's methodological flexibility rather than error.

Attribution of Two Opinions to a Mujtahid
Rasm al-mufti rule on attributing conflicting opinions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule of attributing conflicting opinions to a mujtahid in determining which opinion is operative for fatwa.

Core Idea
When a mujtahid cannot preponderate, both conflicting opinions are equally his and may be followed.

In rasm al-mufti, correctly attributing opinions to a mujtahid is crucial for giving fatwa. This passage clarifies the Hanafi position when a mujtahid has two conflicting opinions and no preponderance: both are his valid opinions. It refutes the views that neither or only one is attributed, and explains how exceptions arise when one opinion becomes preponderant or is abandoned. Understanding this ensures accurate transmission of the madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize that the case is when a mujtahid has two conflicting opinions and cannot preponderate (tarjih) between them.
This is the default situation when evidence is equally balanced.
2
State the Hanafi position
Both opinions are correctly attributed to the mujtahid because they are equal in his view.
This follows from Imam al-Qarafi's ruling that he may judge by either.
3
Refute incorrect views
Reject the views that neither is attributed (because he didn't settle) or that only one is attributed (due to assumed retraction).
The assumption of retraction is invalid; equality prevents preponderance.
4
Apply exceptions
If one opinion becomes preponderant (rajih) without abandoning the other, it is his active view and the other is a narration. If he abandons the other entirely, it ceases to be his opinion.
Even after abandonment, the earlier disagreement in the issue remains.
5
Determine fatwa implication
When no preference exists, a muqallid may follow either opinion. When one is rajih, fatwa must be by the rajih unless the other is also transmitted.
This is the operative rule for muftis consulting conflicting narrations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نسبة القولين إلى مجتهد
وقد قدمنا عن الإمام القرافي أنه لا يحل الحكم والإفتاء بغير الراجح لمجتهد أو مقلد إلا إذا تعارضت الأدلة عند المجتهد، وعجز عن الترجيح. أي فإنّ له الحكم بأيهما شاء؛ لتساويهما عنده. وعلى هذا فيصح نسبة كل من القولين إليه لا كما يقوله بعض الأصوليين من أنه لا ينسب إليه شيء منهما، وما يقوله بعضهم من اعتقاد نسبة أحدهما إليه؛ لأن رجوعه عن الآخر غير معين؛ إذ الفرض تساويهما في رأيه، وعدم ترجح أحدهما على الآخر. نعم إذا ترجح عنده أحدهما مع عدم إعراضه عن الآخر عنه، ينسب إليه الراجح عنده ويذكر الثاني رواية عنه، أما لو أعرض الآخر بالكلية، لم يبق قولا له بل يكون قوله هو الراجح فقط، لكن لا يرتفع الخلاف في المسألة بعد الرجوع، كما قاله بعض الشافعية، وأيده بعضهم بأن أهل عصر إذا أجمعوا على قول بعد اختلافهم، فقد حكى الأصوليون قولين في ارتفاع الخلاف السابق، فما لم يقع فيه إجماع أولى.
Attribution of the two statements to a mujtahid.
We have previously transmitted from Imam al-Qarafi that it is not permissible for a mujtahid or a muqallid to judge or give fatwa except by the preponderant (rajih), unless the evidences conflict for the mujtahid and he is unable to preponderate. That is, he may judge by whichever he wishes because they are equal in his view. Based on this, it is valid to attribute each of the two statements to him, unlike what some usuliyyun say that neither of them is attributed to him, and unlike what some say that he believes one is attributed to him because his retraction from the other is unspecified; since the assumption is their equality in his view and that neither is preponderant over the other. Yes, if one is preponderant in his view without his abandoning the other, then the preponderant is attributed to him and the second is mentioned as a narration from him. But if he abandons the other entirely, then it is no longer his statement; rather his statement is only the preponderant. However, the disagreement in the matter does not cease after retraction, as some Shafi'is said, and some supported it by saying that if the people of an era agree on a statement after their disagreement, the usuliyyun have narrated two opinions about the cessation of the previous disagreement; so if there is no consensus, it is more appropriate [that it does not cease].
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage addresses the rules for attributing two conflicting opinions to a single mujtahid, a key point in rasm al-mufti. It begins by citing Imam al-Qarafi's ruling that neither a mujtahid nor a muqallid may give a fatwa or judgment with anything other than the preponderant (rajih) opinion, except when the evidence is conflicting and the mujtahid cannot preponderate—in that case he may choose either because they are equal. Consequently, both opinions are correctly attributed to him. This refutes two incorrect views: (1) that neither opinion is attributed to him, and (2) that only one is attributed because the alleged retraction from the other is unspecified. The correct position is that when the mujtahid has no preference, both are his valid opinions. If he does have a preference but does not abandon the other, the preponderant is his view and the other is a narration (riwaya) from him. If he abandons the other entirely, it ceases to be his opinion. However, the passage clarifies that even after retraction, the earlier disagreement in the issue remains—it is not erased unless there is consensus (ijma') on one view, a point supported by Shafi'i usuliyyun.

Key Terms
نسبة القولين إلى مجتهد (nisbat al-qawlayn ila mujtahid): The rule of whether two conflicting opinions can both be correctly ascribed to a single mujtahid.
راجح (rajih): The preponderant opinion that outweighs its counterpart in the mujtahid's view.
ترجيح (tarjih): The process of weighing evidence to determine which opinion is stronger.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when a mujtahid has two conflicting opinions and no preponderance, how are the opinions attributed to him?
A) Only the later opinion is attributed; the earlier is considered abrogated.
B) Neither opinion is attributed to him because he has not settled.
C) Both opinions are correctly attributed to him.
D) Only the opinion that he actually issued in a specific case is attributed.

Key Takeaway
When a mujtahid cannot preponderate between two opinions, both are attributed to him and a muqallid may follow either.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
beginner
6 min
Attribution of Two Opinions to a Mujtahid: A Rasm al-Mufti Rule
Explains how and when a mujtahid's two opinions are attributed to him

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule for attributing two equal opinions to a mujtahid and identify when a mufti may choose between them.

Core Idea
When evidence is balanced, both opinions are attributed to the mujtahid and the mufti may act on either.

A mujtahid may derive two different rulings from the same evidence. How should these be recorded and attributed? This lesson unpacks the rule from Rasm al-Mufti: when one opinion is preponderant, it becomes the madhhab; when both are equal, both are authentically his. This rule governs fatwa practice and resolves confusion about contradictory narrations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Evidential Basis
Observe that a mujtahid's two opinions arise from evidence that is susceptible to two or more interpretations. Each interpretation leads to a separate answer.
The evidence itself is the same; the difference is in the istinbat (derivation).
2
Check for Preponderance (Tarjih)
The mujtahid may find one opinion stronger; if so, that opinion is attributed to him as his madhhab, and the other is recorded as a riwayah (narration). If no preponderance exists, his view is balanced between them.
Preponderance is determined by the mujtahid's own ijtihad, not by external factors.
3
Apply the Attribution Rule
When opinions are equal, both are attributed to the mujtahid. The mufti or judge may act on either opinion. This is the Hanafi position, supported by the practice of early scholars (e.g., 'Qala Abu Hanifa katha wa fi riwaya 'anhu katha').
Opposing views that attribute nothing or only one opinion are rejected.
4
Consider Retraction or Disregard
If the mujtahid later disregards one opinion entirely, it no longer remains his opinion. However, the earlier disagreement (ikhtilaf) does not automatically cease—unless there is consensus (ijma) on one view.
This nuance prevents erasing legitimate ikhtilaf from the record.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نسبة القولين إلى مجتهد
شرح عقود رسم المفتي الواحد، فإن الدليل قد يكون محتملا لوجهين أو أكثر، فيبني على كل واحد جوابا، ثم قد يترجح عنده أحدهما، فينسب إليه، ولهذا تراهم يقولون: "قال أبو حنيفة كذا وفي رواية عنه كذا"، وقد لا يترجح عنده أحدهما فيستوي رأيه فيهما، ولذا تراهم يحكون عنه في مسألة القولين على وجه يفيد تساويهما عنده فيقولون: "وفي المسألة عنه روايتان أو قولان".
وقد قدمنا عن الإمام القرافي أنه لا يحل الحكم والإفتاء بغير الراجح لمجتهد أو مقلد إلا إذا تعارضت الأدلة عند المجتهد، وعجز عن الترجيح. أي فإنّ له الحكم بأيهما شاء؛ لتساويهما عنده. وعلى هذا فيصح نسبة كل من القولين إليه لا كما يقوله بعض الأصوليين من أنه لا ينسب إليه شيء منهما، وما يقوله بعضهم من اعتقاد نسبة أحدهما إليه؛ لأن رجوعه عن الآخر غير معين؛ إذ الفرض تساويهما في رأيه، وعدم ترجح أحدهما على الآخر. نعم إذا ترجح عنده أحدهما مع عدم إعراضه عن الآخر عنه، ينسب إليه الراجح عنده ويذكر الثاني رواية عنه، أما لو أعرض الآخر بالكلية، لم يبق قولا له بل يكون قوله هو الراجح فقط، لكن لا يرتفع الخلاف في المسألة بعد الرجوع، كما قاله بعض الشافعية، وأيده بعضهم بأن أهل عصر إذا أجمعوا على قول بعد اختلافهم، فقد حكى الأصوليون قولين في ارتفاع الخلاف السابق، فما لم يقع فيه إجماع أولى.
Attribution of two opinions to a mujtahid. Explanation of Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: Indeed, evidence may be susceptible to two or more aspects, so he builds an answer on each one. Then one of them may become preponderant in his view, so it is attributed to him. For this reason you see them saying: 'Abu Hanifa said such-and-such, and in a narration from him such-and-such.' And one of them may not become preponderant in his view, so his opinion is balanced between them. Hence you see them narrating from him in an issue two opinions in a manner indicating their equality in his view, so they say: 'In the issue there are two narrations or two opinions from him.' And we have previously mentioned from Imam al-Qarafi that it is not permissible to judge or give fatwa based on anything other than the preponderant opinion for a mujtahid or a muqallid, unless the evidences are conflicting for the mujtahid and he is unable to weigh them. That is, he may judge by whichever he wishes because they are equal in his view. On this basis, attributing each of the two opinions to him is valid, unlike what some usul scholars say—that nothing is attributed to him—and what some say—that only one is attributed to him because his turning away from the other is unspecified, since the assumption is that they are equal in his view and neither outweighs the other. Yes, if one becomes preponderant in his view without him disregarding the other, then the preponderant one is attributed to him and the second is mentioned as a narration from him. But if he disregards the other entirely, it no longer remains an opinion of his; rather his opinion is only the preponderant one. However, the disagreement in the issue does not cease after retraction, as some Shafi'is said, and some supported it by saying that if the people of an age agree on one opinion after their disagreement, the usul scholars have narrated two opinions regarding the lifting of the previous disagreement, so it is more worthy [to say it does not lift] without consensus.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage is a rasm rule (methodological rule) for muftis regarding how to attribute two conflicting opinions to a single mujtahid. It explains that a mujtahid may have two opinions from the same evidence if the evidence is susceptible to multiple interpretations. When one opinion becomes preponderant, it is attributed as his madhhab and the other as a riwayah (narration). When both are equal, both are attributed as qawlayn or riwayatan. The passage also quotes Imam al-Qarafi (Maliki) emphasizing that fatwa must be based on the preponderant opinion. It refutes the idea that nothing is attributed to the mujtahid when opinions are equal, affirming that both can be attributed. Finally, it discusses that retraction of an opinion does not necessarily nullify the earlier disagreement.

Key Terms
قولان (qawlan): Two opinions of a mujtahid on the same issue
مجتهد (mujtahid): A scholar qualified to derive rulings directly from the primary sources
ترجيح (tarjih): Weighing evidence to determine the preponderant opinion
رسم المفتي (rasm al-mufti): The methodology and rules governing the practice of a mufti

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, when a mujtahid cannot find one opinion preponderant over another, what should be attributed to him?
A) Only the opinion he mentions first
B) Neither opinion, because he has no clear view
C) Both opinions, and the mufti may choose either
D) The opinion of the majority of scholars

Key Takeaway
When a mujtahid has two equally strong opinions, both are authentically his and a mufti may give fatwa by either.
