The Mufti's Obligation: Following Imam Abu Hanifa's View
Analyzing the permissibility and conditions of giving fatwa according to a view other than Imam Abu Hanifa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions under which a muqallid mufti must give fatwa according to Imam Abu Hanifa's view versus another Hanafi imam, and apply the distinction between fatwa and hikaya.

Core Idea
A muqallid mufti issues hikaya, not fatwa; his duty is to convey the Imam's view, even without knowing its evidence.

This lesson examines a foundational rule of Hanafi mufti practice: when must a non-mujtahid mufti follow Imam Abu Hanifa's view, and when may he adopt another Hanafi imam's view? The passage reveals an apparent tension between Imam Abu Hanifa's own statement requiring knowledge of evidence and the later practice of the mashayikh. The resolution lies in a subtle but crucial distinction between 'fatwa' (ijtihad-based) and 'hikaya' (narration). By parsing this discussion, you will understand the operative rule for muftis today.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Central Question
The passage opens with a question: How could later mashayikh give fatwa according to views other than Imam Abu Hanifa when they are muqallids? This sets up the problem.
2
Locate the Primary Condition
Imam Abu Hanifa's condition: no one may give fatwa by his view without knowing its evidence. Note the example of 'Isam to see the practical impact.
3
Observe the Shift in Time
The author distinguishes between the early period (condition applied) and later times (memorization suffices). This shift is the basis for the later rule.
4
Analyze the Objection by Khayr al-Ramli
He notes a contradiction: the condition seems to forbid what the author makes obligatory. Understand why he objects.
5
Apply the Distinction: Fatwa vs. Hikaya
The resolution: what a muqallid does is hikaya, not fatwa. Therefore, the prohibition on fatwa without evidence does not apply to hikaya. This explains how the later practice is consistent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال في "البحر" من كتاب القضاء فإن قلت: كيف جاز للمشايخ الإفتاء بقول غير الإمام الأعظم مع أنهم مقلدون؟ قلت: قد أشكل علي ذلك مدة طويلة، ولم أرَ فيه جوابا إلا ما فهمته الآن من كلامهم، وهو أنهم نقلوا عن أصحابنا: "أنه لا يحل لأحد أن يفتي بقولنا حتى يعلم من أين قلنا حتى نقل في "السراجية": إن هذا سبب مخالفة عصام للإمام، وكان يفتي بخلاف قوله كثيرا؛ لأنه لم يعلم الدليل، وكان يظهر له دليل غيره فيفتي به. فأقول : إن هذا الشرط كان في زمانهم أما في زماننا فيكتفى بالحفظ كما في "القنية" وغيرها، فيحل الإفتاء بقول الإمام، بل يجب، وإن لم نعلم من أين قال؟ وعلى هذا فما صححه في "الحاوي" - أي من أن الاعتبار لقوة الدليل- مبني على ذلك الشرط، وقد صححوا أن الإفتاء بقول الإمام فينتج من هذا أنه يجب علينا الإفتاء بقول الإمام وإن أفتى المشايخ بخلافه؛ لأنهم إنما أفتوا بخلافه لفقد الشرط في حقهم، وهو الوقوف على دليله وأما نحن فلنا الإفتاء وإن لم نقف على دليله. وقد وقع للمحقق ابن الهمام في مواضع الرد على المشايخ في الإفتاء بقولهما، بأنه لا يُعدل عن قوله إلا لضعف دليله، لكن هو أهل للنظر في الدليل، ومن ليس بأهل للنظر فيه، فعليه الإفتاء بقول الإمام. أقول: ولا يخفى عليك ما في هذا الكلام من عدم الانتظام، ولهذا اعترضه محشيه الخير الرملي بأن قوله: "يجب علينا الإفتاء بقول الإمام، وإن لم نعلم من أين قال" مضاد لقول الإمام لا يحل لأحد أن يفتي بقولنا حتى يعلم من أين قلنا؛ إذ هو صريح في عدم جواز الإفتاء لغير أهل الاجتهاد، فكيف يستدل به على وجوبه؟ فنقول: ما يصدر من غير الأهل ليس بإفتاء حقيقة، وإنما هو حكاية عن المجتهد أنه قائل بكذا، وباعتبار هذا الملحظ تجوز حكاية قول غير الإمام، فكيف يجب علينا الإفتاء بقول الإمام وإن أفتى المشايخ بخلافه؟ ونحن إنما نحكي فتواهم لا غير، فليتأمل.
And he said in 'Al-Bahr' from the book of judiciary: If you say: How is it permissible for the mashayikh to give fatwa according to the view of other than the Great Imam while they are muqallids? I said: This was problematic for me for a long time, and I did not see an answer except what I now understand from their words, which is that they narrated from our companions: 'It is not permissible for anyone to give fatwa according to our view until he knows from where we said it,' so much so that it was narrated in 'Al-Sirajiyya' that this was the reason for 'Isam's opposition to the Imam, and he used to give fatwa contrary to his view often, because he did not know the evidence, and another evidence appeared to him and he gave fatwa accordingly. So I say: This condition was in their time; as for our time, memorization suffices as in 'Al-Qunyah' and others, so giving fatwa according to the Imam's view is permissible, rather obligatory, even if we do not know from where he said it. Upon this, what was corrected in 'Al-Hawi' – i.e., that consideration is for the strength of evidence – is based on that condition, and they have established that giving fatwa according to the Imam's view is correct, so it follows from this that it is obligatory upon us to give fatwa according to the Imam's view even if the mashayikh gave fatwa contrary to it; because they only gave fatwa contrary to it due to the lack of the condition in their case, which is knowledge of his evidence; as for us, we may give fatwa even if we do not know his evidence. And it occurred to the muhaqqiq Ibn al-Humam in places to refute the mashayikh in giving fatwa according to the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), stating that one should not deviate from his view except due to weakness of his evidence, but he is qualified for considering evidence, and one who is not qualified for considering evidence must give fatwa according to the Imam's view. I say: It is not hidden from you what is in this speech of lack of order, and for this reason its commentator Khayr al-Ramli objected that his statement: 'It is obligatory upon us to give fatwa according to the Imam's view even if we do not know from where he said it' contradicts the statement of the Imam: 'It is not permissible for anyone to give fatwa according to our view until he knows from where we said it'; for it is explicit in prohibiting fatwa for other than the people of ijtihad, so how can it be used as evidence for its obligation? So we say: What issues from other than the qualified is not really fatwa, but rather it is a narration from the mujtahid that he said such-and-such, and by this perspective, narrating the view of other than the Imam is permissible, so how can it be obligatory upon us to give fatwa according to the Imam's view even if the mashayikh gave fatwa contrary to it? We only narrate their fatwa, nothing else, so consider.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage addresses the methodological rule regarding the permissibility of giving fatwa according to a view other than that of Imam Abu Hanifa. The author begins by citing a discussion from 'Al-Bahr' where a question is posed: how could later Hanafi scholars (mashayikh) issue fatwas according to views of other Imams (like Abu Yusuf or Muhammad) when they themselves are muqallids? The answer is that earlier Hanafis transmitted a strict condition from Imam Abu Hanifa: no one may give fatwa according to our view unless they know the evidence behind it. This condition was so serious that it caused 'Isam to oppose the Imam frequently, as he did not know the Imam's evidence and found other evidence compelling. However, the author argues that this condition applied in the early period when the school was still being established and the transmission of evidence was crucial. In later times, after the school was settled, it suffices for a mufti to simply memorize the rulings (hifz) without knowing the evidence, as stated in works like 'Al-Qunyah'. Thus, giving fatwa according to the Imam's view becomes not only permissible but obligatory. The author then connects this to the statement in 'Al-Hawi' that consideration is given to strength of evidence for those capable of ijtihad, but for the common mufti, they must follow the Imam. The author then presents an objection by Khayr al-Ramli, who notes a contradiction: the Imam's own statement forbids fatwa without knowledge of evidence, so how can it be used to obligate fatwa without such knowledge? The author resolves this by clarifying that what a non-mujtahid does is not technically 'fatwa' but rather 'hikaya' (narration) of the mujtahid's view. Since narration of another's view is permissible, there is no contradiction. Therefore, the muqallid mufti is simply conveying the Imam's ruling, and it is obligatory to convey the Imam's view even if other scholars (mashayikh) gave contrary fatwas. This lesson highlights the internal Hanafi debate about the qualifications for fatwa and the evolution of practice in the madhhab.

Key Terms
الإفتاء بقول غير الإمام (al-ifta' bi-qawl ghayr al-imam): Giving fatwa according to a view of Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani, or other Hanafi imams rather than Imam Abu Hanifa
حكاية (hikaya): Narrating or transmitting the ruling of a mujtahid without claiming independent ijtihad
أهل الاجتهاد (ahl al-ijtihad): Those qualified to derive rulings directly from primary sources; they may weigh evidence and prefer one view over another

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the relied-upon position for a muqallid mufti regarding giving fatwa according to Imam Abu Hanifa's view?
A) He must first know the evidence before issuing fatwa.
B) It is permissible but not obligatory for him to give fatwa according to the Imam's view.
C) It is obligatory for him to give fatwa according to the Imam's view even if he does not know the evidence.
D) It is prohibited for him to give any fatwa because he is not qualified.

Key Takeaway
A muqallid mufti's duty is to narrate (hikaya) Imam Abu Hanifa's view; he need not know the evidence, and he must follow the Imam's view even if later scholars differed.

The Qualification of a Mufti: Defining Ahliyyat al-Nazr wa al-Fatwa
Defining ahliyya and its condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition and condition of ahliyyat al-fatwa according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A mufti is qualified when correct opinions dominate errors, for Shari'a is built on the dominant.

This lesson introduces the foundational concept of ahliyya (qualification) for issuing fatwa. The Hanafi school defines it as the capacity to distinguish between opinions and weigh them, with the key condition that one's correct rulings exceed errors. This is rooted in the principle that Islamic law is based on the prevalent and dominant practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term and its legal context
The passage begins by defining 'ahliyyat al-nazr wa al-fatwa'. Identify that this is a condition (shart) for the validity of fatwa, not a pillar.
This is a condition for the mufti, not the act of fatwa itself.
2
Parse the two components of ahliyya
The text mentions two abilities: (1) being knowledgeable and distinguishing between statements (mumayyiz bayna al-aqawil), and (2) having the ability to prefer (tarjih) some over others. List these.
These are cumulative; both are required.
3
Analyze the dominance condition
The passage states that one does not become ahl (qualified) unless his correct statements (sawab) exceed his errors (khata). Why? Because when correctness abounds, it dominates (ghalaba), and the subordinate (maghlub) is disregarded. Link this to the maxim: 'Umuur al-shar' mabniyya 'ala al-aghlab.'
This is the quantitative threshold for qualification.
4
Consider the earlier view vs. the established school
The text mentions a narration from Ibn al-Mubarak requiring insight in hadith and opinion and knowledge of Abu Hanifa's statements. Note that this was before the school settled; later taqlid sufficed.
This shows the evolution of the Hanafi mufti hierarchy.
5
Apply the legal definition dissector
Using the term 'ahliyyat al-nazr wa al-fatwa', fill in the hukm, mahall, sabab, shart, mani, and athar as given in the toolbox.
This crystallizes the legal nature of ahliyya.

أهلية النظر والفتوى
والمراد بالأهلية هنا أن يكون عارفا مميزا بين الأقاويل، له قدرة على ترجيح بعضها على بعض، ولا يصير أهلا للفتوى ما لم يصر صوابه أكثر من خطأه؛ لأن الصواب متى كثر فقد غلب، ولا عبرة في المغلوب بمقابلة الغالب؛ فإن أمور الشرع مبنية على الأعم الأغلب، كذا في "الولوالجية" وفي مناقب الكردري قال ابن المبارك وقد سئل: "متى يحل للرجل أن يفتي ويلي القضاء؟ قال: إذا كان بصيرا بالحديث والرأي عارفا بقول أبي حنيفة حافظا له وهذا محمول على إحدى الروايتين عن أصحابنا، وقبل استقرار المذهب، أما بعد التقرر، فلا حاجة إليه؛ لأنه يمكنه التقليد".
أقول: ولا يخفى عليك ما في هذا الكلام من عدم الانتظام، ولهذا اعترضه محشيه الخير الرملي بأن قوله: "يجب علينا الإفتاء بقول الإمام، وإن لم نعلم من أين "قال مضاد لقول الإمام لا يحل لأحد أن يفتي بقولنا حتى يعلم من أين قلنا؛ إذ هو صريح في عدم جواز الإفتاء لغير أهل الاجتهاد، فكيف يستدل به على وجوبه؟ فنقول: ما يصدر من غير الأهل ليس بإفتاء حقيقة، وإنما هو حكاية عن المجتهد أنه قائل بكذا، وباعتبار هذا الملحظ تجوز حكاية قول غير الإمام، فكيف يجب علينا الإفتاء بقول الإمام وإن أفتى المشايخ بخلافه؟ ونحن إنما نحكي فتواهم لا غير، فليتأمل.
لا يجوز الفتوى بقولنا حتى يعلم.
وتوضيحه أن المشايخ اطلعوا على دليل الإمام، وعرفوا من أين قال واطلعوا على دليل أصحابه، فيرجحون دليل أصحابه على دليله، فيفتون به ولا يظن بهم أنهم عدلوا عن قوله لجهلهم بدليله؛ فإنا نراهم قد شحنوا كتبهم بنصب الأدلة، ثم يقولون: "الفتوى على قول أبي يوسف مثلا. وحيث لم نكن نحن أهلا للنظر في الدليل، ولم نصل إلى رتبتهم في حصول شرائط التفريع والتأصيل، فعلينا حكاية ما يقولونه؛ لأنهم هم
أتباع المذهب الذين نصبوا أنفسهم لتقريره وتحريره باجتهادهم. وانظر إلى ما قدمناه من قول العلامة قاسم: "إن المجتهدين لم يفقدوا حتى نظروا في المختلف، ورجحوا وصححوا إلى أن قال: فعلينا اتباع الراجح والعمل به، كما لو أفتوا في حياتهم".
وفي فتاوى العلامة ابن الشلبي: ليس للقاضي ولا للمفتي العدول عن قول الإمام إلا إذا صرح أحد من المشايخ بأن الفتوى على قول غيره. فليس للقاضي أن يحكم بقول غير أبي حنيفة في مسألة لم يرجح فيها قول غيره، ورجحوا فيها دليل أبي حنيفة على دليله، فإن حكم فيها فحكمه غير ماض ليس له غير الانتقاض.

Qualification for inquiry and fatwa. What is meant by qualification here is that he be knowledgeable, distinguishing between statements, having the ability to prefer some over others. He does not become qualified for fatwa unless his correct statements exceed his errors, because when correctness abounds, it dominates, and no heed is paid to the subordinate when opposing the dominant; for the matters of the Shari'a are built on the most common and dominant. Thus in al-Walwalijiyya. And in Manaqib al-Kardari, Ibn al-Mubarak was asked: "When does it become permissible for a man to give fatwa and assume judgeship?" He said: "When he is insightful in hadith and opinion, knowledgeable of Abu Hanifa's statement, and a memorizer of it." This is carried on one of the two narrations from our companions, and before the school was settled; after it was established, there is no need for that, because he can do taqlid. I say: It is not hidden from you the lack of order in this statement, and for that, his commentator al-Khayr al-Ramli objected to it, that his statement "We must give fatwa according to the Imam's statement, even if we do not know from where he said" contradicts the Imam's statement "It is not permissible for anyone to give fatwa according to our statement until he knows from where we said." For it is explicit in the impermissibility of fatwa for other than the people of ijtihad, so how can it be used as evidence for its obligation? We say: What issues from other than the qualified is not actually fatwa; rather, it is a narration from the mujtahid that he says such and such. With this consideration, narrating the statement of other than the Imam is permissible, so how can it be obligatory for us to give fatwa according to the Imam's statement even if the mashayikh gave fatwa contrary to it? And we only narrate their fatwas, nothing else. Let this be pondered. It is not permissible to give fatwa according to our statement until he knows. And its clarification is that the mashayikh have examined the Imam's evidence, and know from where he said, and have examined the evidence of his companions, so they prefer the evidence of his companions over his evidence, and give fatwa accordingly. And it should not be thought of them that they deviated from his statement due to ignorance of his evidence; for we see them having filled their books with the establishment of evidences, then they say: "The fatwa is according to the statement of Abu Yusuf, for example." And since we are not qualified for examining evidence, and have not reached their rank in fulfilling the conditions of derivation and foundation, we must narrate what they say; because they are the followers of the school who appointed themselves for its settlement and revision by their ijtihad. And look at what we have presented from the statement of Allama Qasim: "The mujtahids have not been absent; they looked at the disputed, weighed, and corrected, until he said: We must follow the preponderant and act upon it, as if they had given fatwa in their lifetime." And in the Fatawa of Allama Ibn al-Shibli: It is not permissible for the judge or the mufti to deviate from the Imam's statement unless one of the mashayikh states that the fatwa is according to someone else's statement. So the judge may not judge according to other than Abu Hanifa's statement in a matter where they have not preferred someone else's statement, and they have preferred the evidence of Abu Hanifa over his evidence; for if he judges in it, his judgment is void, and he has no option but to annul it. It is not permissible to give fatwa according to our statement until he knows from where we said. Then know that the Imam's statement "It is not permissible for anyone to give fatwa according to our statement, etc." can have two meanings: One is that what is meant is the apparent meaning, which is that when the madhhab of his imam is established for him in a ruling, like the obligation of witr, for example, it is not permissible for him to give fatwa on it until he knows the evidence of his imam. There is no doubt that this is specific to the mujtahid mufti, not...

Commentary
This passage discusses the qualifications (ahliyya) of a mufti and the nature of fatwa for those who are not full mujtahids. It begins by defining ahliyya as the ability to distinguish between different opinions and to weigh them, with the condition that one's correct statements exceed errors. It references al-Walwalijiyya and relates a narration from Ibn al-Mubarak about the conditions for a mufti, which includes knowledge of Abu Hanifa's statements and hadith. However, the author notes that after the school was established, taqlid became acceptable. The passage then addresses an objection by al-Khayr al-Ramli regarding an apparent contradiction: a statement that 'we must give fatwa according to the Imam's statement even without knowing his evidence' conflicts with Imam Muhammad's saying that 'it is not permissible to give fatwa according to our statement until one knows from where we said.' The response clarifies that what a non-mujtahid does is not actual fatwa but rather a narration (hikaya) of the mujtahid's positions. The mashayikh, who are capable of evaluating evidence, have done the work of weighing and prefering certain views. Therefore, the later followers merely transmit those preferred views. This is reinforced by quoting Allama Qasim and Ibn al-Shibli, who state that a judge or mufti must follow the mashayikh's preferred view unless they explicitly indicate otherwise. Finally, the passage explains that Imam Muhammad's statement can be interpreted in two ways: one is that a mufti must know the evidence, which applies only to mujtahids; the other, left incomplete, likely refers to the permissibility for non-mujtahids to follow the mashayikh.

Key Terms
أهلية النظر والفتوى (ahliyyat al-nazr wa al-fatwā): The legal capacity to engage in juristic reasoning and issue fatwas, defined by knowledge and ability to weigh evidence.
حكاية (ḥikāyah): Transmitting or narrating the fatwa of a mujtahid without claiming ijtihad.
المشايخ (al-mashāyikh): Senior Hanafi jurists who have reviewed the evidence and determined the preponderant view in the school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary condition for a person to be considered qualified (ahl) for fatwa?
A) Memorizing all of Imam Abu Hanifa's statements.
B) Being able to distinguish between opinions and having his correct statements exceed his errors.
C) Having memorized the Quran and hadith completely.
D) Being able to derive rulings directly from the primary sources.

Key Takeaway
A mufti is qualified when his correct rulings dominate errors; this is the foundational condition for fatwa in the Hanafi school.

Fatwa for Non-Mujtahids: Hikaya or Ifta?
Resolving the apparent contradiction in Imam Muhammad's statement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two interpretations of Imam Muhammad's statement and identify when fatwa is actually hikaya (narration) for non-mujtahids.

Core Idea
Non-mujtahids do not give fatwa; they narrate the preponderant views of the mashayikh.

This lesson tackles an apparent contradiction: Imam Muhammad forbade giving fatwa without knowing the evidence, yet later Hanafis obligate following the Imam's statement. The resolution is that a non-mujtahid's 'fatwa' is actually a narration (hikaya) of the mashayikh's preponderant view. The mashayikh have done the ijtihad, so the muqallid merely transmits.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core statement and the objection
Locate Imam Muhammad's saying: 'لا يحل لأحد أن يفتي بقولنا حتى يعلم من أين قلنا' (It is not permissible for anyone to give fatwa according to our statement until he knows from where we said). Then note the objection by al-Khayr al-Ramli: a statement obligating fatwa without evidence contradicts this.
The objection arises from a literal reading.
2
Understand the Hanafi response: distinction between ifta and hikaya
The response clarifies that what a non-mujtahid issues is not actually fatwa (ifta) but a narration (hikaya) of the mujtahid's position. Thus, the prohibition applies to mujtahids only, not to narrators.
This is a key terminological distinction.
3
Examine the role of the mashayikh
The mashayikh have examined the evidence of Abu Hanifa and his companions, weighed them, and chosen the preponderant view. They are the true ijtihad-level scholars. The later mufti merely follows their tarjih.
The mashayikh fill the gap left by the absence of full mujtahids.
4
Analyze the two interpretations of Imam Muhammad's statement
The passage presents two possible meanings: (1) the literal meaning—every mufti must know evidence, applicable only to mujtahids; (2) the implicit meaning—for non-mujtahids, it suffices to follow the mashayikh. The second is the operative view.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf: practical difference.
5
Apply the ruling: judge's obligation to follow mashayikh
From Ibn al-Shibli: a judge or mufti may not deviate from the Imam's statement unless a mashaykh explicitly says the fatwa is on another's statement. If he does, his judgment is void.
This shows the binding nature of the mashayikh's tarjih.

أهلية النظر والفتوى
والمراد بالأهلية هنا أن يكون عارفا مميزا بين الأقاويل، له قدرة على ترجيح بعضها على بعض، ولا يصير أهلا للفتوى ما لم يصر صوابه أكثر من خطأه؛ لأن الصواب متى كثر فقد غلب، ولا عبرة في المغلوب بمقابلة الغالب؛ فإن أمور الشرع مبنية على الأعم الأغلب، كذا في "الولوالجية" وفي مناقب الكردري قال ابن المبارك وقد سئل: "متى يحل للرجل أن يفتي ويلي القضاء؟ قال: إذا كان بصيرا بالحديث والرأي عارفا بقول أبي حنيفة حافظا له وهذا محمول على إحدى الروايتين عن أصحابنا، وقبل استقرار المذهب، أما بعد التقرر، فلا حاجة إليه؛ لأنه يمكنه التقليد".
أقول: ولا يخفى عليك ما في هذا الكلام من عدم الانتظام، ولهذا اعترضه محشيه الخير الرملي بأن قوله: "يجب علينا الإفتاء بقول الإمام، وإن لم نعلم من أين "قال مضاد لقول الإمام لا يحل لأحد أن يفتي بقولنا حتى يعلم من أين قلنا؛ إذ هو صريح في عدم جواز الإفتاء لغير أهل الاجتهاد، فكيف يستدل به على وجوبه؟ فنقول: ما يصدر من غير الأهل ليس بإفتاء حقيقة، وإنما هو حكاية عن المجتهد أنه قائل بكذا، وباعتبار هذا الملحظ تجوز حكاية قول غير الإمام، فكيف يجب علينا الإفتاء بقول الإمام وإن أفتى المشايخ بخلافه؟ ونحن إنما نحكي فتواهم لا غير، فليتأمل.
لا يجوز الفتوى بقولنا حتى يعلم.
وتوضيحه أن المشايخ اطلعوا على دليل الإمام، وعرفوا من أين قال واطلعوا على دليل أصحابه، فيرجحون دليل أصحابه على دليله، فيفتون به ولا يظن بهم أنهم عدلوا عن قوله لجهلهم بدليله؛ فإنا نراهم قد شحنوا كتبهم بنصب الأدلة، ثم يقولون: "الفتوى على قول أبي يوسف مثلا. وحيث لم نكن نحن أهلا للنظر في الدليل، ولم نصل إلى رتبتهم في حصول شرائط التفريع والتأصيل، فعلينا حكاية ما يقولونه؛ لأنهم هم
أتباع المذهب الذين نصبوا أنفسهم لتقريره وتحريره باجتهادهم. وانظر إلى ما قدمناه من قول العلامة قاسم: "إن المجتهدين لم يفقدوا حتى نظروا في المختلف، ورجحوا وصححوا إلى أن قال: فعلينا اتباع الراجح والعمل به، كما لو أفتوا في حياتهم".
وفي فتاوى العلامة ابن الشلبي: ليس للقاضي ولا للمفتي العدول عن قول الإمام إلا إذا صرح أحد من المشايخ بأن الفتوى على قول غيره. فليس للقاضي أن يحكم بقول غير أبي حنيفة في مسألة لم يرجح فيها قول غيره، ورجحوا فيها دليل أبي حنيفة على دليله، فإن حكم فيها فحكمه غير ماض ليس له غير الانتقاض.
لا يجوز الفتوى بقولنا حتى يعلم من أين قلنا ثم اعلم أن قول الإمام: "لا يحل لأحد أن يفتي بقولنا إلخ يحتمل معنيين: أحدهما أن يكون المراد به ما هو المتبادر منه وهو أنه إذا ثبت عنده مذهب إمامه في حكم كوجوب الوتر مثلا، لا يحل له أن يفتي بذلك حتى يعلم دليل إمامه ولا شك أنه على هذا خاص بالمفتي المجتهد دون
Qualification for inquiry and fatwa. What is meant by qualification here is that he be knowledgeable, distinguishing between statements, having the ability to prefer some over others. He does not become qualified for fatwa unless his correct statements exceed his errors, because when correctness abounds, it dominates, and no heed is paid to the subordinate when opposing the dominant; for the matters of the Shari'a are built on the most common and dominant. Thus in al-Walwalijiyya. And in Manaqib al-Kardari, Ibn al-Mubarak was asked: "When does it become permissible for a man to give fatwa and assume judgeship?" He said: "When he is insightful in hadith and opinion, knowledgeable of Abu Hanifa's statement, and a memorizer of it." This is carried on one of the two narrations from our companions, and before the school was settled; after it was established, there is no need for that, because he can do taqlid. I say: It is not hidden from you the lack of order in this statement, and for that, his commentator al-Khayr al-Ramli objected to it, that his statement "We must give fatwa according to the Imam's statement, even if we do not know from where he said" contradicts the Imam's statement "It is not permissible for anyone to give fatwa according to our statement until he knows from where we said." For it is explicit in the impermissibility of fatwa for other than the people of ijtihad, so how can it be used as evidence for its obligation? We say: What issues from other than the qualified is not actually fatwa; rather, it is a narration from the mujtahid that he says such and such. With this consideration, narrating the statement of other than the Imam is permissible, so how can it be obligatory for us to give fatwa according to the Imam's statement even if the mashayikh gave fatwa contrary to it? And we only narrate their fatwas, nothing else. Let this be pondered. It is not permissible to give fatwa according to our statement until he knows. And its clarification is that the mashayikh have examined the Imam's evidence, and know from where he said, and have examined the evidence of his companions, so they prefer the evidence of his companions over his evidence, and give fatwa accordingly. And it should not be thought of them that they deviated from his statement due to ignorance of his evidence; for we see them having filled their books with the establishment of evidences, then they say: "The fatwa is according to the statement of Abu Yusuf, for example." And since we are not qualified for examining evidence, and have not reached their rank in fulfilling the conditions of derivation and foundation, we must narrate what they say; because they are the followers of the school who appointed themselves for its settlement and revision by their ijtihad. And look at what we have presented from the statement of Allama Qasim: "The mujtahids have not been absent; they looked at the disputed, weighed, and corrected, until he said: We must follow the preponderant and act upon it, as if they had given fatwa in their lifetime." And in the Fatawa of Allama Ibn al-Shibli: It is not permissible for the judge or the mufti to deviate from the Imam's statement unless one of the mashayikh states that the fatwa is according to someone else's statement. So the judge may not judge according to other than Abu Hanifa's statement in a matter where they have not preferred someone else's statement, and they have preferred the evidence of Abu Hanifa over his evidence; for if he judges in it, his judgment is void, and he has no option but to annul it. It is not permissible to give fatwa according to our statement until he knows from where we said. Then know that the Imam's statement "It is not permissible for anyone to give fatwa according to our statement, etc." can have two meanings: One is that what is meant is the apparent meaning, which is that when the madhhab of his imam is established for him in a ruling, like the obligation of witr, for example, it is not permissible for him to give fatwa on it until he knows the evidence of his imam. There is no doubt that this is specific to the mujtahid mufti, not...
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage discusses the qualifications (ahliyya) of a mufti and the nature of fatwa for those who are not full mujtahids. It begins by defining ahliyya as the ability to distinguish between different opinions and to weigh them, with the condition that one's correct statements exceed errors. It references al-Walwalijiyya and relates a narration from Ibn al-Mubarak about the conditions for a mufti, which includes knowledge of Abu Hanifa's statements and hadith. However, the author notes that after the school was established, taqlid became acceptable. The passage then addresses an objection by al-Khayr al-Ramli regarding an apparent contradiction: a statement that 'we must give fatwa according to the Imam's statement even without knowing his evidence' conflicts with Imam Muhammad's saying that 'it is not permissible to give fatwa according to our statement until one knows from where we said.' The response clarifies that what a non-mujtahid does is not actual fatwa but rather a narration (hikaya) of the mujtahid's positions. The mashayikh, who are capable of evaluating evidence, have done the work of weighing and prefering certain views. Therefore, the later followers merely transmit those preferred views. This is reinforced by quoting Allama Qasim and Ibn al-Shibli, who state that a judge or mufti must follow the mashayikh's preferred view unless they explicitly indicate otherwise. Finally, the passage explains that Imam Muhammad's statement can be interpreted in two ways: one is that a mufti must know the evidence, which applies only to mujtahids; the other, left incomplete, likely refers to the permissibility for non-mujtahids to follow the mashayikh.

Key Terms
حكاية (ḥikāyah): Transmitting or narrating a fatwa of a mujtahid without claiming ijtihad.
المشايخ (al-mashāyikh): Senior Hanafi jurists who have reviewed the evidence and determined the preponderant view.
ثمرة الخلاف (thamarah al-khilāf): The practical consequence of a legal disagreement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the lesson, what is the status of a non-mujtahid mufti's 'fatwa'?
A) It is true fatwa (ifta).
B) It is a narration (hikaya) of the mujtahid's view.
C) It is invalid unless he knows the evidence.
D) It is a form of ijtihad.

Key Takeaway
Non-mujtahid muftis do not give fatwa; they narrate the preponderant views of the mashayikh, which resolves the apparent contradiction in Imam Muhammad's statement.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
12 min
The Rule: No Fatwa Without Knowing the Evidence
Explaining a rasm al-mufti rule with parsing of two interpretations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two possible interpretations of Imam Abu Hanifa's directive and determine which mufti is obligated to know the evidence.

Core Idea
A mufti must know the Imam's evidence—but only a mujtahid can truly weigh proofs; the rest simply narrate.

Imam Abu Hanifa famously stated that no one may issue a fatwa using his words without knowing the source. This passage unpacks that directive, explaining that it applies to the mujtahid mufti, not the ordinary muqallid. The later shuyukh (mujtahidun fi'l-madhhab) have already done the work of weighing evidences and determining the preponderant view. The muqallid mufti's duty is to narrate that preponderant view, not to independently verify the Imam's original proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule and its context
Locate Imam Abu Hanifa's statement: 'لا يجوز الفتوى بقولنا حتى يعلم'. Note that this is a foundational principle for muftis in the Hanafi school.
The rule is often quoted as 'لا يحل لأحد أن يفتي بقولنا إلا من يعلم من أين قلنا'.
2
Distinguish the two possible meanings
Parse the two interpretations: (1) literal—all muftis must know the Imam's evidence before issuing a fatwa; (2) specific—only the mujtahid mufti is obligated, as he can weigh contradictory proofs.
The author leans toward the second meaning.
3
Understand the role of later shuyukh
Recognize that the later mujtahidun fi'l-madhhab examined evidences and assigned preponderance. Their verdicts are binding on lesser muftis.
They sometimes prefer the companion's view over Abu Hanifa's, but this is due to evidence, not ignorance.
4
Apply the definition of taqlid
Use the legal definition: taqlid is taking the statement of another without knowledge of his evidence. Thus, knowing the evidence is outside taqlid and is a result of ijtihad.
Knowledge of evidence requires surveying all contradictory proofs, which only a mujtahid can do.
5
Determine the mufti's actual obligation
Conclude that the muqallid mufti must simply follow the preponderant view as determined by the mujtahidun fi'l-madhhab. He does not need to independently verify the Imam's proof.
This is supported by quotes from Allamah Qasim and Ibn al-Shilbi.

Source Text

لا يجوز الفتوى بقولنا حتى يعلم.
وتوضيحه أن المشايخ اطلعوا على دليل الإمام، وعرفوا من أين قال واطلعوا على دليل أصحابه، فيرجحون دليل أصحابه على دليله، فيفتون به ولا يظن بهم أنهم عدلوا عن قوله لجهلهم بدليله؛ فإنا نراهم قد شحنوا كتبهم بنصب الأدلة، ثم يقولون: "الفتوى على قول أبي يوسف مثلا. وحيث لم نكن نحن أهلا للنظر في الدليل، ولم نصل إلى رتبتهم في حصول شرائط التفريع والتأصيل، فعلينا حكاية ما يقولونه؛ لأنهم هم
أتباع المذهب الذين نصبوا أنفسهم لتقريره وتحريره باجتهادهم. وانظر إلى ما قدمناه من قول العلامة قاسم: "إن المجتهدين لم يفقدوا حتى نظروا في المختلف، ورجحوا وصححوا إلى أن قال: فعلينا اتباع الراجح والعمل به، كما لو أفتوا في حياتهم".
وفي فتاوى العلامة ابن الشلبي: ليس للقاضي ولا للمفتي العدول عن قول الإمام إلا إذا صرح أحد من المشايخ بأن الفتوى على قول غيره. فليس للقاضي أن يحكم بقول غير أبي حنيفة في مسألة لم يرجح فيها قول غيره، ورجحوا فيها دليل أبي حنيفة على دليله، فإن حكم فيها فحكمه غير ماض ليس له غير الانتقاض.
ثم اعلم أن قول الإمام: "لا يحل لأحد أن يفتي بقولنا إلخ يحتمل معنيين: أحدهما أن يكون المراد به ما هو المتبادر منه وهو أنه إذا ثبت عنده مذهب إمامه في حكم كوجوب الوتر مثلا، لا يحل له أن يفتي بذلك حتى يعلم دليل إمامه ولا شك أنه على هذا خاص بالمفتي المجتهد دون المقلد المحض؛ فإن التقليد: "هو الأخذ بقول الغير بغير معرفة دليله".
أخذه قالوا: فخرج مع معرفة دليله فإنه ليس بتقليد؛ لأنه أخذ من الدليل لا من المجتهد بل قيل: إن أخذه مع معرفة دليله نتيجة الاجتهاد؛ لأن معرفة الدليل إنما تكون للمجتهد؛ لتوقفها على معرفة المعارض، وهي متوقفة على استقراء الأدلة كلها، ولا يقدر
سلامته
من
على ذلك إلا المجتهد أما مجرد معرفة أن المجتهد الفلاني أخذ الحكم الفلاني من الدليل الفلاني فلا فائدة فيها فلا بد أن يكون المراد من وجوب معرفة الدليل على المفتي أن يعرف حاله، حتى يصح له تقليده في ذلك مع الجزم به وإفتاء غيره به وهذا لا يتأتى إلا في المفتي المجتهد في المذهب، وهو المفتي حقيقة، أما غيره فهو ناقل.
لكن كون المراد هذا بعيد؛ لأن هذا المفتي حيث لم يكن وصل إلى رتبة الاجتهاد المطلق يلزمه التقليد لمن وصل إليها، ولا يلزمه معرفة دليل إمامه إلا على قول. قال في "التحرير":
مسألة: غير المجتهد المطلق يلزمه التقليد، وإن كان مجتهدا في بعض مسائل الفقه، أو بعض العلوم كالفرائض، على القول بتجزئ الاجتهاد وهو الحق، فيقلد غيره فيما لا يقدر عليه وقيل في العالم: إنما يلزمه التقليد بشرط تبين صحة مستند المجتهد، وإلا لم يجز له تقليده. والأول قول الجمهور، والثاني قول لبعض المعتزلة، كما ذكره شارحه، فقوله: يلزمه التقليد" مع ما قدمناه من تعريف التقليد، يدل على أن معرفة الدليل للمجتهد المطلق فقط، وأنه لا يلزم غيره ولو كان ذلك الغير مجتهدا في المذهب.
It is not permissible to give fatwa by our word until he knows. Its explanation: The shuyukh have examined the evidence of the Imam, and they know from where he said, and they examined the evidence of his companions, so they give preponderance to the evidence of his companions over his evidence, and they give fatwa accordingly. And one should not think that they turned away from his statement due to ignorance of his evidence; indeed we see them filling their books with the establishment of evidences, then they say: 'The fatwa is on the statement of Abu Yusuf for example. And since we ourselves are not qualified to examine the evidence, and we have not reached their rank in fulfilling the conditions of furu' and usul, it is upon us to narrate what they say; because they are the followers of the madhhab who appointed themselves to its establishment and refinement through their ijtihad. And look to what we have presented from the statement of Allamah Qasim: 'The mujtahids did not fail until they examined what is disputed, and gave preponderance and corrected, until he said: upon us is to follow the preponderant and act upon it, just as if they had issued fatwa in their lifetime.' And in the Fatawa of Allamah Ibn al-Shilbi: It is not for the judge or the mufti to turn away from the statement of the Imam unless one of the shuyukh explicitly stated that the fatwa is upon the statement of someone else. So the judge may not judge by the statement of other than Abu Hanifah in an issue where the statement of another has not been given preponderance, and they have given preponderance to the evidence of Abu Hanifah over his [companion's] evidence. If he judges therein, his judgement is not executable; he has nothing but to rescind it. Then know that the statement of the Imam: 'It is not permissible for anyone to give fatwa by our word, etc.' admits of two meanings: One of them is that what is intended is what is immediately apparent, namely that when the madhhab of his Imam is established for him in a ruling, such as the obligation of Witr, it is not permissible for him to give fatwa by that until he knows the evidence of his Imam. And there is no doubt that according to this it is specific to the mujtahid mufti, not the pure muqallid; for taqlid is: 'Taking the statement of another without knowledge of his evidence.' Hence they said: So when [one takes] with knowledge of his evidence, it is not taqlid; because it is taking from the evidence, not from the mujtahid. Rather it is said: Taking with knowledge of his evidence is a result of ijtihad; because knowledge of the evidence is only for the mujtahid, due to its dependence on knowing the contradicting evidence, and that depends on surveying all evidences, and no one has the ability for that except the mujtahid. As for mere knowledge that a certain mujtahid derived a certain ruling from a certain evidence, there is no benefit in it. So it must be that what is intended by the obligation of knowing the evidence for the mufti is that he knows its status, so that his taqlid in that matter is correct with certainty and with his issuing fatwa to others. And this is only achievable for the mufti who is a mujtahid within the madhhab, and he is the mufti in reality; as for others, they are transmitters. However, that this is the intended meaning is unlikely; because this mufti, when he has not reached the rank of absolute ijtihad, is obligated to perform taqlid of one who has reached it, and knowledge of the evidence of his Imam is not obligatory upon him except according to one opinion. It is stated in al-Tahrir: Issue: The non-absolute mujtahid is obligated to perform taqlid, even if he is a mujtahid in some issues of fiqh, or some sciences like fara'id, according to the opinion of the divisibility of ijtihad, and that is the correct view. So he performs taqlid of others in what he is unable to do. And it was said concerning the scholar: He is only obligated to perform taqlid on condition that the soundness of the mujtahid's basis becomes clear to him; otherwise, it is not permissible for him to perform taqlid of him. The first is the opinion of the majority, and the second is the opinion of some Mu'tazila, as mentioned by its commentator. So his statement 'he is obligated to perform taqlid', along with what we have presented of the definition of taqlid, indicates that knowledge of the evidence is only for the absolute mujtahid, and it is not obligatory upon others even if that other is a mujtahid within the madhhab.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage is a rule (rasm) for muftis, explaining Imam Abu Hanifa's famous directive: 'No one may give fatwa by our word until he knows from where we said it.' The author first clarifies that the later shuyukh (mujtahidun fi'l-madhhab) have examined the evidences of the Imam and his companions, and they sometimes give preponderance to the companions' view. This is not due to ignorance of Abu Hanifa's evidence, but because they have weighed the proofs. Therefore, ordinary muftis who are not at that level must simply narrate the preponderant view as determined by those shuyukh, as they are the true architects of the madhhab. The author then quotes Allamah Qasim and Ibn al-Shilbi to reinforce that a judge or mufti cannot deviate from Abu Hanifa's position unless a mujtahid of the madhhab has explicitly ruled that fatwa is on another's saying. The author then analyzes the two possible meanings of the Imam's statement: either it applies to all muftis (implying they must know the evidence), or it is specific to the mujtahid mufti. The latter is more plausible because a non-mujtahid cannot truly know the evidence in the sense of weighing all proofs. The passage concludes by citing al-Tahrir on the obligation of taqlid for the non-absolute mujtahid, and that knowledge of the evidence is only required for the absolute mujtahid.

Key Terms
لا يجوز الفتوى بقولنا حتى يعلم (la yajuzu al-fatwa bi-qawlina hatta ya'lam): A rule that a mufti must know the evidence of the Imam before issuing a fatwa; interpreted as specific to the mujtahid mufti.
التقليد (al-taqlid): Taking the statement of another without knowledge of his evidence.
المجتهد المطلق (al-mujtahid al-mutlaq): One who can derive rulings directly from the primary sources without relying on a particular madhhab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary reason a muqallid mufti does not need to know the Imam's evidence?
A) The Imam's evidence is unknown.
B) The muqallid cannot properly weigh contradictory evidences.
C) The muqallid is not permitted to issue fatwa at all.
D) The muqallid must only follow the later shuyukh's preponderance.

Key Takeaway
Imam Abu Hanifa's directive is understood to apply to the mujtahid mufti; the muqallid mufti is obligated to follow the preponderant view as determined by the later mujtahidun fi'l-madhhab.

Taqlid and the Mufti's Knowledge of Evidence
Definition of taqlid and mufti's knowledge requirement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define taqlid and explain why a mufti must know the evidence, distinguishing between an absolute mujtahid and a mujtahid fi al-madhhab.

Core Idea
Taqlid is accepting without evidence; a mufti must know the evidence to avoid being a mere transmitter.

This passage from a Hanafi manual on fatwa procedure (Rasm al-Mufti) tackles a critical distinction: what is taqlid, and what does it require of a mufti? The text clarifies that a mufti cannot simply parrot the madhhab without understanding the evidence. It defines taqlid precisely and then explains that knowledge of evidence is only fully possible for an absolute mujtahid, while a mujtahid fi al-madhhab must still rely on the absolute mujtahid's proof.

Guided Path
1
Define Taqlid
Identify the precise definition given in the passage: 'taking the statement of another without knowledge of its evidence.' This is the foundation of the discussion.
Memorize the Arabic definition.
2
Distinguish Taqlid from Following Evidence
Understand that if one knows the evidence, it is not taqlid but deriving the ruling from the evidence. True knowledge of evidence requires weighing counter-evidence, which only an absolute mujtahid can do.
This distinction is key to understanding the mufti's role.
3
Identify the True Mufti
According to the passage, the true mufti is the one who knows the status of the evidence (mujtahid fi al-madhhab). Others are mere transmitters (naqil).
Only a mujtahid fi al-madhhab can issue fatwas with confidence.
4
Analyze the Ikhtilaf
Note the disagreement: the majority holds that a non-absolute mujtahid must practice taqlid without needing to know evidence, while some (Mu'tazila) require verification of the basis. The passage sides with the majority for practical purposes.
This ikhtilaf is about the obligation of the mufti, not the layperson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا يجوز الفتوى بقولنا حتى يعلم .
المقلد المحض؛ فإن التقليد: "هو الأخذ بقول الغير بغير معرفة دليله".
أخذه قالوا: فخرج مع معرفة دليله فإنه ليس بتقليد؛ لأنه أخذ من الدليل لا من المجتهد بل قيل: إن أخذه مع معرفة دليله نتيجة الاجتهاد؛ لأن معرفة الدليل إنما تكون للمجتهد؛ لتوقفها على معرفة المعارض، وهي متوقفة على استقراء الأدلة كلها، ولا يقدر على ذلك إلا المجتهد أما مجرد معرفة أن المجتهد الفلاني أخذ الحكم الفلاني من الدليل الفلاني فلا فائدة فيها فلا بد أن يكون المراد من وجوب معرفة الدليل على المفتي أن يعرف حاله، حتى يصح له تقليده في ذلك مع الجزم به وإفتاء غيره به وهذا لا يتأتى إلا في المفتي المجتهد في المذهب، وهو المفتي حقيقة، أما غيره فهو ناقل.
لكن كون المراد هذا بعيد؛ لأن هذا المفتي حيث لم يكن وصل إلى رتبة الاجتهاد المطلق يلزمه التقليد لمن وصل إليها، ولا يلزمه معرفة دليل إمامه إلا على قول. قال في "التحرير":
مسألة: غير المجتهد المطلق يلزمه التقليد، وإن كان مجتهدا في بعض مسائل الفقه، أو بعض العلوم كالفرائض، على القول بتجزئ الاجتهاد وهو الحق، فيقلد غيره فيما لا يقدر عليه وقيل في العالم: إنما يلزمه التقليد بشرط تبين صحة مستند المجتهد، وإلا لم يجز له تقليده. والأول قول الجمهور، والثاني قول لبعض المعتزلة، كما ذكره شارحه، فقوله: يلزمه التقليد" مع ما قدمناه من تعريف التقليد، يدل على أن معرفة الدليل للمجتهد المطلق فقط، وأنه لا يلزم غيره ولو كان ذلك الغير مجتهدا في المذهب.
It is not permissible to give fatwa by our statement until he knows. The pure muqallid: for taqlid is: 'taking the statement of another without knowledge of its evidence.' They said: so what comes with knowledge of its evidence is not taqlid; because it is taking from the evidence, not from the mujtahid. Rather it was said: taking with knowledge of its evidence is a result of ijtihad; because knowledge of the evidence is only for the mujtahid, due to its dependence on knowing the counter-evidence, which depends on surveying all evidences, and only a mujtahid can do that. As for mere knowledge that a certain mujtahid took a certain ruling from a certain evidence, there is no benefit in it. So it is necessary that the intended meaning of the obligation of knowing the evidence upon the mufti is that he knows its status, so that his taqlid of it is valid with certainty and giving fatwa by it to others. And this is only achieved for a mufti who is a mujtahid in the madhhab, and he is the true mufti. As for other than him, he is a transmitter. But this interpretation is far; because this mufti, since he has not reached the rank of absolute ijtihad, is obliged to taqlid of one who has reached it, and he is not obliged to know the evidence of his imam except according to one view. He said in al-Tahrir: Issue: A non-absolute mujtahid is obliged to follow taqlid, even if he is a mujtahid in some fiqh issues or some sciences like fara'id, according to the opinion of the divisibility of ijtihad, which is correct. So he follows others in what he is not capable of. And it was said concerning the scholar: he is only obliged to taqlid on condition that the validity of the mujtahid's basis becomes clear; otherwise he is not allowed to follow him. The first is the view of the majority, and the second is a view of some Mu'tazila, as mentioned by its commentator. So his statement: 'he is obliged to taqlid' with what we have presented of the definition of taqlid, indicates that knowledge of the evidence is only for the absolute mujtahid, and it is not obligatory upon others even if that other is a mujtahid in the madhhab.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the qualifications of a mufti regarding knowledge of evidence. It begins by stating that a mufti cannot give fatwa without knowing the evidence. It then defines taqlid as accepting another's opinion without knowing the evidence. If one knows the evidence, it is not taqlid but rather following the evidence. However, true knowledge of evidence requires the ability to evaluate counter-evidence, which only an absolute mujtahid possesses. The text then explains that the obligation for a mufti to know the evidence actually means he must know the status of the evidence (i.e., be able to verify its authenticity and applicability), which is only possible for a mujtahid fi al-madhhab. Such a mufti is the true mufti; others are mere transmitters. The author notes that this interpretation is problematic because a non-absolute mujtahid must still follow (taqlid) an absolute mujtahid and is not required to know the evidence except according to one opinion. The passage quotes al-Tahrir, which states that a non-absolute mujtahid is obliged to practice taqlid, even if he is specialized in some areas. The majority opinion holds that taqlid is obligatory without condition, while a minority (some Mu'tazila) require verification of the basis. The text concludes that knowledge of the evidence is only for the absolute mujtahid, not for anyone else, even a mujtahid fi al-madhhab.

Key Terms
تقليد (taqlīd): Taking the statement of another without knowledge of its evidence
مجتهد في المذهب (mujtahid fī al-madhhab): One who is capable of deriving rulings within the principles of a specific madhhab, but not an absolute mujtahid
مجتهد مطلق (mujtahid muṭlaq): An absolute mujtahid who can derive rulings directly from the primary sources without being bound by a specific madhhab

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the definition of taqlid?
A) Accepting the Quran and Sunnah directly.
B) Taking the statement of another with knowledge of its evidence.
C) Taking the statement of another without knowledge of its evidence.
D) Rejecting all scholarly opinions.

Key Takeaway
A mufti must know the evidence to be a true mufti; pure taqlid without knowledge is only permissible for those who cannot perform ijtihad.

The Intermediate Mujtahid and Fatwa by Takhrij
Debates the status of intermediate mujtahids and explains takhrij

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the status of mujtahid fi al-madhhab and explain the conditions and method of giving fatwa by takhrij.

Core Idea
A mujtahid fi al-madhhab is not a muqallid but a mujtahid who can issue fatwa by deriving rulings from the imam's principles.

This lesson clarifies a critical distinction in Hanafi ifta: the status of scholars who are deeply rooted in a madhhab but not absolute mujtahids. Are they mere muqallids or are they mujtahids in their own right? The passage presents the Hanafi resolution and then introduces the second mode of fatwa — takhrij, where the mufti derives rulings from the imam's usul rather than transmitting his exact words.

Guided Path
1
Identify the debate
Read the first part of the passage which quotes al-Zarkashi and Ibn al-Munir. What is the dispute about? Are followers of madhhabs considered mujtahids or muqallids?
The debate centres on whether a scholar committed to a madhhab can be called a mujtahid.
2
Analyse the Hanafi position
Note Ibn al-Munir's preferred view: they are mujtahids committed to not creating a new madhhab. Understand the reasoning: they possess the qualifications of ijtihad but the closure of absolute ijtihad prevents a new school.
This is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in Hanafi usul.
3
Understand the second type of ifta
The passage then states the second possibility: giving fatwa by takhrij (derivation) from the imam's principles. Distinguish this from mere transmission (naql).
Takhrij requires the mufti to understand the imam's sources and principles.
4
List the conditions for takhrij
From the excerpt of al-Tahrir, identify the qualifications: the mufti must be acquainted with the imam's foundations, be capable of deriving rulings, and have the ability to differentiate and combine.
These conditions transform a muqallid into a mujtahid fi al-madhhab.
5
Appreciate the historical reality
The author notes that takhrij occurred among early Hanafis who disagreed with Abu Hanifa in some principles and many branches. This shows that the category is not theoretical but practical.
This demonstrates that mujtahidun fi al-madhhab have legitimate authority in the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لكن نقل الشارح عن الزركشي من الشافعية: "أن إطلاق إلحاقه بالعامي الصرف فيه نظر، لا سيما في أتباع المذاهب المتبحرين؛ فإنهم لم ينصبوا أنفسهم نصبة المقلدين، ولا شك في إلحاقهم بالمجتهدين؛ إذ لا يقلد مجتهد مجتهدا، ولا يمكن أن يكون واسطة بينهما؛ لأنه ليس لنا سوى حالتين. قال ابن المنير : والمختار أنهم مجتهدون ملتزمون أن لا يحدثوا مذهباً، أما كونهم مجتهدين فلأن الأوصاف قائمة بهم، وأما كونهم ملتزمين أن لا يحدثوا مذهباً فلأن إحداث مذهب زائد بحيث يكون لفروعه أصول وقواعد مباينة لسائر قواعد المتقدمين، فمتعذر الوجود؛ لاستيعاب المتقدمين سائر الأساليب. نعم لا يمتنع عليهم تقليد إمام في قاعدة، فإذا ظهر له صحة مذهب غير إمامه في واقعة، لم يجز له أن يقلد إمامه، لكن وقوع ذلك مستبعد؛ لكمال نظر من قبله.
الثاني من الاحتمالين: أن يكون المراد الإفتاء بقول الإمام تخريجاً واستنباطاً من أصوله.
قال في "التحرير" وشرحه
www.
مسألة: "إفتاء غير المجتهد بمذهب مجتهد تخريجا على أصوله لا نقل عينه إن كان مطلعا على مبانيه - أي مأخذ أحكام المجتهد أهلاً للنظر فيها، قادرا على التفريع على قواعده، متمكنا من الفرق والجمع والمناظرة في ذلك بأن يكون له ملكة الاقتدار على استنباط أحكام
مستبعد وما استبعده غير بعيد كما أفاده في شرح التحرير، فإنه واقع في مثل أصحاب الإمام الأعظم، فإنهم خالفوه في بعض الأصول وفي فروع كثيرة جدا إلخ.
But the commentator transmitted from al-Zarkashi of the Shafi'is: 'That unconditionally attaching him to the pure commoner is questionable, especially regarding the followers of the deeply-rooted schools; for they did not set themselves up as muqallids, and there is no doubt in attaching them to the mujtahids; since a mujtahid does not follow another mujtahid, and there cannot be an intermediary between them; because we have only two states.' Ibn al-Munir said: 'The preferred view is that they are mujtahids committed to not creating a new madhhab. As for being mujtahids, because the characteristics exist in them; and as for being committed to not creating a new madhhab, because creating an additional madhhab such that its branches have principles and rules distinct from all the rules of the predecessors is impossible to exist, due to the predecessors having encompassed all methods. Yes, it is not impossible for them to follow an imam in a principle, so if the correctness of a madhhab other than his imam appears to him in a case, he is not permitted to follow his imam, but its occurrence is unlikely due to the completeness of the consideration of those before him.'
The second of the two possibilities: that the intended meaning is giving fatwa by the statement of the imam by way of extraction and derivation from his principles.
He said in al-Tahrir and its commentary: Issue: 'Giving fatwa by a non-mujtahid according to the madhhab of a mujtahid by way of takhrij upon his principles, not by transmitting his exact words, if he is acquainted with his foundations – meaning the sources of the mujtahid's rulings, qualified to examine them, capable of branching upon his rules, able to differentiate and combine and debate in that, such that he has the capacity to derive rulings. Unlikely, and what he deemed unlikely is not unlikely, as indicated in the commentary of al-Tahrir, for it occurs among the followers of the Great Imam (Abu Hanifa), for they opposed him in some principles and in many branches, etc.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement of the earlier discussion. It begins by quoting al-Zarkashi, who argues that followers of deep-rooted madhhabs (like the Hanafis) should not be equated with lay commoners; they are actually mujtahids in the madhhab, even if they commit to not creating a new madhhab. This is because they possess the qualifications of ijtihad, but the closure of ijtihad (in the absolute sense) prevents them from founding a new school. They can, however, follow an imam in a principle, and if evidence from another madhhab appears stronger in a particular case, they are not allowed to blindly follow their imam, though such situations are rare due to the thoroughness of earlier scholars.

The second part presents the second possibility for understanding the earlier statement: that the mufti gives fatwa by extracting and deriving rulings from the imam's principles (takhrij), not by merely transmitting his words. This is the method of a mujtahid fi al-madhhab. The passage from al-Tahrir outlines the conditions for this type of fatwa: the mufti must understand the foundations of the imam's rulings, be capable of deriving rulings, and have the skill to differentiate and combine. The author notes that this is not as unlikely as some think, since it actually occurred among the early Hanafi scholars who disagreed with Imam Abu Hanifa in some principles and many branches.

Key Terms
تخريج (takhrij): Deriving rulings from the principles (usul) of a mujtahid imam, not merely transmitting his statements
مجتهد في المذهب (mujtahid fī al-madhhab): A scholar qualified to derive rulings within the framework of a specific madhhab, but not an absolute mujtahid

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Blindly following the imam without any knowledge.
B) Transmitting the exact words of the imam.
C) Deriving rulings from the imam's principles (takhrij).
D) Creating a new independent madhhab.

Key Takeaway
Followers of deep-rooted madhhabs are mujtahids in the madhhab, capable of issuing fatwa by takhrij, not mere muqallids.

8 min
The Rule of Ifta by Non-Mujtahid through Takhrij
Examining the permissibility of a non-mujtahid issuing fatwa via takhrij

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a non-mujtahid may issue a fatwa via takhrij and identify the mufta bihi position from the Hanafi hierarchy.

Core Idea
A non-mujtahid may only give fatwa by takhrij if he is a mujtahid fi al-madhhab – aware of the imam's usul and able to derive rulings.

This passage examines a core rasm al-mufti rule: 'It is not permissible to give fatwa by our statement until he knows.' The discussion unpacks what 'knowing' means – does it require full ijtihad, or mere transmission? The passage presents three positions, culminating in the relied-upon view that a mufti must be at least a mujtahid fi al-madhhab to derive rulings from the imam's usul. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for any mufti operating within the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core rule
Extract the maxim 'لا يجوز الفتوى بقولنا حتى يعلم' from the passage. This sets the baseline: a mufti must have knowledge beyond rote memorization.
This maxim is often cited in rasm al-mufti works.
2
Distinguish naql and takhrij
The passage differentiates between mere transmission (naql) of the imam's words and derivation (takhrij) from his usul. The dispute centers on takhrij, not naql.
Naql is accepted with conditions of reliable narration; takhrij requires ijtihad within the madhhab.
3
Define mujtahid fi al-madhhab
Identify the definition from al-Tahrir: someone aware of the imam's foundations (mabani), capable of derivation, distinction, combination, and debate – possessing 'malakat al-iftiqadir'.
This term belongs to the third level of the sevenfold hierarchy of mujtahids.
4
Map the three positions
Three views: (1) strict (Abu Yusuf/Zufar: must know where from), (2) moderate (permissible if no full mujtahid), (3) absolute (any transmitter – author of al-Badi'). Note their proofs.
The author of al-Badi' argues the mufti is a mere narrator.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The passage resolves that the dispute is about takhrij, not naql. The relied-upon view is the middle: a mufti must be a mujtahid fi al-madhhab for takhrij; naql is accepted with reliability.
This view balances competence with practicality.

الثاني من الاحتمالين: أن يكون المراد الإفتاء بقول الإمام تخريجاً واستنباطاً من أصوله.
قال في "التحرير" وشرحه مسألة: "إفتاء غير المجتهد بمذهب مجتهد تخريجا على أصوله لا نقل عينه إن كان مطلعا على مبانيه - أي مأخذ أحكام المجتهد أهلاً للنظر فيها، قادرا على التفريع على قواعده، متمكنا من الفرق والجمع والمناظرة في ذلك بأن يكون له ملكة الاقتدار على استنباط أحكام مستبعد وما استبعده غير بعيد كما أفاده في شرح التحرير، فإنه واقع في مثل أصحاب الإمام الأعظم، فإنهم خالفوه في بعض الأصول وفي فروع كثيرة جدا إلخ.
لا يجوز الفتوى بقولنا حتى يعلم.
المتجددة التي لا نقل فيها عن صاحب المذهب من الأصول التي مهدها صاحب المذهب، وهذا المسمى بالمجتهد في المذهب جاز، وإلا يكن كذلك لا يجوز.

أقول: ويظهر مما ذكره الهندي: أن هذا غير خاص بأقوال الإمام بل أقول أصحابه كذلك وأن المراد بالمجتهد في المذهب هم أهل الطبقة أصحاب وهم الثالثة من الطبقات السبع المارة. وأن الطبقة الثانية - الإمام - أهل اجتهاد مطلق إلا أنهم قلدوه في أغلب أصوله وقواعده، بناء على أن المجتهد له أن يقلد آخر، وفيه عن أبي حنيفة روايتان، جاز: جواب الشرط في قوله: إن كان مطلعاً.
It is not permissible to give fatwa by our statement until he knows. But the commentator narrated from al-Zarkashi of the Shafi'is: 'Indeed, unconditionally deeming him as a layman is questionable, especially for the followers of the thoroughly grounded madhhabs; for they did not appoint themselves as mere muqallids, and there is no doubt in deeming them as mujtahids; because a mujtahid does not follow another mujtahid, and it is not possible for an intermediary between them; because there are only two states for us.' Ibn al-Munir said: The chosen view is that they are mujtahids who are committed to not creating a new madhhab. As for them being mujtahids, it is because the qualifications exist in them. As for them being committed to not creating a new madhhab, it is because creating an additional madhhab such that its furu' have usul and rules contradictory to all the rules of the predecessors is impossible to occur, because the predecessors have covered all methods. Yes, it is not impossible for them to follow an imam in a rule; but if it appears to him the correctness of a madhhab other than his imam's in an incident, he is not allowed to follow his imam. But the occurrence of that is far-fetched due to the completeness of the consideration of those before him.
The second of the two probabilities: It is that what is meant is issuing fatwa by the statement of the imam through takhrij and istinbat from his usul.
He said in al-Tahrir and its commentary: Issue: 'The fatwa of a non-mujtahid according to the madhhab of a mujtahid by takhrij based on his usul, not mere transmission of his exact words, if he is aware of his foundations – i.e., the derivations of the mujtahid's rulings, qualified to examine them, capable of deriving branches based on his rules, able to distinguish, combine, and debate in that, by having a faculty of power to derive rulings... [it is] far-fetched, but what he deemed far-fetched is not so far as he suggested in Sharh al-Tahrir, for it actually occurs in the companions of the Great Imam, for they differed with him in some usul and in many furu', etc.
It is not permissible to give fatwa by our statement until he knows.
...the newly occurring (matters) for which there is no transmitted statement from the master of the madhhab from the usul that the master of the madhhab laid down, and this is called mujtahid fi al-madhhab – it is permissible, otherwise it is not permissible.
And in Sharh al-Badi' al-Hindi: It is the chosen view of many of our Companions and others, for he narrated from Abu Yusuf, Zufar, and other our imams that they said: It is not permissible for anyone to give fatwa by our statement unless he knows from where we said it. And the statement of some: Whoever memorizes the statements and does not know the proofs, it is not permissible for him to give fatwa in what they differed about.
And it was said: It is permissible with the condition of the absence of a mujtahid, and the Allamah considered it as likely. And it was said: It is permissible absolutely, i.e., whether he is aware of the foundations or not, with or without the absence of a mujtahid, and this is the choice of the author of al-Badi' and many scholars, because he is a transmitter, so there is no difference between the scholar and others in that. And it was answered: The dispute is not about transmission, but about takhrij; because transmission of the exact madhhab of the mujtahid is accepted with the conditions of the narrator of reliability and others by agreement. End summarized.
I say: It appears from what the Hindi mentioned: That this is not specific to the statements of the Imam, but also to the statements of his Companions, and that the meaning of mujtahid in the madhhab are the people of the third level from the seven levels mentioned. And that the second level – the Imam – they are people of absolute ijtihad except that they followed him in most of his usul and rules, based on that a mujtahid may follow another, and about that there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa. 'Jaz' is the answer to the condition in his statement: 'If he is aware.'
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion on the rasm rule that 'it is not permissible to give fatwa by our statement until he knows' – meaning a mufti must understand the evidential basis of the madhhab, not merely transmit its rulings. The commentary opens with a quotation from the Shafi'i scholar al-Zarkashi, who argues that advanced followers of a madhhab should not be equated with laymen; they possess ijtihad but commit not to establish a new school. This sets up the framework for two possibilities for non-mujtahid fatwa: either it is permissible only through takhrij (derivation from the imam's usul) or through mere naql (transmission). The author then presents the text from Al-Tahrir, which stipulates that a non-mujtahid may issue fatwa via takhrij only if he has mastery of the imam's principles and the ability to derive new rulings – this qualifies him as a 'mujtahid fi al-madhhab'. The discussion then reports conflicting positions: the strict view of Abu Yusuf and Zufar denying license without knowing the proof; the moderate view allowing fatwa when no full mujtahid exists; and the broad view of the author of al-Badi' permitting absolute transmission. The author resolves the dispute by clarifying that the disagreement concerns takhrij, not naql; transmission is unanimously accepted with reliable narration. He concludes by noting that the criteria apply not only to the Imam but also to his senior disciples, and reaffirms that a 'mujtahid fi al-madhhab' belongs to the third level of the sevenfold hierarchy – one who can derive rulings from the established usul without being an absolute mujtahid.

Key Terms
مجتهد في المذهب (mujtahid fī al-madhhab): A scholar who is able to derive rulings from the usul of the imam, though not an absolute mujtahid; belongs to the third level of the seven levels.
تخريج (takhrij): Deriving rulings from the imam's usul for new cases not explicitly transmitted.
نقل (naql): Mere transmission of the exact statements of the imam without independent derivation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passagem, what condition must a mufti fulfill to issue a fatwa on a new case that has no transmitted ruling?
A) He must have memorized all the transmitted rulings of the madhhab.
B) He must be a mujtahid fi al-madhhab, able to derive from the imam's usul.
C) He must be an absolute mujtahid independent of any madhhab.
D) Any reliable transmitter may issue fatwa without condition.

Key Takeaway
A non-mujtahid may only issue fatwa via takhrij if he is a mujtahid fi al-madhhab; otherwise, he must transmit only the known rulings of the madhhab.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Condition for Mufti: Knowledge of Evidential Sources
Explaining the ikhtilaf on whether a mufti must know the source of Hanafi rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three positions on whether a mufti must know the source, apply the Hanafi refinement based on mufti level, and determine which mufti requires knowledge of the dalil.

Core Idea
A mufti's duty to know the source depends on his level: mujtahids must derive, narrators need only transmit.

This passage examines a famous condition for muftis: must they know the evidential source of Hanafi rulings? The author presents three views within the madhhab, then refines the rule by distinguishing between a mujtahid fi al-madhhab (who derives rulings) and a pure narrator (naqil) who simply transmits. Understanding this refinement is crucial for a mufti to know his proper role and responsibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling in question
Locate the central statement: 'لا يجوز الفتوى بقولنا حتى يعلم من أين قلنا' (It is not permissible to give fatwa according to our statement until he knows from where we said it).
This is attributed to Abu Yusuf, Zufar, and other Imams.
2
List the three positions
Identify the three views: (1) absolute requirement to know the source; (2) permissible only in absence of a mujtahid; (3) absolutely permissible for anyone.
The author of al-Badi' holds the third view.
3
Analyze the key distinction
Understand that the disagreement is not about narration (naql) but about derivation (takhrij). A naqil transmits the exact madhhab; a mujtahid derives new rulings.
Narration requires integrity, derivation requires knowledge of usul.
4
Apply the refinement
Determine which mufti levels the condition applies to: classes 3, 4, and 5 (mujtahid fi al-madhhab and above) must know the source for istinbat; pure narrators (lower levels) may simply transmit.
The story of Abu Yusuf following the people of Madinah supports permissibility of taqlid even for mujtahids in certain cases.
5
Examine supporting evidence
Consider the examples from Shafi'i scholars (al-Qaffal, etc.) who said they are not blind followers but their opinion coincided with al-Shafi'i's. This shows that even a mujtahid may follow another's principle.
This reinforces the idea that the rule is tailored to the mufti's role.

It is not permissible to give fatwa according to our statement until he knows. As for new issues for which there is no transmission from the author of the madhhab from the principles that he laid down, if the one called a mujtahid within the madhhab does so, it is permissible; otherwise it is not. In Sharh al-Badi' al-Hindi: it is the chosen view of many of our companions and others, for it is transmitted from Abu Yusuf, Zufar and other Imams that they said: It is not lawful for anyone to give fatwa according to our statement unless he knows from where we said it. And the wording of some: One who memorizes the statements and does not know the proofs, it is not lawful for him to give fatwa in matters where they differed. And it was said: it is permissible on condition of absence of a mujtahid, and the 'Allamah considered it preferable. And it was said: it is permissible absolutely, whether he is aware of the basis or not, whether a mujtahid is absent or not, and this is the choice of the author of al-Badi' and many scholars, because he is a narrator, so there is no difference between a scholar and others. The response was that the disagreement is not about narration but about derivation, because narrating the exact madhhab of the mujtahid is accepted with the conditions of a narrator (integrity etc.) by agreement. End summary. I say: It appears from what al-Hindi mentioned that this is not specific to the statements of the Imam, but rather includes the statements of his companions as well, and that by 'mujtahid in the madhhab' are meant the people of the third class of the seven classes mentioned, and that the second class - the Imam - are people of absolute ijtihad except that they followed him in most of his principles and rules, based on the fact that a mujtahid may follow another, and on this from Abu Hanifa there are two narrations. 'Jaaza' is the answer to the condition in his statement: 'if he is aware.' And supporting permissibility is the case of Abu Yusuf when he prayed Jumu'ah and they informed him of a mouse in the water tank of the bathhouse, he said: 'We follow the people of Madinah.' And from Muhammad: 'He follows one more knowledgeable than him,' or that his ijtihad agreed with their ijtihad in that. Since such is narrated from some of the Shafi'i Imams like al-Qaffal, Shaykh Abu 'Ali, and al-Qadi Husayn that they say: 'We are not followers of al-Shafi'i, rather our opinion agreed with his opinion,' similar is said about the companions of Abu Hanifa like Abu Yusuf and Muhammad all the more so. And they disagreed with him in many branches, yet their statements are not considered outside the madhhab. As established before. So it is settled from what we have mentioned that the statement of the Imam and his companions: 'It is not lawful for anyone to give fatwa according to our statement until he knows from where we said it' - is applied to the fatwa of the mujtahid in the madhhab by way of deduction and derivation, as you know from the words of al-Tahrir and Sharh al-Badi' - and apparently the people of the third, fourth, and fifth classes share in that - and that others suffice with narration, and that we must follow what they transmitted to us from them of their derivations not explicitly stated by the earlier scholars, and of their preferences, even if they were for other than the statement of the Imam, as we established at the beginning of this discussion; because they... or is a conjunctive attachment to his statement... as established. Then I saw in the handwriting of one I trust the following: Ibn al-Mulaqqin said in Tabaqat al-Shafi'iyyah: Ibn Burhan al-Awsat said: Our companions and the companions of Abu Hanifa disagreed about al-Muzani, Ibn Surayj, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad ibn al-Hasan. Some said they are absolute mujtahids, some said they are mujtahids in the madhhab. And Imam al-Haramayn said: I consider every selection of al-Muzani as derivation, for he does not contradict the principles of al-Shafi'i, unlike Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, for they contradict their companion. Al-Rafi'i said in the chapter of wudu: The singular opinions of al-Muzani are not counted as part of the madhhab if he did not derive them from al-Shafi'i's principle.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement of the rule 'لا يجوز الفتوى بقولنا حتى يعلم من أين قلنا' (It is not permissible to give fatwa according to our statement until one knows from where we said it). The author presents the ikhtilaf among Hanafi scholars on this condition. Three positions are mentioned: (1) It is absolutely required to know the source, as transmitted from Abu Yusuf and Zufar. (2) It is permissible only in the absence of a mujtahid, preferred by the 'Allamah (Ibn Abidin?). (3) It is absolutely permissible for anyone, even without knowing the source, because he is a mere narrator (naqil). The author then clarifies that the disagreement is not about simple narration but about derivation (takhrij). The core of the issue is that a mufti who engages in istinbat (deduction) must know the principles, while a mufti who only transmits rulings can do so without that knowledge. The author further explains the layers of mujtahids: the second class (Imam Abu Hanifa) are absolute mujtahids; the third class are mujtahid fi al-madhhab; and the fourth and fifth classes share in the requirement to know the sources when issuing fatwa. The story of Abu Yusuf following the people of Madinah and the examples from Shafi'i scholars support the permissibility of taqlid for a mujtahid in certain cases. The passage concludes that 'لا يحل لأحد أن يفتي بقولنا حتى يعلم' is specifically for the mujtahid fi al-madhhab who derives rulings, while others (pure narrators) suffice with transmission. Thus, the rule is refined: it applies to the higher levels of ijtihad, not to every mufti.

Key Terms
مجتهد في المذهب (mujtahid fi al-madhhab): A scholar who can derive rulings within the Hanafi madhhab by applying its principles to new cases, but does not have absolute ijtihad.
ناقل (naqil): A mufti who merely transmits established rulings from the madhhab without engaging in independent derivation.
تخريج (takhrij): The process of deriving a ruling from the principles of the madhhab for a case not explicitly stated in the texts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view in this passage, which type of mufti is required to know the source (dalil) of a ruling before giving fatwa?
A) Any mufti, regardless of his level
B) Only a mujtahid fi al-madhhab who derives rulings
C) Only a pure narrator (naqil)
D) Only the Imam (Abu Hanifa)

Key Takeaway
The condition 'know the source' is binding only for deriving rulings; narrators may simply transmit.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
