The Ruling on Issuing Fatwa Without Knowledge of Evidence
Explains the Hanafi rule on knowing the dalil before issuing fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the levels of muftis in the Hanafi school and apply the rule that only mujtahids in the madhhab must know the evidence before issuing fatwa.

Core Idea
Issuing fatwa without knowledge of evidence is only forbidden for those who derive rulings, not for mere transmitters.

This passage from a Hanafi work on rasm al-mufti addresses a critical question: who exactly is bound by the principle that a mufti must know the evidence before issuing a fatwa? The author uses examples from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani to show that even the great imams sometimes followed others when they didn't have direct knowledge, and he clarifies that the prohibition is directed at the mujtahid within the madhhab, while transmitters may rely on established positions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central prohibition
The text begins with 'لا يجوز الفتوى بقولنا حتى يعلم' – it is not permissible to give fatwa by our saying until he knows. This seems to require knowledge of evidence. Note the phrasing 'بقولنا' (by our saying) indicating the Hanafi school's positions.
The prohibition is absolute in its initial formulation.
2
Examine the supporting examples
The author cites Abu Yusuf's case: when asked about a mouse in bathwater, he said 'نقلد أهل المدينة' (we follow the people of Madina), showing he did not give his own ijtihad but followed a transmitted practice. Muhammad's statement indicates following a more knowledgeable person or his agreement in ijtihad. These examples soften the absolute prohibition.
The examples show that even the great imams sometimes acted without direct evidence.
3
Understand the analogy with Shafi'i scholars
Some Shafi'i imams said they were not blindly following al-Shafi'i but that their opinions agreed with his. The author argues the same applies to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad a fortiori, as they disagreed with Abu Hanifa in many branches yet remained within the madhhab.
This justifies that following the school does not require personal evidence in every case.
4
Distinguish between mufti levels
The author states the prohibition is interpreted as applying only to the mujtahid fi al-madhhab who performs istinbat and takhrij (levels 3-5). Others (mere transmitters) suffice with transmission. This is the key parsing of the rule.
The hierarchy: levels 3-5 must know evidence; level 1-2 (transmitters) need not.
5
Conclude the operative rule
The mufta bihi is that the prohibition is restricted to those engaging in derivation. Transmitters must follow the transmitted positions, including later scholars' tarjih, even if against the original imam's statement.
This ensures continuity of the madhhab while allowing flexibility.

لا يجوز الفتوى بقولنا حتى يعلم. ويؤيد الجواز مسألة أبي يوسف لما صلى الجمعة، فأخبروه بوجود فأرة في حوض الحمام، فقال: "نقلد أهل المدينة". وعن محمد: "يقلد أعلم منه، أو على أنه وافق اجتهادهم فيها اجتهاده. وحيث نقل مثل هذا عن بعض الأئمة الشافعية كالقفال والشيخ أبي علي، والقاضي حسين أنهم يقولون: لسنا مقلدين للشافعي، بل وافق رأينا رأيه"، يقال مثله في أصحاب أبي حنيفة مثل أبي يوسف ومحمد بالأولى. وقد خالفوه في كثير من الفروع، ومع هذا لم تخرج أقوالهم لم تخرج أقوالهم عن المذهب، كما مر تقريره فقد تحرر مما ذكرناه أن قول الإمام وأصحابه: "لا يحل لأحد أن يفتي بقولنا حتى يعلم من أين "قلنا؟ - محمول على فتوى المجتهد في المذهب بطريق الاستنباط والتخريج، كما علمت من كلام "التحرير" و"شرح البديع" - والظاهر اشتراك أهل الطبقة الثالثة والرابعة والخامسة في ذلك - وأن من عداهم يكتفي بالنقل، وأن علينا اتباع ما نقلوه لنا عنهم من استنباطاتهم الغير المنصوصة عن المتقدمين، ومن ترجيحاتهم، ولو كانت لغير قول الإمام، كما قررناه في صدر هذا البحث؛ لأنهم
It is not permissible to give fatwa by our statement until he knows. They have disagreed with him in many branches, yet their statements did not exit from the madhhab, as has been established. Commentary
This passage addresses a key rasm al-mufti rule: the mufti must know the legal evidence (dalil) before issuing a fatwa according to the Hanafi school. The author begins by stating the principle: it is not permitted to give fatwa with 'our sayings' (i.e., the Hanafi school's positions) until one knows the basis. He then provides supporting evidence: the case of Abu Yusuf who, when faced with a situation regarding a mouse in the bathwater, said 'we follow the people of Madina' – indicating that he was not giving a fatwa from his own ijtihad but was following the practice of the Medinese, which is a form of taqlid. From Muhammad al-Shaybani, it is reported that he said one follows a more knowledgeable person, or that his ijtihad agreed with theirs. The author then draws an analogy with some Shafi'i scholars who claimed they were not following al-Shafi'i but rather their opinions agreed with his; the same applies to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, though they differed from Abu Hanifa in many detailed matters, yet their views remained within the madhhab. The author concludes that the well-known prohibition (that one cannot give fatwa by our saying without knowing the evidence) is directed at the mujtahid in the madhhab who derives and extrapolates rulings. The third, fourth, and fifth levels of muftis are included in this category. Others who are not capable of ijtihad suffice with transmission. It is obligatory to follow what the later scholars have transmitted of the early scholars' deductions and preferences, even if those preferences are for a position other than Imam Abu Hanifa's original statement. This is because they (the later scholars) are the ones who have investigated and weighted the evidence. The passage emphasizes the hierarchy of muftis and the importance of understanding the source of rulings.

Key Terms
الفتوى (al-fatwa): The issuance of a legal ruling (ḥukm sharʿī) in answer to a question.
الاجتهاد (al-ijtihād): The effort to deduce a ruling from its textual evidence within the confines of the school.
يعلم (ya'lam): To know the source (dalīl) and reasoning behind a ruling, not merely to memorize the text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the correct understanding of the imam's statement 'It is not lawful for anyone to give fatwa by our saying until he knows from where we said it'?
A) It applies to all muftis, including mere transmitters.
B) It applies only to the mujtahid in the madhhab who engages in istinbat and takhrij.
C) It applies only to absolute mujtahids.
D) It is no longer applicable because we now have many books.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires knowledge of evidence only for those who engage in ijtihad within the madhhab; transmitters may rely on established rulings.

Conditions for a Mufti of Tarjih: The Case of Ibn al-Humam
Defense of Ibn al-Humam's status as a mufti of tarjih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the criteria for a Hanafi mufti to be considered from ahl al-tarjih and evaluate Ibn al-Humam's qualifications using the textual evidence from this passage.

Core Idea
A mufti of tarjih must know the sources, not just the rulings; Ibn al-Humam was explicitly endorsed.

This passage defends Ibn al-Humam's status as a mufti capable of tarjih (weighing evidence) and ijtihad within the Hanafi school. It refutes claims that he lacked the necessary qualifications by citing endorsements from peers and the principle that one must understand the reasoning (ma'khadh) behind rulings. You will learn the difference between mere memorization of branches and true capacity for legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main claim and counterclaim
Read the first paragraph: the author asserts Ibn al-Humam is from ahl al-tarjih, contrary to what was said in al-Bahr. Underline the explicit statement that he did not give tarjih arbitrarily.
Focus on 'خلافا لما قاله في البحر' – this sets up the dispute.
2
Analyze the evidence from al-Bahr
Find where al-Bahr is quoted: 'إنه أهل للنظر في الدليل'. Note that this qualifies Ibn al-Humam for tarjih, but with the condition that he does not leave the madhhab.
The phrase 'ما لم يخرج عن المذهب' is crucial – his tarjih is valid only within the madhhab.
3
Examine additional endorsements
Locate the statements from Burhan al-Anbasi, Ali al-Maqdisi, and Allamah Qasim. These explicitly call Ibn al-Humam a mujtahid or refer to his expertise.
Ali al-Maqdisi uses 'بلغ رتبة الاجتهاد' – a strong endorsement.
4
Understand the condition of knowing the sources
The author quotes Abu Hanifa's statement that no one may give fatwa without knowing the 'ma'khadh'. This is the core criterion for a mufti of tarjih.
Also note Qasim's dissatisfaction with mere taqlid of pages – he studied the sources.
5
Evaluate the counter-argument and conclusion
The passage critiques al-Bayri's praise of the author of al-Bahr, arguing that knowing many branches does not imply ijtihad. The final takeaway: Ibn al-Humam is indeed from ahl al-tarjih because he met the condition of examining evidence.
Reflect: the author of al-Bahr himself admitted Ibn al-Humam's qualification, so the dispute is partially resolved.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شرح عقود رسم المفتي
ابن الهمام من أهل الترجيح
لم يرجحوا ما رجحوه جزافاً، وإنما رجحوا بعد اطلاعهم على المأخذ، كما شهدت مصنفاتهم بذلك خلافا لما قاله في "البحر".
ابن الهمام من أهل الترجيح]
تنبيه كلام البحر" صريح في أن المحقق ابن الهمام من أهل الترجيح، حيث قال عنه: "إنه أهل للنظر في الدليل وحينئذ فلنا اتباعه فيما يحققه ويرجحه من الروايات أو الأقوال، ما لم يخرج عن المذهب؛ فإنه له اختيارات خالف فيها المذهب فلا يتابع عليها كما قاله تلميذه العلامة قاسم وكيف لا يكون أهلا لذلك، وقد قال فيه بعض أقرانه وهو البرهان الأنباسي : لو طلبت حجج الدين ما كان في بلدنا من يقوم بها غيره".
قلت: بل قد صرح العلامة المحقق شيخ الإسلام علي المقدسي في شرحه على نظم "الكنز" في باب نكاح الرقيق: "بأن ابن الهمام بلغ رتبة الاجتهاد". وكذلك نفس العلامة قاسم من أهل تلك الكتيبة؛ فإنه قال في أول رسالته المسماة رفع الاشتباه عن مسألة المياه": لما منع علماؤنا عنهم - من كان له أهلية النظر من محض تقليدهم، على ما رواه الشيخ الإمام العالم العلامة أبو إسحاق إبراهيم بن يوسف، قال: حدثنا أبو يوسف عن أبي حنيفة وله أنه قال: "لا يحل لأحد أن يفتي بقولنا ما لم يعرف من أين "قلناه" تتبعت مآخذهم، وحصلت منها بحمد الله تعالى- على الكثير ، و لم أقنع بتقليد ما في صحف كثير من المصنفين إلخ.
وقال في رسالة أخرى وإني - ولله الحمد - لأقول كما قال الطحاوي لابن حربوية: "لا يقلد إلا عصبي أو غبي". ويؤخذ من قول صاحب البحر" : يجب علينا الإفتاء بقول الإمام إلخ، أنه نفسه ليس من أهل النظر في الدليل، فإذا صحح قولا مخالفا لتصحيح غيره لا يعتبر، فضلا عن الاستنباط والتخريج على القواعد، خلافا لما ذكره البيري عند قول صاحب "البحر" في كتابه "الأشباه " : النوع الأول معرفة القواعد التي ترد إليها، وفرعوا الأحكام عليها، وهي أصول الفقه في الحقيقة وبها يرتقي الفقيه إلى درجة الاجتهاد، ولو في الفتوى، وأكثر فروعه ظفرت به. إلخ. فقال البيري بعد أن عرف المجتهد في المذهب بما قدمناه عنه: "وفي هذا إشارة إلى أن المؤلف قد بلغ هذه المرتبة في الفتوى وزيادة، وهو في الحقيقة قد من الله تعالى عليه بالاطلاع على خبايا الزوايا، وكان من جملة الحفاظ المزيدين." إذ لا يخفى أن ظفره بأكثر فروع هذا النوع لا يلزم منه أن يكون له أهلية النظر في الأدلة التي دل كلامه في "البحر" على أنها لم تحصل له وعلى أنها شرط للاجتهاد في المذهب، فتأمل.
Commentary on 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti
Ibn al-Humam is among the people of tarjih (preponderance).
They did not give preponderance arbitrarily, but only after being informed of the legal bases, as their works testify, contrary to what was said in al-Bahr.
[Ibn al-Humam is among the people of tarjih]
A note: The statement of al-Bahr is explicit that the muhaqqiq Ibn al-Humam is among the people of tarjih, where he said about him: 'He is qualified to examine evidence, and therefore we may follow him in what he verifies and gives preponderance among narrations or opinions, as long as he does not depart from the madhhab; for he has choices in which he opposed the madhhab, so he is not followed in that, as his student Allamah Qasim said. And how could he not be qualified for that, when one of his peers, Burhan al-Anbasi, said about him: 'If you sought the proofs of the religion, there was no one in our town who could fulfill that other than him.'
I say: Rather, the Allamah, the muhaqqiq, Shaykh al-Islam Ali al-Maqdisi explicitly stated in his commentary on the versification of al-Kanz, in the chapter on marriage of slaves, 'that Ibn al-Humam reached the rank of ijtihad.' Likewise, Allamah Qasim himself is among the people of that cohort; for he said at the beginning of his treatise titled 'Raf' al-Ishtibah 'an Mas'alat al-Miyah': 'Since our scholars prohibited from pure taqlid anyone who has the capacity for independent reasoning, as narrated by Shaykh Imam Allamah Abu Ishaq Ibrahim ibn Yusuf, who said: Abu Yusuf narrated to us from Abu Hanifa that he said: 'It is not permissible for anyone to give fatwa according to our statement unless he knows from where we said it.' I have studied their sources and obtained from them, thanks to Allah Almighty, much, and I was not satisfied with taqlid of what is in the pages of many authors, etc.'
And he said in another treatise: 'And I - praise be to Allah - say as al-Tahawi said to Ibn Harbawayh: 'Only a fanatic or a fool practices taqlid.' And it is understood from the statement of the author of al-Bahr: 'We must give fatwa according to the statement of the Imam, etc.' that he himself is not among the people of examining evidence. So if he declares a statement correct contrary to the correction of others, it is not considered, let alone istinbat (derivation) and takhrij (extrapolation) based on rules, contrary to what al-Bayri mentioned regarding the statement of the author of al-Bahr in his book al-Ashbah: 'The first type: knowledge of the rules to which [branches] are referred, and they derived rulings from them, and they are truly the principles of fiqh, and through them the faqih rises to the degree of ijtihad, even if only in fatwa, and I have grasped most of its branches...' So al-Bayri said after defining the mujtahid in the madhhab as we have previously mentioned: 'And in this there is an indication that the author has reached this rank in fatwa and more, and in truth, Allah has bestowed upon him insight into hidden corners, and he was among the preservers and the increased.' It is not hidden that his grasping most of the branches of this type does not necessarily imply that he has the capacity to examine the evidences which his statement in al-Bahr indicates he did not attain, and which is a condition for ijtihad in the madhhab. So reflect.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage is an extended discussion on the qualifications of a mufti, specifically Ibn al-Humam. The author argues that Ibn al-Humam is indeed from ahl al-tarjih (those capable of weighing evidences) because he based his tarjih on knowledge of the legal bases (ma'khadh). This refutes a claim made in al-Bahr. The author then cites al-Bahr's own statement that Ibn al-Humam is qualified to examine evidence, so his tarjih can be followed as long as it does not contradict the madhhab. He further cites Ali al-Maqdisi affirming that Ibn al-Humam reached the rank of ijtihad. The passage also includes a report from Abu Hanifa that a mufti must know the reasoning behind the rulings, not merely imitate. The author concludes by critiquing the author of al-Bahr for not being among ahl al-nazar (independent reasoning), despite al-Bayri's praise. The lesson emphasizes that true capacity for tarjih and ijtihad requires understanding the sources, not just memorizing branches.

Key Terms
أهل الترجيح (ahl al-tarjih): Those qualified to weigh conflicting evidences and give preponderance to one opinion over another.
مأخذ (ma'khadh): The source or basis of a ruling, such as a specific hadith or qiyas.
اجتهاد (ijtihad): The ability to derive rulings directly from the primary sources (Qur'an, Sunnah, ijma', qiyas). Reaching this rank allows a person to potentially oppose the madhhab under certain conditions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One must memorize the entire Qur'an.
B) One must know the source (ma'khadh) from which the ruling is derived.
C) One must be a mujtahid mutlaq.
D) One must have written a commentary on al-Hidayah.

Key Takeaway
Ibn al-Humam is from ahl al-tarjih because he had the capacity to examine evidence; mere knowledge of branches does not suffice.

The Hierarchy of Fatwa When No Riwaya Exists
Hierarchy for fatwa when no direct transmission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct the correct hierarchy of sources for issuing a fatwa when no riwaya from Imam Abu Hanifa is available, and identify the circumstances under which the mufti may use independent ijtihad.

Core Idea
When no riwaya exists: Abu Yusuf → Muhammad → Zufar/Hasan → later scholars' consensus → majority of later seniors → cautious ijtihad.

This lesson presents the foundational hierarchy for Hanafi fatwa-giving when no direct transmission (riwaya) from Imam Abu Hanifa exists. The passage, drawn from al-Hawi al-Qudsi and versified in an urjuza, outlines a strict ladder of authority: first the explicit statements of the senior companions (Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, Zufar, al-Hasan), then the consensus of later scholars, their majority opinion, and only as a final resort, the mufti's own ijtihad. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for any mufti to ensure rulings remain grounded in the school's transmitted heritage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six levels of the hierarchy
List the levels from highest priority to lowest: (1) riwaya from Abu Hanifa, (2) zahir qawl of Abu Yusuf, (3) zahir qawl of Muhammad, (4) zahir qawl of Zufar and al-Hasan and other senior companions, (5) consensus of the later scholars (muta'akhkhirun), (6) majority opinion among the well-known later seniors (e.g., Abu Hafs, Abu Ja'far, Abu al-Layth, al-Tahawi), and finally (7) the mufti's cautious personal ijtihad when no textual answer exists at all.
Notice the transition from individual companion opinions to collective later scholar authority.
2
Understand the order of precedence
Each level is consulted only if the previous level provides no clear answer. The mufti must not skip levels or jump to ijtihad prematurely.
The phrase 'thumma' (then) in the text indicates strict sequencing.
3
Recognize the role of 'zahir al-qawl'
Zahir al-qawl refers to the apparent, explicit statement of a mujtahid, as opposed to inferred or ambiguous positions. Only such explicit statements are considered authoritative in the hierarchy.
This excludes rulings derived by qiyas or istihsan from the early imams unless explicitly voiced.
4
Apply the condition for independent ijtihad
The mufti may only resort to his own ijtihad if there is absolutely no textual answer (jawab) from any of the preceding levels. Even then, he must do so with extreme caution, fear of Allah, and after deep reflection.
The passage warns harshly against casual fatwa-giving: 'None dares except an ignorant wretch.'
5
Examine the mufti's required attitude
The mufti must approach fatwa with seriousness (jidd), ijtihad, and fear of Allah (khashya). The text emphasizes his responsibility before Allah on the Day of Return.
This attitude is part of the adab al-mufti and reinforces the gravity of issuing rulings without authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
طريق الإفتاء عند عدم الرواية
ثم إذا لم توجد الروايه عن واختلف الذين قد تأخروا يرجح الذي عليه الأكثر مثلُ الطحاوي وأبي حفص الكبير وأبوَي جعفر والليث الشهير وحيث لم توجد لهؤلاء مقالة واحتيج للإفتاء
فلينظر المفتي بجد واجتهاد وليخش بطش ربِّه يوم المعاد فليس يجسر على الأحكام سوى شقي خاسر المرام
طريق الإفتاء عند عدم الرواية ]
قال في آخر الحاوي القدسي : ومتى لم يوجد في المسألة عن أبي حنيفة رواية، يؤخذ بظاهر قول أبي يوسف ثم بظاهر قول محمد، ثم بظاهر قول زفر والحسن ،وغيرهم الأكبر فالأكبر هكذا إلى آخر من كان من كبار الأصحاب.
وإذا لم يوجد في الحادثة عن واحد منهم جواب ظاهر، وتكلم فيه المشايخ المتأخرون قولا واحدا يؤخذ به فإن اختلفوا يؤخذ بقول الأكثرين مما اعتمد عليه الكبار المعروفون كأبي حفص وأبي جعفر
وأبي الليث والطحاوي وغيرهم، فيعتمد عليه.
وإن لم يوجد منهم جواب البتة نصا ينظر المفتي فيها نظر تأمل وتدبر واجتهاد؛ ليجد فيها ما يقرب إلى الخروج عن العهدة، ولا يتكلم فيها جُزافاً؛ لمنصبه وحرمته وليخش الله تعالى ويراقبه؛ فإنه أمر عظيم
لا يتجاسر عليه إلا كل جاهل شقي".
The method of fatwa when there is no riwaya. Then when there is no riwaya from him, and the later scholars differed, the one which the majority such as al-Tahawi, Abu Hafs al-Kabir, Abu Ja'far, and al-Layth al-Shahir (may be preferred). And when there is no statement from these and there is need for fatwa, then the mufti should look with seriousness and ijtihad, and fear the might of his Lord on the Day of Return. None dares to give rulings except a wretched loser. [The method of fatwa when there is no riwaya] He said at the end of al-Hawi al-Qudsi: 'Whenever there is no narration from Abu Hanifa on a matter, the apparent saying of Abu Yusuf is taken, then the apparent saying of Muhammad, then the apparent saying of Zufar and al-Hasan, and so on from the greater to the greater, until the last of the senior companions. And if there is no apparent answer from any of them, and the later scholars have spoken with a single opinion, it is taken. If they differ, the saying of the majority among those relied upon by the known seniors such as Abu Hafs, Abu Ja'far, Abu al-Layth, al-Tahawi, and others is taken. And if there is absolutely no textual answer from them, the mufti should look into it with reflection, deliberation, and ijtihad to find what brings him closer to discharge of responsibility, and not speak without basis, due to his position and sanctity. Let him fear Allah and be watchful; for it is a grave matter that none dares except every ignorant wretch.'
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage presents a hierarchical method for issuing fatwas when no direct transmission (riwaya) from Imam Abu Hanifa exists. It is structured as a poem (urjuza) followed by a commentary from al-Hawi al-Qudsi. The hierarchy begins with the opinions of Abu Yusuf, then Muhammad al-Shaybani, then Zufar and al-Hasan ibn Ziyad (the 'senior companions'). If none of these have a clear answer, the consensus of the later scholars (mutakkhirin) is taken; if they differ, the majority opinion among the well-known later authorities (Abu Hafs, Abu Ja'far, Abu al-Layth, al-Tahawi) is followed. If no textual answer exists at all, the mufti must exert personal ijtihad with fear of Allah. This rule underscores the importance of adhering to the transmitted opinions of the Hanafi school before resorting to independent reasoning, and it warns against reckless fatwa-giving. The mufti must be conscious of his grave responsibility.

Key Terms
الرواية (al-riwaya): A transmitted narration from Imam Abu Hanifa or other early Imams containing a legal ruling.
ظاهر القول (zahir al-qawl): The apparent or explicit statement of a mujtahid, as opposed to an inferred or ambiguous one.
المشايخ المتأخرون (al-mashayikh al-muta'akhkhirun): Later Hanafi scholars, typically those after the 5th century AH, who compiled and commented on the school's rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the first source to consult if there is no riwaya from Abu Hanifa on a matter?
A) The opinion of the later scholars (muta'akhkhirun)
B) The opinion of Abu Yusuf
C) The mufti's own ijtihad
D) The opinion of the majority of the mujtahidun

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi fatwa hierarchy prioritizes transmitted opinions over independent reasoning, ensuring consistency within the school.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

The Mufti Must Transmit Naql, Not Derive from Qawaid Alone
Ruling on prohibition of issuing fatwa from qawaid without direct textual transmission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the correct method for issuing a fatwa in the Hanafi school by distinguishing between naql (transmission) and qawaid (maxims) and applying the rule of tawaqquf (pausing) when no explicit text is found.

Core Idea
A mufti must transmit transmitted rulings, not derive from general maxims alone — qawaid are akthari, not kulli.

This passage addresses a critical principle in Hanafi ifta: the mufti's primary duty is to transmit existing rulings (naql/hikaya) from the madhhab's authoritative texts, not to derive new rulings from general qawaid (legal maxims). The author warns that relying on qawaid alone is impermissible because qawaid are akthari (majority-based) not kulli (universal), and subtle differences between cases may escape the mufti's understanding. Instead, the mufti must pause or consult another scholar if no direct text is found.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Read the passage and determine what is forbidden (issuing fatwa from qawaid alone) and what is required (transmission of naql via hikaya).
Focus on the phrases 'لا يحل الإفتاء من القواعد' and 'على المفتي حكاية النقل'.
2
Understand the reasoning (ta'lil)
Analyze why qawaid alone are insufficient: they are akthari (apply to most cases) but not kulli (universal), so exceptions exist. Also, there may be subtle distinctions (furq) between similar cases that the mufti might miss.
The text mentions 'فإنه لا يأمن أن يكون بين حادثة وما وجده فرق، لا يصل إليه فهمه'.
3
Note the authority cited
Identify the scholars and texts quoted: Ibn Nujaym (al-Fawa'id al-Zayniyya), al-Khaniyya, al-Zahiriyya. This shows the rule is firmly established in the madhhab.
The passage uses 'قال العلامة ابن نجيم' and references to 'الخانية' and 'الظهيرية'.
4
Recognize the exception
Find the exception for customary matters ('urfiyya) that do not contradict Shari'ah. In such cases, the mufti may give fatwa based on custom directly.
The text says 'نعم! قد توجد حوادث عرفية غير مخالفة للنصوص الشرعية، فيفتي المفتي بها'.
5
Apply the rule
Consider what the mufti must do when no explicit text is found: either pause (tawaqquf) or ask a more knowledgeable scholar, even if in another town.
The command is 'فعلى من لم يجد نقلا صريحا أن يتوقف في الجواب، أو يسأل من هو منه'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإفتاء بالقواعد في بعض الحوادث
شرح عقود رسم المفتي والغالب أن عدم وجدانه النص لقلة اطلاعه، أو عدم معرفته بموضع المسألة المذكورة فيه؛ إذ قلّ ما تقع حادثة إلا ولها ذكر في كتب المذهب، إما بعينها أو بذكر قاعدة كلية تشملها.
ولا يكتفى بوجود نظيرها مما يقاربها؛ فإنه لا يأمن أن يكون بين حادثة وما وجده فرق، لا يصل إليه فهمه فكم من مسألة فرّقوا بينها وبين نظيرتها، حتى ألفوا كتب الفروق لذلك، ولو وكل الأمر إلى أفهامنا لم ندرك الفرق بينهما، بل قال العلامة ابن نجيم في "الفوائد الزينية": "لا يحل الإفتاء من القواعد والضوابط وإنما على المفتي حكاية النقل كما صرحوا به. وقال أيضا: "إن المقرر في الأربعة المذاهب الصريح أن قواعد الفقه أكثرية لا كلية". نقله البيري.
أعلم
فعلى من لم يجد نقلا صريحا أن يتوقف في الجواب، أو يسأل من هو منه ولو في بلدة أخرى، كما يعلم مما نقلناه عن "الخانية". وفي "الظهيرية" : " وإن لم يكن من أهل الاجتهاد لا يحل له أن يفتي إلا بطريق الحكاية، فيحكي ما يحفظ من أقوال الفقهاء". نعم! قد توجد حوادث عرفية غير مخالفة للنصوص الشرعية، فيفتي المفتي بها كما سنذكره آخر المنظومة.
Issuing fatwa by [use of] qawaid in some incidents. Commentary on 'Uquud Rasm al-Mufti: And most often, his not finding the text is due to lack of his knowledge, or his ignorance of the location of the mentioned issue in it; for rarely does an incident occur except that it has mention in the books of the madhhab, either explicitly or by mention of a universal qa'ida that encompasses it. And one is not satisfied with the existence of its similar from what is close to it; for he is not safe from there being between the incident and what he found a difference that his understanding cannot reach. How many issues have they distinguished between them and their parallels, such that they authored books of furuq for that. Had the matter been entrusted to our understandings, we would not perceive the difference between them. Rather, Allamah Ibn Nujaym said in al-Fawa'id al-Zayniyya: 'It is not permissible to issue fatwa from the qawaid and dawabit; rather it is upon the mufti to transmit the narration, as they have explicitly stated.' And he also said: 'Indeed, the established [position] in the four schools is that the qawaid of fiqh are akthari (majority) not kulli (universal).' Narrated by al-Bayri. Know: So for one who does not find an explicit text, he should pause in answering, or ask one who is knowledgeable even if in another town, as is known from what we have transmitted from al-Khaniyya. And in al-Zahiriyya: 'And if he is not from the people of ijtihad, it is not permissible for him to give fatwa except by way of transmission, so he transmits what he memorizes of the statements of the jurists.' Yes! There may occur customary incidents that do not contradict the textual proofs; then the mufti gives fatwa on them, as we will mention at the end of the poem.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the methodology of fatwa. It establishes that a mufti must primarily rely on direct textual transmission (naql) and cannot derive rulings solely from general qawaid (legal maxims). The author explains that the apparent reason for a mufti not finding a direct text is either his limited knowledge or lack of awareness of where the issue is discussed. He emphasizes that it is rare for a new incident to have no mention in the madhhab books — either explicitly or by a universal qa'ida that includes it. However, one cannot be satisfied with a similar case (nazir) because there may be subtle differences (furq) that the mufti's understanding cannot grasp. Scholars have authored separate works on these distinctions (furuq). Ibn Nujaym is quoted stating that it is haram to give fatwa from qawaid alone; the mufti must transmit (hikaya) the transmitted ruling. He also states that qawaid are akthari (apply to most cases) not kulli (universal), so they are not absolute. The mufti who cannot find a text must pause (tawaqquf) or ask another scholar, even if in another city. A non-mujtahid mufti can only transmit what he memorizes from the jurists. The exception is customary matters (umur 'urfiyya) that don’t contradict Shari'ah, where the mufti may rely on custom directly.

Key Terms
قاعدة (qa'ida): A general legal maxim that applies to most cases but not all.
نقل (naql): A direct textual transmission of a ruling from the madhhab's foundational texts.
حكاية (hikaya): The act of the mufti transmitting the exact wording of a ruling from earlier jurists, without personal derivation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what should a mufti do if he cannot find an explicit textual ruling (naql sarih) for a new incident?
A) Derive a ruling using qiyas (analogy) based on a similar case.
B) Apply the most appropriate qa'ida (legal maxim) directly.
C) Pause in answering or ask another scholar, even in another town.
D) Use istihsan (juristic preference) to arrive at a ruling.

Key Takeaway
The mufti must rely on direct textual transmission (naql) and cannot derive fatwa from general qawaid alone; qawaid are akthari (majority) not kulli (universal).

Tarjih Qawaid: Preferring Opinions in Fatwa (Poetic Rules)
Poetic summary of tarjih rules for determining which madhhab opinion to give fatwa on.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi tarjih rules for preferring an opinion in fatwa and apply the rule regarding 'ibadat to identify when Abu Hanifa's opinion is preferred.

Core Idea
Fatwa in 'ibadat follows Abu Hanifa's opinion unless an authentic narration from him takes another view.

This lesson presents a set of poetic rules (qawaid) from the Hanafi tradition that guide a mufti in choosing between differing opinions within the madhhab. These rules are condensed into verses for easy memorization. We will examine the first and most comprehensive rule regarding acts of worship, which establishes a default preference for Imam Abu Hanifa's view, and then survey the other rules that cover judiciary, inheritance, istihsan, and textual hierarchy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first rule and its scope
The first rule states that in all chapters of 'ibadat (worship), the opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa is given preference absolutely. Understand that this is a general rule covering acts like prayer, fasting, zakat, and hajj.
This rule is a dabt (sub-maxim) that governs fatwa practice in the Hanafi school.
2
Note the exception to the first rule
The rule includes an exception: 'as long as no authentic narration from him exists by which another opinion was taken.' This means if Abu Hanifa himself transmitted a different view or later scholars reliably attributed a different view to him, then that other view takes precedence.
Example: tayammum for one who throws away dates (a case where a different narration from Abu Hanifa exists).
3
List the remaining rules from the poem
The poem continues with rules for judiciary (Abu Yusuf preferred), inheritance for dhawi al-arham (Muhammad preferred), preference of istihsan over qiyas, adherence to apparent meaning (zahir) of transmitted rulings, preference for rulings that negate kufr, treatment of retracted statements as abrogated, and hierarchy of texts (mutun > shuruh > fatawa).
These rules are all sughra (minor) qawaid that guide the mufti in specific contexts.
4
Understand the hierarchy of textual sources
The last rule establishes a hierarchy: the primary texts (mutun) are preferred over commentaries (shuruh), and commentaries over old fatawa. However, if a corrected wording exists in a later source, the more explicit statement is preferred.
This hierarchy ensures that the mufti relies on the most authoritative and clear transmission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شرح عقود رسم المفتي وههنا ضوابط محرره
الفتوى في العبادات
غدت لدى أهل النهى مقرّره
في كل أبواب العبادات رُجح قولُ الإمام مطلقا ما لم تصح عنه رواية بها الغير أخذ مثل تيمم لمن تمرا نَبَذ وكل فرع بالقضا تعلّقا قول أبي يوسف فيه يُنتقى
وفي مسائل ذوي الأرحام قد أفتوا
بما
يقوله
محمد
ورجحوا استحسانهم على القياس إلا مسائل وما فيها التباس وظاهر المروي ليس يُعدل عنه إلى خلافه إذ يُنقل لا ينبغي العدول عن درايه إذا أتى بوفقها روايه وكل قول جاء ينفي الكفرا عن مسلم ولو ضعيفا أحرى وكل ما رجع عنه المجتهد صار كمنسوخ فغيره اعتمد وكل قول في المتون أثبتا فذاك ترجيح له ضمنا أتى فرجحت على الشروح والشروح على الفتاوى القدم من ذات رُجوح ما لم يكن سواه لفظا صُححا فالأرجح الذي به قد صُرّحا قواعد الترجيح من الأقوال]
جمعت في هذه الأبيات قواعد ذكروها مفرقة في الكتب، وجعلوها علامة على المرجح من الأقوال.
الفتوى في العبادات]
الأولى: ما في "شرح المنية للبرهان إبراهيم الحلبي من فصل التيمم حيث قال: فلله در الإمام الأعظم ما أدق نظره وما أسد فكره وإلا ما جعل العلماء الفتوى على قوله في العبادات مطلقا، وهو الواقع بالاستقراء
Commentary on 'Uquud Rasm al-Mufti: And here are verified principles: Fatwa in acts of worship has become established among people of understanding. In all chapters of worship, the statement of the Imam (Abu Hanifa) is given preference absolutely, as long as there is no authentic narration from him by which another (opinion) was taken, such as tayammum for one who throws away dates. And every branch related to judiciary, the statement of Abu Yusuf in it is chosen. And in the matters of dhawu al-arham, they gave fatwa according to what Muhammad says. And they gave preference to their istihsan over qiyas, except for issues and what has ambiguity therein. And the apparent of what is narrated should not be turned away from to its contrary, since it is transmitted; it is not appropriate to turn away from a reliable transmission when a narration consistent with it comes. And every statement that negates disbelief from a Muslim, even if weak, is more appropriate. And every statement that the mujtahid retracted from becomes like abrogated, so another is relied upon. And every statement that is established in the texts (mutun) contains an implicit preference for it. So the texts are preferred over the commentaries, and the commentaries over the old fatawa, from that which has preference, as long as there is not another wording that is corrected. So the most preponderant is that which has been explicitly stated. 'Rules of preference from the statements': In these verses are collected rules that they mentioned scattered in the books, and they made them a sign for the preponderant among statements. 'Fatwa in acts of worship': The first: What is in Sharh al-Munya by Burhan Ibrahim al-Halabi from the chapter of tayammum where he said: 'How excellent is the Imam al-A'zam, how precise his view and how correct his thought! Otherwise, the scholars would not have made the fatwa on his statement in worship absolutely, and that is the reality by induction.'
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage presents a set of rules (qawaid) for tarjih (preference) among different opinions within the Hanafi madhhab, composed in poetic form for easy memorization. The verses are from the matn of 'Uquud Rasm al-Mufti, and the commentary explains them. The rules are: (1) In acts of worship ('ibadat), the opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa is absolutely preferred, unless a sahih narration from him shows that another view was adopted (like the case of tayammum for dates). (2) In matters related to judiciary (qada'), the opinion of Imam Abu Yusuf is chosen. (3) In issues of dhawu al-arham (inheritance of distant relatives by blood), the opinion of Imam Muhammad is given fatwa upon. (4) Their istihsan (juristic preference) is preferred over qiyas, except where confusion exists. (5) The apparent meaning of a transmitted ruling should not be abandoned for a contrary meaning if the transmission is reliable and consistent narrations support it. (6) Any statement that removes disbelief from a Muslim is given precedence, even if weak. (7) A statement that the mujtahid retracted is like abrogated, and another is relied upon. (8) Statements established in the primary texts (mutun) have implicit preference over commentaries, and commentaries over old fatawa, unless a corrected wording exists. The commentary then begins explaining the first rule, quoting Sharh al-Munya that the fuqaha' have made fatwa on Abu Hanifa's view in 'ibadat absolutely, as a matter of inductive reality.

Key Terms
ترجيح (tarjih): The process of determining which opinion among multiple valid ones is most preponderant and should be given fatwa upon.
قول الإمام (qawl al-Imam): The opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa, particularly in acts of worship.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas in certain cases.
ظاهر المروي (zahir al-marwi): The apparent meaning of a transmitted ruling from the imams.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the poetic rules, which imam's opinion is given preference in matters related to judiciary (qada')?
A) Imam Abu Hanifa
B) Imam Abu Yusuf
C) Imam Muhammad
D) All three equally

Key Takeaway
The first rule of tarjih in 'ibadat is to follow Abu Hanifa's opinion unless an authentic narration from him indicates otherwise, and each subject area has its own preferred imam or principle, ensuring consistency in fatwa.

Fatwa in 'Ibadat: Preference for Abu Hanifa's Qawl
Establishes the rule for preferring Abu Hanifa's qawl in 'ibadat unless a riwaya supports the other.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule for preferring Abu Hanifa's qawl in 'ibadat and apply it to examples of used water and tayammum with nabidh.

Core Idea
In 'ibadat, fatwa follows Abu Hanifa's qawl unless a supporting riwaya from him favors another view.

This lesson introduces a foundational rule for muftis navigating 'ibadat matters within the Hanafi madhhab. The rule, derived from the practice of later scholars, prioritizes the qawl of Imam Abu Hanifa in all acts of worship unless a specific transmission (riwaya) from the Imam himself supports the opposing view. We will unpack the rule with two illustrative examples from the chapter of tayammum and water purity.

Guided Path
1
State the rule verbatim
Read the Arabic qawida and its translation. Note the two parts: the general preference for Abu Hanifa's qawl and the conditional exception.
The exception is introduced by 'ما لم تصح عنه رواية بها الغير أخذ'.
2
Understand the justification
The rule is based on induction (istiqra') and the consensus of later scholars. Recognize that this is an inductive, not a transmitted, proof.
The author cites 'شرح المنية' to emphasize the precision of Abu Hanifa's thought.
3
Examine the first example: used water
Abu Hanifa says used water is tahir but not mutahhir. If a sahih riwaya from Abu Hanifa says it is mutahhir (matching the Sahibayn), fatwa may follow that riwaya. Note how the exception applies.
4
Examine the second example: tayammum with nabidh
Abu Hanifa permits tayammum when only date nabidh is available for wudu. Since no riwaya contradicts, fatwa follows his qawl absolutely.
The commentator praises Abu Hanifa's precise reasoning.
5
Recognize the scope and application
This rule applies to all chapters of 'ibadat (taharah, salah, zakah, sawm, hajj, etc.). It does not apply to mu'amalat or other areas.
A mufti must first confirm whether a riwaya exists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في كل أبواب العبادات رجح قول الإمام مطلقا ما لم تصح عنه رواية بها الغير أخذ مثل تيمم لمن تمرا نبذ
الأولى: ما في "شرح المنية للبرهان إبراهيم الحلبي من فصل التيمم حيث قال: فلله در الإمام الأعظم ما أدق نظره وما أسد فكره وإلا ما جعل العلماء الفتوى على قوله في العبادات مطلقا، وهو الواقع بالاستقراء
ما لم يكن عنه رواية كقول المخالف، كما في طهارة الماء المستعمل
والتيمم فقط عند عدم غير نبيذ التمر".
In all chapters of acts of worship, the statement of the Imam (Abu Hanifa) is preferred absolutely, unless a transmission from him is authenticated by which the other (view) is taken, like tayammum for one who has dates [but no water] except date nabidh. The first [rule]: What is in "Sharh al-Munya" by Burhan Ibrahim al-Halabi from the section on tayammum where he said: 'By Allah, the greatest Imam, how precise his view and how sound his thought! Otherwise, the scholars would not have made the fatwa on his statement in acts of worship absolutely, and that is the reality by induction, unless there is a transmission from him like the saying of the opponent, as in the purity of used water, and tayammum only when there is no other [water] except date nabidh.'
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage presents the first rule of tarjih: in all matters of 'ibadat (acts of worship), the preferred qawl for fatwa is that of Imam Abu Hanifa, without exception, unless there is a riwaya (transmission) from the Imam himself that supports the opposing view (e.g., the view of the Sahibayn or others). The commentator illustrates this with two examples from Sharh al-Munya: (1) the ruling on water that has been used for wudu (musta'mal) – Abu Hanifa considers it tahir but not mutahhir, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad consider it mutahhir; however, if a riwaya from Abu Hanifa exists that agrees with them, fatwa may follow that. (2) The permissibility of tayammum when only date nabidh (a type of non-water liquid) is available – Abu Hanifa allows tayammum in such a case, and fatwa is on his qawl. The rule is established by induction (istiqra').

Key Terms
قول الإمام (qawl al-imam): The legal opinion of Abu Hanifa, the founder of the Hanafi school.
رواية (riwaya): A transmission of a legal opinion attributed to Abu Hanifa, either directly or through his students.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) When the Sahibayn agree against him.
B) When a sahih riwaya from him supports the opposing view.
C) When the matter is related to qada'.
D) When the case involves dhawi al-arham.

Key Takeaway
In 'ibadat, fatwa follows Abu Hanifa's qawl unless a supporting riwaya from him indicates otherwise.

Fatwa in Qada': The Rule of Preferring Abu Yusuf's Qawl
Specifies that in judicial matters, fatwa is on Abu Yusuf's qawl due to his experience.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qawida that in judicial matters (qada'), fatwa is given on Abu Yusuf's qawl, and identify its scope and exceptions.

Core Idea
In judicial rulings, Abu Yusuf's practical experience trumps theoretical strength.

This lesson examines a key rule in Hanafi fatwa methodology: when a matter concerns qada' (judicial procedure), the mufti prioritizes Abu Yusuf's position over even Abu Hanifa's. This is not arbitrary but based on his unparalleled experience in court. We will explore the reasoning, scope, and application through the text from al-Bahr, al-Quniya, and al-Bazzaziyya.

Guided Path
1
State the qawida
Identify the rule in Arabic and its plain English meaning. The qawida is: 'وكل فرع بالقضا تعلقا قول أبي يوسف فيه ينتقى' – 'And every branch related to qada', the statement of Abu Yusuf in it is selected.'
2
Identify the ʿilla (reason)
Why is Abu Yusuf preferred? The text states 'لزيادة تجربته' (due to his increased experience). His judicial practice gave him deeper insight into court procedures and outcomes.
Compare with the anecdote about Abu Hanifa changing his view on hajj after experiencing it.
3
Determine the scope
Does this apply to all fiqh? No, only to qada' and its accessories. The commentator explicitly includes shahadat (testimonies) as accessories. Other areas follow different tarjih rules (e.g., 'ibadat prefer Abu Hanifa).
4
Apply to a furuʿ
Use the example of the silent defendant. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, the defendant is considered a denier; according to Abu Yusuf, he is imprisoned until he answers. Fatwa follows Abu Yusuf.
This is a practical consequence for judges and muftis.
5
Note the tarjih mechanism
Understand that this is a settled rule in later Hanafi fatwa. The sources (al-Quniya, al-Bazzaziyya, al-Bahr) all confirm it, and Imam al-Sarakhsi endorses it.
This rule is part of Rasm al-Mufti – the mufti's methodology for preferring opinions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكل فرع بالقضا تعلقا قول أبي يوسف فيه ينتقى
الثانية: ما في "البحر" قبيل فصل الحبس، قال: وفي "القنية" من باب المفتي: الفتوى على قول أبي يوسف فيما يتعلق بالقضاء؛ لزيادة تجربته. وكذا في "البزازية" من "القضاء" أي لحصول زيادة العلم له بتجربته، ولهذا أبو حنيفة عن القول بأن الصدقة أفضل من حج التطوع، لما حج وعرف مشقته. زاد في "شرح البيري على الأشباه": أن الفتوى على قول أبي يوسف أيضا في الشهادات قلت لكن هي من توابع القضاء. وفي "البحر" من كتاب الدعوى: "لو" سكت المدعى عليه ولم يجب، ينزل منكرا عندهما، أما عند أبي يوسف فيحبس إلى أن يجيب كما قال الإمام السرخسي والفتوى على قول أبي يوسف فيما يتعلق بالقضاء، كما في "القنية" و"البزازية"، فلذا أفتيت بأنه يحبس إلى أن يجيب".
And every branch related to qada', the statement of Abu Yusuf in it is selected. The second [rule]: What is in "al-Bahr" before the chapter on imprisonment, he said: And in "al-Quniya" from the chapter of the mufti: Fatwa is on the statement of Abu Yusuf regarding matters related to qada' due to his increased experience. Similarly in "al-Bazzaziyya" from "al-Qada'" i.e., because of his attainment of increased knowledge through his experience, and for this reason Abu Hanifa [reconsidered] his statement that charity is better than supererogatory Hajj, after he performed Hajj and learned of its difficulty. He added in "Sharh al-Bayri 'ala al-Ashbah": that fatwa is on the statement of Abu Yusuf also in testimonies, I said: but they are from the accessories of qada'. And in "al-Bahr" from the book of claims: If the defendant remains silent and does not answer, he is considered a denier according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad); but according to Abu Yusuf, he is imprisoned until he answers, as Imam al-Sarakhsi said, and fatwa is on the statement of Abu Yusuf regarding matters related to qada', as in "al-Quniya" and "al-Bazzaziyya", so I gave fatwa that he is imprisoned until he answers.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage presents the second rule: in all matters pertaining to qada' (judicial rulings, litigation, court procedures), the qawl of Abu Yusuf is preferred for fatwa. The reason given is his greater practical experience (tajriba) in judicial matters. The text cites multiple sources (al-Bahr, al-Quniya, al-Bazzaziyya) to support this. An illustrative example is given: in a case where the defendant remains silent after a claim, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad consider him a denier, but Abu Yusuf holds that the judge should imprison him until he answers. The fatwa follows Abu Yusuf's view. Additionally, the commentator notes that this preference extends to shahadat (testimonies) as they are accessories to qada'.

Key Terms
القضاء (al-qada'): The domain of judicial rulings, court procedures, and litigation.
تجربة (tajriba): Practical experience, especially in judicial matters.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is Abu Yusuf's qawl preferred in matters of qada'?
A) Because he is the most knowledgeable in hadith.
B) Because of his greater practical experience in judicial matters.
C) Because he was the chief judge.
D) Because his opinions are always the strongest analogically.

Key Takeaway
In judicial matters, fatwa is given on Abu Yusuf's qawl due to his experience, and this extends to accessories like shahadat.

Fatwa on Dhawi al-Arham: Following Muhammad's Qawl
Rule specifying the relied-upon qawl for dhawi al-arham inheritance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the mufta bihi for dhawi al-arham inheritance and explain the tarjih mechanism based on ashhar al-riwayatayn.

Core Idea
In dhawi al-arham inheritance, fatwa follows Muhammad's qawl because it is the more famous narration from Abu Hanifa.

This passage introduces a key rule from Rasm al-Mufti: when two narrations exist from Imam Abu Hanifa on a single issue, the more famous one (ashhar al-riwayatayn) is preferred for fatwa. In the case of dhawi al-arham, Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani's position aligns with that stronger narration. We will examine the textual evidence and understand the hierarchy that ensures consistency in fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Subject
Recognize that this rule concerns inheritance of dhawi al-arham (distant relatives not among primary heirs). The passage specifies that fatwa is given with what Muhammad (al-Shaybani) says.
This is a subset of fara'id; it does not apply to primary heirs (ashab al-fara'id and 'asabat).
2
State the Mufta Bihi
The operative ruling (mufta bihi) is the qawl (opinion) of Imam Muhammad. All later sources affirm this: al-Multaqa, Sakb al-Anhur, al-Kafi.
The text says 'وبقول محمد يفتى' — 'and with the statement of Muhammad fatwa is given.'
3
Trace the Basis: Ashhar al-Riwayatayn
Muhammad's qawl is preferred because it is the more famous of two narrations (riwayat) from Abu Hanifa. The phrase 'وهو أشهر الروايتين عن الإمام أبي حنيفة' appears in the text.
The other riwaya is considered weaker (marjuh) for fatwa purposes, though it remains a valid scholarly opinion.
4
Confirm the Scope
Commentators like the author of Sakb al-Anhur and al-Kafi explicitly state that this applies to 'all inheritance of dhawi al-arham' (في جميع توريث ذوي الأرحام), not just a subset.
The rule is universal within its domain.
5
Apply the Rule in Fatwa
When a mufti encounters a case involving dhawi al-arham, he must use Muhammad's methodology for calculation and distribution. This ensures consistency with the established Hanafi position.
Knowing this rule prevents the mufti from following a weaker riwaya out of ignorance.

بما يقوله محمد

Commentary
This passage presents the third rule: in matters of dhawi al-arham (distant relatives who inherit in the absence of primary heirs), the qawl of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani is preferred for fatwa. The text notes that this is actually the more famous of two narrations from Abu Hanifa himself, so following Muhammad's qawl is effectively following a well-known riwaya from Abu Hanifa. The commentators emphasize that this applies universally to all inheritance calculations involving dhawi al-arham. The sources cited include al-Multaqa, Sakb al-Anhur, and al-Kafi.

Key Terms
ذوو الأرحام (dhawi al-arham): Distant relatives who are not included in the primary inheritors (ashab al-fara'id and 'asabat). They inherit when there are no primary heirs.
أشهر الروايتين (ashhar al-riwayatayn): The more famous of the two transmitted opinions from Abu Hanifa on this issue.

Fatwa on Dhawi al-Arham When No Narration Exists
Rule for mufti when Hanafi narration absent on dhawi al-arham

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rasm al-mufti rule for dhawi al-arham when no Hanafi narration exists, and identify the purification examples where this rule applies.

Core Idea
No Hanafi narration? Adopt the opponent's view.

This lesson presents a key principle in Hanafi fatwa methodology: when no transmitted narration from the founding imams exists for a ruling on distant relatives (dhawi al-arham), the mufti defaults to the opinion of the opposing school. The examples from purification (tahara) illustrate this rule in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal gap
Determine that the matter involves dhawi al-arham and that no Hanafi narration (riwaya) from Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, or Muhammad is recorded.
Check the six major Zahir al-Riwayah works first.
2
Apply the default rule
Adopt the opinion of the opposing school (al-mukhalif) for that specific issue.
This is not free choice; it is a structured default.
3
Recognize the examples
Note that the text gives two tahara examples: used water (maa' musta'mal) and tayammum when only date syrup (nabidh al-tamr) is available. In these cases, if no Hanafi narration is known, the mufti follows the Shafi'i or other school's ruling.
These examples show the rule beyond inheritance.
4
Scope the rule
Understand that this rule applies only when there is absolutely no Hanafi narration on the specific sub-issue. It does not allow disregarding existing Hanafi positions.
The mufti must exhaust available Hanafi sources first.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The fatwa in matters of dhawi al-arham when there is no narration from him is like the saying of the opponent, as in the purity of used water and tayammum only when there is no date syrup (nabidh) other than that.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This is a rasm al-mufti rule: When there is no transmitted narration (riwaya) from the Hanafi imams regarding inheritance of distant relatives (dhawi al-arham), the mufti may adopt the opinion of the opposing school (al-mukhalif). The examples given are from tahara: used water (maa' musta'mal) and tayammum when only date syrup (nabidh al-tamr) is available but no pure water—these are issues where the Hanafi school may follow the Shafi'i or other view in the absence of a clear Hanafi narration.

Key Terms
ذوي الأرحام (dhawi al-arham): Distant relatives who are not Quranic sharers or agnatic heirs; their inheritance is by uterine relation.
رواية (riwaya): A transmitted narration from the founding imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) regarding a ruling.

Key Takeaway
When no Hanafi narration exists for dhawi al-arham, the default is to adopt the opposing school's opinion.

Preferring Abu Yusuf's Opinion in Judiciary
Rule preferring Abu Yusuf in judiciary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that in judiciary matters, the mufta bihi is Abu Yusuf's view, and identify the practical consequence in the silent defendant case.

Core Idea
Abu Yusuf's opinion is preferred in judiciary due to his practical experience.

This passage establishes a key principle in the Hanafi rasm al-mufti: in matters of judiciary (qada) and its adjuncts like testimonies, the relied-upon view is that of Abu Yusuf, not Abu Hanifa or Muhammad. The reason given is his greater practical experience. Understanding this rule helps a mufti know which opinion to adopt when issuing fatwas in court-related matters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
State the explicit rule: 'Fatwa is on the saying of Abu Yusuf regarding matters related to judiciary.'
2
Understand the reason (ta'lil)
Note the cause: 'because of his increased experience' (li-ziyadat tajribatih). This is a causal argument based on practical expertise.
Also supported by Abu Hanifa's retraction on a similar matter after gaining experience.
3
See the application in a silent defendant
Examine the furu': if a defendant remains silent, Abu Yusuf says he is imprisoned until he answers; the Sahibayn consider him a denier without imprisonment.
The fatwa follows Abu Yusuf, so the mufti should rule imprisonment.
4
Recognize the scope
The rule applies to judiciary (qada) and its adjuncts, like testimonies (shahadat). Confirm that the passage extends it to shahadat.
5
Distinguish from other areas
Remember that this preference is specific to judiciary; in other areas, the mufta bihi may be different.

Fatwa in Dhawi al-Arham: The Preference for Muhammad's View
Rule preferring Muhammad's view in dhawi al-arham

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for fatwa in dhawi al-arham inheritance and explain the tarjih mechanism of ashhar al-riwayatayn.

Core Idea
In all dhawi al-arham inheritance, fatwa is given by Muhammad's view — the more famous narration from Abu Hanifa.

This rule from Rasm al-Mufti settles the fatwa position in a key area of inheritance: the distribution among uterine relatives (dhawi al-arham). Although multiple narrations from Abu Hanifa exist, the mufti must follow the more famous one, which is the view of Muhammad al-Shaybani. Understanding this preference is essential for issuing correct fatwa in these cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the rule
Read the passage and identify the exact wording of the rule: 'وبقول محمد يفتى' (With the saying of Muhammad, fatwa is given). Recognize that it applies to all dhawi al-arham inheritance matters.
The sources al-Multaqa, Sakhb al-Anhar, and al-Kafi all affirm this.
2
Locate the basis for the preference
The passage states that Muhammad's view is ashhar al-riwayatayn (the more famous of the two narrations) from Abu Hanifa. Understand that in Hanafi usul, when two conflicting riwayat exist from the same imam, the more famous one is adopted for fatwa.
This is a key principle of tarjih within the madhhab.
3
Apply the rule to a concrete scenario
Consider a case where a deceased leaves only a maternal uncle and a paternal aunt's son as dhawi al-arham. Applying Muhammad's method yields a specific distribution; applying a less famous narration would give a different result. The mufti must use Muhammad's view.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is the calculation of shares.
4
Recognize the authority weight
The rule is based on ashhar al-riwayatayn, which is considered a strong authority. It falls under the category of mufta bihi positions from the classical Hanafi books.
This is not a weak or rare narration; it is the established fatwa.

This is because Muhammad's view is the more famous (ashhar) of two narrations reported from Abu Hanifa on this subject. The sources cited are al-Multaqa, Sakhb al-Anhar (a commentary), and al-Kafi. The rule applies to all aspects of dhawi al-arham inheritance, including the method of distribution (qisma). The author emphasizes that this is the position on which fatwa is given (wa bihi yafti).

Key Terms
ذوي الأرحام (dhawi al-arham): Uterine relatives who are not ashab al-fara'id or 'asabat; they inherit in absence of closer heirs.
أشهر الروايتين (ashhar al-riwayatayn): The more famous of two narrations attributed to the same imam.

Preferring Istihsan over Qiyas with Exceptions
Rule that istihsan generally prevails over qiyas except in specific exceptional cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that istihsan is preferred over qiyas and identify the exceptional cases where qiyas prevails, while explaining the intra-Hanafi dispute on the binding nature of this preference.

Core Idea
Istihsan generally trumps qiyas, but not in a handful of specific exceptions.

This lesson examines a foundational rasm al-mufti rule: when both analogy (qiyas) and juristic preference (istihsan) are present, istihsan is given precedence over qiyas. However, there are exceptions—a finite set of issues where qiyas is preferred. The number of exceptions varies by authority (11 or 22), and there is a nuanced debate about whether this preference is obligatory or merely a priority.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Rule
State the rule as given in the text: 'When there is both qiyas and istihsan in an issue, istihsan is preferred over qiyas.'
This is the default position.
2
Identify the Exceptions
Note that the rule has exceptions: there are specific issues where qiyas is preferred. Recognize that the count differs according to different scholars (Ibn Nujaym mentions 11, al-Nasafi mentions 22).
The exceptions are recorded in Ajnas al-Natifi and other works.
3
Analyze the Nature of the Preference
Understand the two interpretations: al-Talwih holds that the tarjih is binding (obligatory to follow istihsan), while Fakhr al-Islam holds it is merely a priority (awardiyya), permitting qiyas in some cases.
This distinction affects whether a mufti can ever choose qiyas.
4
Determine the Practical Fatwa Application
For issuing fatwa, the mufti must follow the general rule that istihsan prevails, unless the case is one of the documented exceptions. The mufti should be aware of the authoritative list (e.g., the 11 exceptions in Ajnas al-Natifi).
The debate on the nature of tarjih may influence the mufti's discretion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابعة ما في عامة الكتب: من أنه إذا كان في مسألة قياس واستحسان ترجح الاستحسان على القياس إلا في مسائل، وهي إحدى عشرة مسألة على ما في "أجناس الناطفي"، وذكرها العلامة ابن نجيم في شرحه على "المنار"، ثم ذكر أن نجم الدين النسفي أوصلها إلى اثنتين وعشرين. وذكر قبله عن "التلويح": أن الصحيح أن معنى الرجحان هنا تعين العمل بالراجح، وترك العمل بالمرجوح وظاهر كلام فخر الإسلام أنه الأولوية، حتى يجوز العمل بالمرجوح.
Fourth: What is in most books: That when there is in an issue both qiyas and istihsan, istihsan is given preference over qiyas, except in a few issues, which are eleven issues according to what is in Ajnas al-Natifi, and Allama Ibn Nujaym mentioned them in his commentary on al-Manar, then he mentioned that Najm al-Din al-Nasafi raised them to twenty-two. And before him it was mentioned from al-Talwih: that the correct view is that the meaning of preference here is obligation to act by the preponderant and abandonment of acting by the outweighed, while the apparent meaning of Fakhr al-Islam's statement is that it is a preference (priority), such that acting by the outweighed is permissible.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This is a foundational rasm al-mufti rule regarding the method of legal reasoning. In any issue where there is both a qiyas (analogical deduction) and an istihsan (juristic preference), the general rule is that istihsan takes precedence over qiyas. However, there are exceptions: a specific count of issues where qiyas prevails. The number of exceptions varies by source: Ibn Nujaym mentions eleven from Ajnas al-Natifi, while Najm al-Din al-Nasafi expanded it to twenty-two. There is also a theoretical discussion about the nature of this preference: according to al-Talwih, the preponderance (tarjih) means that acting by the rajih (istihsan) is obligatory and acting by the marjuh (qiyas) is not permissible. In contrast, Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi holds that it is merely a priority (awlawiyya), so acting by the marjuh is permissible, though not preferred. The author does not definitively choose between these interpretations but presents both.

Key Terms
قياس (qiyas): Analogical deduction from an original ruling to a new case based on a common effective cause.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; departing from a strict analogy for a stronger evidence or custom.
ترجيح (tarjih): Giving preponderance to one evidence over another; here, preferring istihsan over qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the general rule regarding istihsan and qiyas when both are present in a case?
A) Qiyas always takes precedence
B) Istihsan takes precedence except in some exceptional cases
C) Both are equal; mufti may choose
D) Neither is used; only nass is followed

Key Takeaway
The rule 'istihsan takes precedence over qiyas' is a fundamental rasm al-mufti principle, but it has specific exceptions whose count varies by source, and the binding nature of the preference is debated within the Hanafi school.

The Authority of Zahir al-Riwayah in Fatwa
Rule on the precedence of Zahir al-Riwaya and the condition for using rare narrations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that rulings from Zahir al-Riwayah are primary, and identify when a rare riwaya may be used in fatwa.

Core Idea
Zahir al-Riwayah is the base; rare narrations are rejected unless no base ruling exists.

This passage from Rasm al-Mufti clarifies the hierarchy of riwayat in the Hanafi school. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for a mufti: not every authentic transmission is equally operative. The rule distinguishes between a conflicting riwaya and a gap-filling riwaya.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of riwaya
Recognize that Zahir al-Riwayah (the six core books) is the primary source. Other riwayat (e.g., shadhdh, nawadir) are secondary.
Zahir al-Riwayah includes al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, and al-Ziyadat.
2
Apply the default rule for conflicting riwaya
If a ruling in another riwaya contradicts a ruling in Zahir al-Riwayah, the latter is 'marju'' (rejected) and not to be used in fatwa or judgment.
The passage states: 'ما خرج عن ظاهر الرواية، فهو مرجوع عنه'.
3
Recognize the exception for missing rulings
If an issue is not mentioned in Zahir al-Riwayah but is found in another riwaya, that riwaya must be adopted. The gap-filling rule overrides the general preference.
The passage: 'إذا لم تذكر في ظاهر الرواية وثبتت في رواية أخرى تعين المصير إليها'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخامسة ما في قضاء "البحر": من أن ما خرج عن ظاهر الرواية، فهو مرجوع عنه. والمرجوع عنه لم يبق قولا للمجتهد كما ذكروه. وقدمنا "أنفع المسائل": أن القاضي المقلد لا يجوز له أن يحكم إلا بما هو ظاهر المذهب لا بالرواية الشاذة إلا أن ينصّوا على أن الفتوى عليها. وفي قضاء الفوائت من "البحر": "أن المسألة إذا لم تذكر في ظاهر الرواية وثبتت في رواية أخرى تعين المصير إليها".
Fifth: What is in Qada of al-Bahr: That which goes beyond Zahir al-Riwayah is rejected. And the rejected (marju') is no longer a saying of the mujtahid, as they mentioned. And we have presented in Anfa' al-Masa'il: That a judge who is a muqallid is not allowed to judge except by what is the apparent (zahir) of the madhhab, not by the shadhdh riwayah, unless they stated that the fatwa is upon it. And in Qada al-Fawa'it from al-Bahr: 'That an issue if it is not mentioned in Zahir al-Riwayah and is established in another riwayah, then it is necessary to adopt it.'
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage clarifies the authority of different types of riwaya. The primary source is Zahir al-Riwayah (the six core books of Imam Muhammad). Any ruling that contradicts Zahir al-Riwayah (i.e., is shadhdh or rare) is considered 'marju'' (rejected) and no longer considered a valid opinion of the mujtahid. A muqallid judge cannot base his judgment on such rare narrations unless later scholars explicitly state that fatwa is upon that rare narration. However, there is a nuance: if an issue is not found in Zahir al-Riwayah at all, but exists in another riwaya (even rare), then that other riwaya must be followed. This is because in the absence of a zahir ruling, the only available narration becomes the basis. The passage distinguishes between two situations: (1) a ruling contradicts zahir (rejected), and (2) a ruling is absent from zahir but present elsewhere (must be adopted).

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani: al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat.
رواية شاذة (riwaya shadhdha): A rare or irregular transmission that contradicts the more widely accepted narrations.
مرجوع عنه (marju' 'anhu): Rejected; an opinion that is no longer considered valid for fatwa or judgment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a muqallid judge encounters a ruling that is outside Zahir al-Riwayah but is mentioned in another riwaya, what should he do?
A) Reject it entirely, as it is marju'
B) Adopt it only if no ruling on the issue exists in Zahir al-Riwayah
C) Always adopt it because all riwayat are equal
D) Consult a mujtahid

Key Takeaway
The operative ruling in fatwa is from Zahir al-Riwayah; other riwayat are used only when the issue is absent from it.
